# CRTK Improvement Plan

> **CRTK is NOT, and will not become, an online play / matchmaking / social / anti-cheat / cloud-credit platform, and it will not chase Stockfish-level playing strength.** This is a permanent, load-bearing product boundary. CRTK is a *local-first, deterministic chess toolkit* for study, research, ML datasets, and publishing ŌĆö your games, your data, your datasets, offline. Reference-grade strength always routes through an external UCI engine you control; it is never rented from a cloud and never the product.

This plan was generated by inspecting the `chess-rtk` repository at commit **`1ab42b9`** on branch **`eval-tuning`**. Every factual claim, file path, line number, and behavior cited below was checked against the source at that commit; inferences are explicitly labeled `ASSUMPTION`. Because it is pinned to a specific commit, some details will drift as the codebase evolves ŌĆö treat the grounding as accurate *as of `1ab42b9`*.

---

## Implementation status

Checked and updated on **2026-06-16** from the local `eval-tuning` worktree.
The baseline diagnosis below is intentionally preserved, but these roadmap
items are now ticked off in the implementation:

- [x] **Theme M: roadmap reconciliation.** `TODO.txt` no longer tells agents to
  rebuild finished `Threats.java` work, and `URGENT.md` is resolved for the
  repository-shipped OTIS placeholder weights.
- [x] **Theme F: machine-readable contract foundation.** `crtk help --json`,
  `crtk schema list|show|validate`, `crtk record validate`, `crtk.record.v2`,
  `crtk.record.training-jsonl.v1`, and `crtk.dataset.manifest.v1` exist and are
  covered by `CommandCatalogRegressionTest`, `SchemaAgreementRegressionTest`,
  and `RecordValidateRegressionTest`.
- [x] **Theme I: dataset provenance foundation.** Dataset exporters emit
  `crtk.dataset.manifest.v1` sidecars; `crtk dataset verify|audit|diff`,
  deterministic exporter reruns, `record dedupe`, `record split`, and
  `record audit-split` are covered by focused regressions wired into the CLI
  suite.
- [x] **Theme A foundation: local PGN store.** `chess.pgn.PgnStore` and
  `crtk pgn import|show|find|stats|delete|compact` are implemented with
  append-safe JSONL, side indexes, FEN-verified signature lookup, and focused
  PGN-store regressions.
- [x] **Theme A import hardening:** PGN SetUp/FEN precedence, Variant-tagged
  Chess960 X-FEN normalization, and multi-source parser/store fixtures are
  covered by focused regressions.
- [x] **Theme A scale validation:** `PgnStoreScaleRegressionTest` imports a
  deterministic 2,048-game corpus through the real file path, checks sidecar
  counts, reopens the store, verifies representative FEN lookups, and confirms
  duplicate import stays idempotent.
- [x] **Theme C classifier foundation:** `chess.review.Classifier` and
  `ReviewClassifierRegressionTest` pin engine-free mistake categories, WDL
  gating, severity, and false-positive guards for only-move, already-decided,
  dead-draw, theory, and blitz noise-floor cases.
- [x] **Theme C row-contract foundation:** `chess.review.ReviewRow`,
  `crtk.review.ply.v1`, and `ReviewRowSchemaRegressionTest` pin the
  schemaVersion-stamped JSONL row, reproducibility block, tag delta shape, and
  byte-stable golden fixture before engine or CLI orchestration.
- [x] **Theme C offline review command:** `crtk review game --offline` now
  reviews PGN mainlines through the shared `GameReviewer`, writes
  `crtk.review.ply.v1` JSONL, and pins the path with
  `ReviewCommandRegressionTest`.
- [x] **Theme C external-UCI review command:** `crtk review game` now runs a
  bounded external UCI backend over the same `GameReviewer`/`ReviewRow`
  contract, pins `go nodes` behavior with a fake-UCI regression, and records
  protocol, nodes, duration, MultiPV, thread, hash, WDL, and deterministic
  metadata in each row.
- [x] **Theme C study-unit emission:** `crtk review game --to-study` now
  stamps drillable mistake rows with stable study-unit ids, writes
  `crtk.review.study_unit.v1` JSONL, and writes existing `Record` JSON whose
  `parent` is the pre-move FEN and whose `position` is the post-best-move FEN,
  pinned by the fake-UCI `ReviewCommandRegressionTest` fixture.
- [x] **Theme C artifact contract and Workbench command hook:** `wiki/review-to-study.md`
  documents the review JSONL, study-unit JSONL, and Record sidecar contract;
  the Workbench command builder now has a `Review game` template that emits the
  real `crtk review game --to-study` CLI path with explicit engine budgets.
- [x] **Theme C Review artifact consumer:** the Workbench Review panel can load
  produced `.review.jsonl` plus optional `.study.jsonl` rows through a dedicated
  artifact loader and render them without recomputing verdicts.
- [x] **Theme C Workbench Review producer:** the Review surface now has a
  CLI-backed `Build Study` path that materializes the loaded game as PGN, runs
  `crtk review game --to-study`, and loads the produced artifacts back through
  the artifact consumer.
- [x] **Theme G grounding verifier foundation:** `PositionDescriptionVerifier`
  now rejects non-candidate SAN, wrong side-to-move, contradictory eval direction,
  and narrow material falsehoods before future model prose can replace classical
  text.
- [x] **Theme G deterministic why/plan slice:** `StrategicPlanNarrator` turns
  already-extracted passed-pawn, center-state, king-safety, space, and pawn-weakness
  tags into bounded classical plan sentences without naming unverified moves.
- [x] **Theme G T5 surface cleanup:** `position describe` is now classical-only;
  the working T5 runtime is documented as `fen text` / `puzzle text`, and legacy
  `--engine t5` points users to that path instead of a dead stub.
- [x] **Theme E localhost daemon foundation:** `crtk serve` now binds loopback,
  exposes `/rpc`, `/catalog`, and `/health`, serializes CLI dispatch through
  `application.Main`, and is pinned by `ServeRegressionTest`.
- [x] **Theme E generated Python SDK stub:** `scripts/generate_python_sdk.py`
  emits `sdk/python/crtk_client.py` from `crtk help --json`, with deterministic
  regeneration and daemon smoke coverage in `PythonSdkRegressionTest`.
- [x] **Theme H Workbench doc reconciliation:** `wiki/workbench.md` and the
  Workbench design guide now document the shipped 8-view shell, and
  `WorkbenchStructureRegressionTest` checks the wiki table against
  `WindowLifecycle` registered views.
- [x] **Theme H PGN/Review command palette surfacing:** the Workbench Run
  surface has curated templates for `pgn import`, `pgn find`, `pgn show`,
  `pgn stats`, and `review game`; palette jump actions and the All CLI template
  are covered by `WorkbenchCommandRegression`.
- [x] **Theme H file-size slice:** `Theme.java`, `WindowLifecycle.java`,
  `BoardPanel.java`, `WindowBoardLayer.java`, `TreePanel.java`,
  `DrawPanel.java`, `PublishingPanel.java`, `EngineGauntletPanel.java`, and
  `MctsSearch.java` now delegate cohesive
  palette/font/component/menu, palette-search, board-painting, board-animation,
  board-layout, board setup editing, Run/Console/Logs construction, tree target
  tracking, tree inspector widgets, and tree growth scrubbing, Draw
  annotation-list rendering and color parsing/formatting, publishing preview
  planning, gauntlet result rendering, and MCTS snapshot formatting plus leaf
  scoring, restoring raw-line headroom on those facades; Workbench package
  coverage now includes `draw`, `engine`, `play`, and `relations`.
- [x] **Theme H Theme facade guard-band:** `Theme.java` is now below the
  2000-raw-line guard band and delegates cohesive implementation details to
  package-private helpers: `ThemePalette`, `ThemeFonts`, `ThemeComponents`,
  `ThemeInstaller`, `ThemeRefresh`, `ThemeColors`, `ThemeBorders`,
  `ThemeForeground`, and `ThemeState`. The public `Theme.*` facade remains the
  caller contract. Focused verification after this slice: `javac --release 17`,
  `java -Djava.awt.headless=true -cp out testing.WorkbenchRegressionTest`, and
  `git diff --check`.

## What is still missing

Use this queue as the live "what to do next" list. The historical diagnosis and
deep-dive sections below remain useful context, but this block is the current
working order from the local tree.

### P0 - stabilize the current refactor/worktree

- [x] **Run the full recommended gate before any checkpoint commit.**
  `./scripts/run_regression_suite.sh recommended` passed on 2026-06-16 after
  the Theme facade split, including build/lint, core, CLI, engine, UCI, book,
  perft-smoke, and jar smoke phases. `shellcheck` was skipped because it is not
  installed on this machine. It passed again on 2026-06-17 after the
  `position describe --audience` slice and regression-runner default hardening;
  the runner now keeps whole-suite phases and Java test classes serial by
  default, with `CRTK_SUITE_JOBS`/`CRTK_TEST_JOBS` left as explicit opt-ins.
  Follow-up hardening added a shared build lock for the regression runner and
  Linux runtime/release packagers so separate app-server invocations wait
  instead of clobbering the shared `out/` tree mid-test.
- [ ] **Consolidate the broad dirty worktree into coherent commits only after
  full validation.** Keep commits grouped by contract: CLI/schema/data work,
  Workbench UI refactors, docs/generated docs, and native/model notes should not
  be mixed unless the dependency is real. Candidate grouping is prepared, but
  no commit has been made because commit/push still needs explicit maintainer
  approval:
  1. CLI catalog, schemas, record validation, dataset provenance, and generated
     SDK/server contract.
  2. Local PGN store and PGN command/test surface.
  3. Review pipeline, review-to-study artifacts, and Workbench review artifact
     consumer/producer.
  4. Grounded description verifier, deterministic why/plan narration, and T5
     surface cleanup.
  5. Workbench UI/package refactors, including Theme facade helpers, board,
     draw, engine, MCTS, publish, window, and command-surface splits.
  6. Documentation/roadmap/generated docs, including this improvement plan,
     wiki updates, and generated `docs/` pages.
  7. Packaging/model/native maintenance notes and scripts.
- [x] **Refresh Java diagnostics after the Theme split.**
  `scripts/inspect_java_diagnostics.sh` was refreshed into
  `reports/java-diagnostics-triage.md` on 2026-06-16. `javac -Xlint:all`
  reported no warnings, no active JDT marker messages were found, SonarLint
  local issue counts were zero, and SonarQube for IDE logs had no
  review-needed messages.

### P1 - highest-value product gaps still open

- [ ] **Workbench manual layout-control pass.** The shell has strong regression
  coverage, but still needs a real narrow/normal/wide manual pass for split,
  dock, detach, collapse, restore, close, hover, focus, disabled, and tooltip
  behavior.
  - [x] First automated guard added: editor tab context-menu split/close/layout
    actions now expose stable command ids, disabled split actions explain the
    recovery path, and `WorkbenchUiEditorRegression` pins those contracts.
  - [x] Second automated guard added: `WorkbenchUiEditorRegression` now sizes a
    four-group editor layout at compact, normal, and wide widths and asserts
    split/restore controls keep stable command ids, tooltips, accessible names,
    positive bounds, and horizontal reachability.
  - [x] Third automated guard and fix added: split-group focus feedback now
    refreshes when selecting an already-visible pane, and the regression
    interleaves compact/normal/wide layouts with pane focus changes,
    keyboard-style tab cycling, close, restore, and collapse.
  - [ ] Remaining manual pass: verify narrow, normal, and wide Workbench
    windows for open, split, dock, detach, collapse, restore, close, keyboard
    focus, hover/focus feedback, disabled affordances, and tooltip clarity.
- [ ] **MCTS graph and live-search visualization.** The table workflow is still
  the stable baseline; the missing product slice is the zoomable graph canvas,
  table/graph synchronization, and visible incremental Follow-leaf/NN frames
  during live search.
  - [x] Live-frame regression guard added: `WorkbenchBackendRegression` now
    drives the Network tab's follow-leaf PUCT worker headlessly and asserts more
    than two distinct intermediate visualization states during a bounded search.
- [ ] **NN runtime diagnostics and board consistency.** Finish the reusable
  collapsible board wrapper, consistent NN view states, and richer Dashboard
  runtime diagnostics for Java2D/OpenGL, model availability, native/GPU
  backends, cache status, and model paths.
  - [x] Dashboard runtime diagnostics now reuse the compact
    `NetworkDiagnosticsPanel(false)` for model, Java2D/native backend, cache,
    and configured model-path status; `WorkbenchBackendRegression` pins the
    shared compact widget.
  - [x] First shared board-section helper added: CNN and BT4 atlas board tiles
    now route through `NetworkBoardSection`, with a headless regression pinning
    small-board caption suppression, oriented hit regions, and per-square
    tooltip values.
  - [x] OTIS sheaf-focus and sheaf-Laplacian boards now use
    `NetworkBoardSection` with preserved whole-board inspector bindings and
    shared per-square tooltip/orientation behavior.
  - [x] BT4 token-energy board now also uses `NetworkBoardSection`, leaving
    the specialized triangle-attention board and raw tensor tiles for later
    focused passes.
  - [x] CNN policy-attention and detailed-position boards now use
    `NetworkBoardSection`; `CnnView` no longer owns a duplicate square-tooltip
    helper, while raw input-plane tiles remain specialized inspector tiles.
  - [x] NNUE overview and trace current-position boards now use
    `NetworkBoardSection` through its custom overlay hook, preserving
    feature-square highlights and the existing board-click hit regions.
  - [x] NNUE atlas slot-detail weight board now uses `NetworkBoardSection`
    underlay/overlay hooks, preserving the dense weight plane under pieces, the
    selected-square ring, and inspectable slot metadata.
  - [x] Classical evaluator position board now uses `NetworkBoardSection` too,
    so the network/evaluator package has one shared shell for generic
    current-position boards; remaining direct board drawing is specialized raw
    tensor or triangle-attention rendering.
  - [x] BT4 detailed selected-head triangle-attention board now routes its
    generic board shell through `NetworkBoardSection` while preserving
    selected-square click behavior, the incoming/outgoing triangle overlay,
    and per-square hover metadata.
- [ ] **Grounded explanation hardening.** Do not add a duplicate `crtk explain`
  noun yet; deepen the existing `position describe`, `fen text`, and Workbench
  explanation surfaces with machine-readable grounding, stricter verifier
  contracts, audience/facts modes, and model-verified fallback.
  - [x] `position describe` JSON, JSONL, and training-JSONL rows now expose the
    verifier verdict as `grounding.grounded` plus structured violations, making
    the existing command consumable without prose parsing.
  - [x] `position describe --facts-only` now emits JSON/JSONL rows with the
    structured facts object, schema marker, and grounding verdict while
    suppressing prose/prompt/target fields; help, catalog examples, and the
    Workbench command template expose the same flag.
  - [x] The grounding verifier now rejects explicit named-opening claims that
    lack a matching opening-name fact and unproved "only move" claims when the
    structured legal-move count is not exactly one; focused verifier regressions
    also pin the backed-by-facts allowed cases.
  - [x] Material-surplus verification now covers side-specific queen, rook,
    bishop, knight, pawn, and generic minor-piece claims such as "White is a
    rook up" or "Black has an extra knight"; verifier regressions pin both
    unsupported and backed-by-count cases.
  - [x] `position describe --audience` now provides stable beginner, club,
    advanced, coach, researcher, ML, and engine-debug presets over the existing
    detail/facts modes; ML/research presets default to structured facts output,
    explicit `--detail` still overrides the prose level, and help/catalog/
    Workbench templates expose the same selector.
- [ ] **Repertoire and spaced repetition.** `crtk repertoire import|review|grade`
  is still the largest missing study-loop feature after PGN/review foundations:
  versioned cards, deterministic due dates, overload caps, and Workbench command
  parity are not done.

### P2 - correctness and distribution hardening

- [ ] **Dataset provenance refinements.** The manifest foundation exists and
  exporter-level `--row-hashes` sidecars now cover tensor/text dataset exports;
  future `--keep highest-depth` dedupe policy and a nested `label_policy`
  schema bump remain intentionally deferred.
- [ ] **OTIS CUDA parity and benchmark trail.** Keep CPU/GPU parity tests,
  fallback reporting, and measured kernel optimization as the bar before any
  backend performance claims.
- [ ] **Packaging/onboarding polish.** Finish the thin `crtk setup` path,
  version agreement checks, and bundled runtime story so a fresh user gets a
  runnable toolkit without relying on stale `crtk.jar` assumptions.
  - [x] Version agreement guard added: `CLICommandRegressionTest` now asserts
    `VersionCommand.VERSION`, `crtk version`, `crtk version --json`, and
    `package.json` agree, and `wiki/releasing.md` documents that guard.
  - [x] JSON diagnostics added: `crtk doctor --json` emits
    `crtk.doctor.v1` with warning/error arrays and native backend rows,
    `crtk config show --json` emits `crtk.config.v1`, and the CLI regression
    phase verifies exit-code parity with text mode.
  - [x] Linux self-contained runtime groundwork added:
    `scripts/make_runtime_linux.sh` builds the jar with `javac --release 17`,
    creates a jlink/jpackage app image, and smoke-tests `crtk version` from the
    produced bundle with an empty `PATH`.
- [ ] **Docs regeneration after final stabilization.** Once the worktree is
  coherent, run the docs phase and ensure generated `docs/` reflects the updated
  wiki and command catalog.

## 1. Executive diagnosis

### What CRTK is today (grounded)

CRTK (`crtk`) is a **deterministic, zero-third-party-dependency Java 17 chess toolkit** built around one invariant that almost nothing else in the chess-software world holds to: *there is exactly one shared chess core, and every surface asks it the same questions* ([wiki/architecture.md](wiki/architecture.md), [README.md](README.md):27-31). That core ŌĆö [Position.java](src/chess/core/Position.java), [MoveGenerator.java](src/chess/core/MoveGenerator.java), [Fen.java](src/chess/core/Fen.java), [SAN.java](src/chess/core/SAN.java) ŌĆö is genuinely strong: strict FEN validation that rejects 5-field input and validates king counts / castling-rook presence / en-passant consistency ([Fen.java](src/chess/core/Fen.java):65-67), full Chess960 with all 960 Scharnagl start positions, legal movegen gated behind a `perft-suite` regression with 19 embedded truth tables ([PerftSuite.java](src/chess/debug/PerftSuite.java)), and SAN/PGN round-tripping.

On top of that core sits a wide, coherent surface:

- **A noun-then-verb CLI** with 15 areas + 2 shortcut leaves, built declaratively in [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java):125-184. Dispatch is process-per-invocation through [Main.java](src/application/Main.java).
- **External UCI engine orchestration** ([Engine.java](src/chess/uci/Engine.java)) driven entirely by per-engine TOML protocol files ([Protocol.java](src/chess/uci/Protocol.java)) ŌĆö a new engine is config, not code.
- **An in-house engine** (alpha-beta + PUCT MCTS, [AlphaBeta.java](src/chess/engine/AlphaBeta.java), [Mcts.java](src/chess/engine/Mcts.java)) with a bounded forced-mate prover ([MateProver.java](src/chess/engine/MateProver.java)) and self-play SPRT gauntlet ŌĆö deterministic, explicitly *not* trying to out-play Stockfish.
- **A deterministic tag engine** ([Generator.java](src/chess/tag/Generator.java), 2115 lines) with 22 named checkmate patterns, SEE-backed tactics, grounded THREAT/IDEA families, and four shipped game-analysis layers (MoveEffect/Line/Variation/Game).
- **Grounded explanations** via `position describe` ([ClassicalPositionDescriptionGenerator.java](src/chess/describe/ClassicalPositionDescriptionGenerator.java)) ŌĆö faithful-by-construction, cannot hallucinate ŌĆö plus a working in-process T5 summarizer ([Runner.java](src/chess/nn/t5/Runner.java)).
- **Dataset/ML export** (npy/lc0/classifier tensors, training/puzzle JSONL) with train==serve encoding.
- **A native, dependency-free PDF publishing pipeline** ([Document.java](src/chess/pdf/document/Document.java)) ŌĆö no LaTeX, no PDFBox.
- **A registry-driven Swing Workbench** that mirrors the CLI and runs commands by spawning the real CLI in a child JVM ([CommandRunner.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java):505-511), enforced by [WorkbenchCommandRegression.java](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java).
- **An in-house, framework-free test harness** (no JUnit; 53 `main()` test classes) driven by one shared script that gates both laptop and CI ([run_regression_suite.sh](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh)).

This is a *remarkably complete* single-maintainer codebase. It is also, today, **a toolkit in search of the product its own README implies.**

### The single strongest advantage

**Determinism enforced by a single shared core, with zero third-party Java dependencies, verified by a perft-and-regression gate.** This is not marketing ŌĆö it is structurally true and structurally rare. ChessBase is closed and Windows-bound; Lichess/Chess.com are cloud services; `python-chess` is a library with no engine/dataset/publishing stack; SCID is C++/Tcl legacy. Nothing in the field offers *one rules core that legality, notation, tags, diagrams, engine jobs, datasets, and books all share* such that "the same input produces the same output every time" ([AGENTS.md](AGENTS.md)). For research and ML ŌĆö where reproducibility *is* the deliverable ŌĆö this is a moat competitors cannot cheaply copy because it is an architectural commitment, not a feature.

### The single biggest weakness

**CRTK cannot store, index, or review a user's own games.** There is no local PGN database, no game id, no provenance, no `crtk pgn` area ŌĆö only stateless `fen pgn` / `record export pgn` conversions. The Workbench has [PgnExplorerModel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java), [PgnPrepReport.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnPrepReport.java), and [GameReviewPanel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/GameReviewPanel.java) ŌĆö but all are **in-memory, per-session, and have no CLI peer**. The roadmap ([TODO.txt](TODO.txt)) mentions none of this. A "study toolkit" that forgets your games the moment you close it is not a study toolkit; it is a calculator. This is the foundation on which review, repertoire, and the whole study loop must stand, and it is simply absent.

### What it should become

**The best *local-first, reproducible* chess workbench for people who treat chess as data** ŌĆö students who want grounded explanations they can trust, researchers and ML practitioners who need byte-stable datasets with real provenance, and authors who publish from source. The unifying promise: *your games and positions become a queryable, taggable, explainable, exportable local corpus that produces identical results forever, with no cloud and no dependencies.*

### What it must NOT become

- **An online play / matchmaking / social / anti-cheat / cloud platform.** This is a hard product boundary. Every networked temptation (B platform-sync, N OTB/broadcast) must be either rejected or scoped to *read-only, on-demand, local-file* ingestion.
- **A Stockfish competitor.** The in-house engine exists for determinism, not strength ([wiki/in-house-engine.md](wiki/in-house-engine.md):5). Reference-grade analysis routes through external UCI engines. Pouring effort into engine Elo is mission drift.
- **A plugin host.** [TODO.txt](TODO.txt):632 already declares this a non-goal, and it directly fights determinism + the no-deps build. The TOML protocol seam is sufficient extensibility.
- **A GUI-first product.** The CLI is source of truth ([wiki/cli-command-guide.md](wiki/cli-command-guide.md)). The Workbench is the most-funded theme in the TODO, but continuing to pour P0 effort into UI polish while the PGN store, review router, and machine-readable schemas are absent is the wrong altitude.

### The clearest market opening

**Reproducible, grounded chess data tooling that runs entirely offline.** Lichess and Chess.com own online play and casual study but are cloud-locked and opaque. ChessBase owns the serious-database market but is proprietary, Windows-only, expensive, and not scriptable/ML-friendly. `python-chess` owns programmatic access but ships no engine management, no tag taxonomy, no publishing, no determinism guarantee. **No one owns "I want a local, scriptable, byte-reproducible chess corpus with grounded explanations and a clean ML export path, with no account and no dependencies."** CRTK is two missing pieces ŌĆö a local PGN store and a machine-readable contract ŌĆö away from owning exactly that.

### Blunt bottom line

CRTK has built an extraordinary *engine room* and almost no *product deck*. The codebase is more mature than the roadmap, which is itself stale to the point of being dangerous: [TODO.txt](TODO.txt):308 instructs contributors to rebuild [Threats.java](src/chess/tag/Threats.java) "from this spec" because it is "an 11-byte stub" ŌĆö but the file is a real 10,600-byte implementation already wired into the tag pipeline. The work that matters next is not more research polish; it is connecting the engine room to a user's actual games and publishing a contract the rest of the ecosystem can build on.

---

## 2. End-goal product vision

### Target users

| User | What they want from CRTK | Why they can't get it elsewhere today |
|---|---|---|
| **The serious learner** | Import their own games, get grounded (non-hallucinated) explanations of mistakes, turn blunders into puzzles, drill openings | Chessable/Lichess give cloud study but no local corpus, no transparency; explanations are either absent or LLM-confabulated |
| **The researcher / ML practitioner** | Byte-reproducible datasets with provenance (version, git, input/weights checksums), stable schemas, train==serve encoding | `python-chess` has no dataset stack; Lichess dumps have no per-row provenance; nothing guarantees byte-determinism |
| **The author / publisher** | Publish puzzle books and studies from a source-controlled manifest, diffable in VCS, no LaTeX | ChessBase exports are binary; everyone else needs a LaTeX/InDesign pipeline |
| **The automation / agent builder** | A self-describing CLI with stable JSON contracts and bounded work | CRTK is *almost* there ([wiki/ai-agents.md](wiki/ai-agents.md)) but has no `crtk help --json` catalog to build against |
| **The programmer-hobbyist** | A clean, dependency-free Java codebase to read, extend, and learn chess programming from | The README's own epigraph; this audience is already served and should stay served |

### Core workflows (the end-state loop)

1. **Ingest** ŌĆö `crtk pgn import games.pgn` ŌåÆ a local, indexed, queryable store keyed on game-id + position signature. *(Absent today ŌĆö the keystone.)*
2. **Review** ŌĆö `crtk game review <id>` ŌåÆ detect blunders/turning-points using the shipped game-analysis layers + external-engine grading, emit study units. *(Primitives exist; router absent.)*
3. **Explain** ŌĆö grounded "why," not just "what": the loss was *because* of a backward pawn / weak back rank, surfaced from tags that already exist but are never turned into sentences.
4. **Drill** ŌĆö turn the refutation into a puzzle Record (the miner already does FENŌåÆpuzzle); schedule it via repertoire/SRS. *(Drill scheduling absent.)*
5. **Export / Publish** ŌĆö datasets with provenance, or a puzzle book from the same corpus, all byte-reproducible.

The differentiator running through all five: **one core, one corpus, identical results, fully offline.**

### Differentiation vs the field

- **vs Chess.com / Lichess:** local-first and offline; you own the data; byte-reproducible; grounded explanations instead of opaque coaching; ML export instead of a closed garden. CRTK does *not* compete on play, social, or ratings ŌĆö and must not try.
- **vs ChessBase:** open (GPL-3.0), scriptable, cross-platform-capable (Java), ML-native, free; sacrifices ChessBase's vast curated database and Windows-native polish. CRTK wins on reproducibility and automation, not on catalog size.
- **vs Chessable:** Chessable owns spaced-repetition courseware with a content marketplace; CRTK's SRS would be *your-own-games-first* and offline, not a content store. Different axis.
- **vs ChessTempo:** tactics-server vs local puzzle mining + rating you can audit ([Scorer.java](src/chess/puzzle/Scorer.java) is deterministic, signature-keyed, no RNG). CRTK's ratings are corpus-internal and *honest about it* ŌĆö a feature, not a bug.
- **vs SCID / SCID vs PC:** SCID is the closest open analog (local database + analysis) but is aging C++/Tcl, not ML-aware, not reproducibility-focused, and has no grounded-explanation or dataset story. CRTK should aim to be "SCID for the ML era."
- **vs Arena:** Arena is a UCI GUI; CRTK orchestrates UCI engines as a sub-feature with TOML protocols and JSONL batch output, not as the whole product.
- **vs python-chess:** the honest comparison. python-chess is the dominant programmatic library. CRTK is a *toolkit* (engine mgmt + tags + datasets + publishing + Workbench), not a library ŌĆö but it must publish a machine-readable contract (and arguably ship/document a way to call the engines) or python-chess remains the default for programmers.
- **vs Chessvision.ai / DGT:** OCR and OTB hardware are explicitly out of scope (reject). The in-boundary answer is "export a PGN and import it."

### What "success" looks like

- A researcher cites "datasets generated with crtk X.Y.Z (commit abc, inputs sha256 ŌĆ”)" in a paper and a reviewer reproduces them byte-for-byte.
- A learner runs `crtk pgn import my-lichess-export.pgn && crtk game review` offline and gets trustworthy mistake explanations with no account.
- An author ships a puzzle book whose manifest lives in git and renders identically on any machine.
- An agent/IDE drives CRTK entirely off `crtk help --json` without scraping prose.

### What CRTK should be famous for

**"The chess toolkit where the same input always produces the same output ŌĆö your games, your data, your datasets, offline, forever."** Determinism + grounding + local-first, fused.

---

## 3. Strategic principles

1. **One core, no forks ŌĆö ever.** *Any feature that re-implements legality, notation, or position state outside [Position.java](src/chess/core/Position.java) is rejected at review, no exceptions; the shared core is the entire value proposition.*
2. **The CLI is the contract; the GUI is a mirror.** *New capability lands as a CLI verb first ([WorkbenchCommandRegression.java](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java) already enforces the mirror), so no Workbench-only feature (PgnExplorer, GameReview) is allowed to be the only home of logic.*
3. **Determinism is a tested contract, not a slogan.** *Wire the unwired ML/NNUE tests into CI and add byte-equality assertions where wiki/datasets.md claims byte-stability ŌĆö currently nothing verifies the re-run-identical promise, and [Result.equals()](src/chess/engine/Result.java):106 even includes `elapsedMillis`.*
4. **Provenance or it didn't happen.** *Every dataset export stamps crtk version + git commit + input/weights checksums; today `record dataset npy` writes no meta at all and no exporter records version/commit, so "reproducible datasets" is currently unprovable.*
5. **Grounded beats fluent.** *No explanation states a fact absent from the structured input; the dead T5 stub ([T5PositionDescriptionGenerator.java](src/chess/describe/T5PositionDescriptionGenerator.java)) stays dead until a verification pass exists, because a hallucinating explainer destroys the trust moat.*
6. **The boundary is load-bearing.** *Online play, matchmaking, social, anti-cheat, cloud credits, and live broadcast are permanently out; networked import is allowed only as read-only on-demand ingestion of user-supplied files/public exports.*
7. **Schema before SDK before server.** *Serialize [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) to `crtk help --json` and publish JSON Schemas before building any daemon/SDK/editor tooling, or those consumers hard-code contracts that drift.*
8. **Bounded work is a user-facing feature.** *Every long-running command keeps explicit budgets (`--max-nodes`, `--max-duration`, `--max-total`); an unbounded operation is a bug because agents and CI depend on termination guarantees.*
9. **Fail loud on bad data.** *[Record.fromJson](src/chess/struct/Record.java) and [Reader.java](src/chess/io/Reader.java) silently drop malformed input today; reproducible corpora require a strict mode that errors per-line instead of quietly shrinking the dataset.*
10. **Reference-grade routes outward.** *Strength-critical analysis goes through external UCI engines via [Protocol.java](src/chess/uci/Protocol.java) TOML; the in-house engine optimizes for determinism, and chasing its Elo is mission drift.*
11. **No third-party Java deps, plain `javac --release 17`.** *This constraint is why the build is hermetic and the test gate is the build gate; any feature that "needs a library" must be re-scoped, not granted an exception (this is the real reason OCR/CV is rejected).*
12. **The roadmap must match HEAD.** *Reconcile [TODO.txt](TODO.txt) against source now ŌĆö it tells contributors to rebuild a finished [Threats.java](src/chess/tag/Threats.java) and to "add" an already-built OTIS CUDA backend ([libotis_cuda.so](native/cuda/build/libotis_cuda.so) exists), so a plan built on it would waste weeks.*
13. **Internal research polish is rate-limited.** *Workbench MCTS graphs, NN view consistency, and OTIS kernel speed are capped to a background stream; none of them moves the toolkit toward storing/reviewing a user's games, which is the actual mission.*
14. **Honesty about model fidelity is permanent.** *Keep stating that LC0 CNN/BT4/OTIS are usable-not-bit-exact and that OTIS ships only a random placeholder; the trust that grounding buys is destroyed the moment a caveat is quietly dropped.*
15. **Onboarding correctness is non-negotiable.** *Fix the live first-run lie now: [getting-started.md](wiki/getting-started.md):48 promises "a prebuilt `crtk.jar` ships in the repository root," but `crtk.jar` is gitignored ([.gitignore](.gitignore):31), so a fresh clone's documented `java -jar crtk.jar` fails.*

---

## 4. Current-state map

Maturity: **strong** = production-grade, tested, mission-aligned ┬Ę **ok** = works, has notable gaps ┬Ę **weak** = exists but thin/risky ┬Ę **absent** = not present.

| Area | Maturity | Key files | One-line gap |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Core rules / data structs** | **strong** | [Position.java](src/chess/core/Position.java), [Fen.java](src/chess/core/Fen.java), [MoveGenerator.java](src/chess/core/MoveGenerator.java), [SAN.java](src/chess/core/SAN.java) | No threefold/fifty-move draw-by-rule API and `signatureCore()` is FNV-1a, not collision-resistant Zobrist ŌĆö limits large-scale dedup/repetition. |
| **CLI surface & dispatch** | **strong** | [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java), [Main.java](src/application/Main.java), [Constants.java](src/application/cli/Constants.java) | No machine-readable catalog (`crtk help --json`/`schema`) despite the registry holding all metadata in memory; exit-code 2 is overloaded across 84/88 failure sites. |
| **External UCI orchestration** | **ok** | [Engine.java](src/chess/uci/Engine.java), [Protocol.java](src/chess/uci/Protocol.java), [EngineBatchCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/EngineBatchCommand.java) | `analyse()` hard-codes `go nodes` so TOML `searchDepth`/`searchTime` are inert; no PGN/game-level analysis; provenance lacks engine version/budget/run-id. |
| **Built-in engine / search** | **strong** (for its goal) | [AlphaBeta.java](src/chess/engine/AlphaBeta.java), [Mcts.java](src/chess/engine/Mcts.java), [MateProver.java](src/chess/engine/MateProver.java), [Gauntlet.java](src/chess/engine/Gauntlet.java) | [Result.equals()](src/chess/engine/Result.java) includes `elapsedMillis` (golden-test foot-gun); no JSON serializer for in-house search; MCTS non-deterministic under `--threads`. |
| **Tag engine** | **strong** | [Generator.java](src/chess/tag/Generator.java), [Checkmate.java](src/chess/tag/Checkmate.java), [Threats.java](src/chess/tag/Threats.java), [game/GameAnalyzer.java](src/chess/tag/game/GameAnalyzer.java) | Dynamic families (MOVE_EFFECT/LINE/VARIATION/GAME) are unregistered in [Sort.java](src/chess/tag/Sort.java)/[Literals.java](src/chess/tag/core/Literals.java) and undocumented in [SCHEMA.md](tag/SCHEMA.md), bypassing the canonical sort/dedupe/Filter pipeline. |
| **Explanations / describe** | **ok** | [ClassicalPositionDescriptionGenerator.java](src/chess/describe/ClassicalPositionDescriptionGenerator.java), [Runner.java](src/chess/nn/t5/Runner.java), [PositionRelationsCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/PositionRelationsCommand.java) | States verdicts but never causation ("why/plan"); collected strategic tags are unused in prose; the describe-package T5 is a permanent stub and the documented grounding/verification pass is unimplemented. |
| **Records & dataset export** | **ok** | [Record.java](src/chess/struct/Record.java), [RecordDatasetExporter.java](src/chess/io/RecordDatasetExporter.java), [ClassifierDatasetExporter.java](src/chess/io/ClassifierDatasetExporter.java), [RecordLc0Exporter.java](src/chess/io/RecordLc0Exporter.java) | No schema-version field; `npy` writes no meta.json; no exporter records version/commit/checksums; no train/val/test split or dedupe; tolerant parsing silently drops bad rows. |
| **Puzzle mining & rating** | **ok** | [MineCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/MineCommand.java), [Scorer.java](src/chess/puzzle/Scorer.java), [PuzzleEloExporter.java](src/chess/io/PuzzleEloExporter.java) | No blunderŌåÆpuzzle router (mistakes aren't auto-converted); rating is hand-tuned, uncalibrated to humans, with no in-repo validation set; volatility/distribution tooling stranded in `testing/` mains. |
| **Publishing / rendering** | **strong** (Linux) | [Document.java](src/chess/pdf/document/Document.java), [Svg.java](src/chess/pdf/document/Svg.java), [book/render/Writer.java](src/chess/book/render/Writer.java), [Font.java](src/chess/pdf/document/Font.java) | "Byte-stable" untested (regressions assert size thresholds, not equality) and broken by design: line metrics + glyphs come from AWT and a hardcoded `/usr/share/texmf` Latin Modern path, so output differs across machines; non-ASCII ŌåÆ `?`. |
| **Swing Workbench** | **strong** (productized) | [WindowLifecycle.java](src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowLifecycle.java), [CommandRunner.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java), [RunManifest.java](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java), [PgnExplorerModel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java) | PGN explorer / review / prep are in-memory and GUI-only with no CLI peer (violates CLI-is-source-of-truth); 9 files exceed 2000 raw lines; [wiki/workbench.md](wiki/workbench.md) stale (12 tabs vs shipped 8). |
| **Tests & CI** | **strong** (narrow) | [run_regression_suite.sh](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh), [TestSupport.java](src/testing/TestSupport.java), [.github/workflows/ci.yml](.github/workflows/ci.yml) | 6 ML/NNUE tests compile but are unwired from CI (rot silently); no coverage metric; single-OS/single-JDK; no byte-reproducibility test; golden values hardcoded in source. |
| **Packaging / install** | **ok** (Linux-only) | [install.sh](install.sh), [make_release_linux_cuda.sh](scripts/make_release_linux_cuda.sh), [DoctorCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/DoctorCommand.java) | Ubuntu/apt-only, CUDA-only release; model fetch has no checksum verification (unlike [fetch_lc0_net.sh](scripts/fetch_lc0_net.sh)); version duplicated in [VersionCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/VersionCommand.java):20 and [package.json](package.json):3. |
| **Docs site** | **ok** | [build_docs_site.py](scripts/build_docs_site.py), [build_manual_pdf.py](scripts/build_manual_pdf.py), [wiki/ai-agents.md](wiki/ai-agents.md) | Live doc drift: [getting-started.md](wiki/getting-started.md):48 claims a committed `crtk.jar` that is gitignored; manual PDF silently needs a headless Chromium binary. |
| **ECO / opening data** | **ok** | [Encyclopedia.java](src/chess/eco/Encyclopedia.java), [config/book.eco.toml](config/book.eco.toml), [position/Opening.java](src/chess/tag/position/Opening.java), [EcoCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/EcoCommand.java) | Bundled book now has 3,412 parsed entries, complete A00-E99 coverage, and a `crtk eco` CLI for lookup/search/continuations/validate. Remaining debt: no reusable `chess.eco` opening-tree API beyond CLI-local continuation logic, no machine-readable provenance/checksum metadata, and brittle reflection on Toml internals. |
| **Local PGN database** | **absent** | ŌĆö (closest: [Pgn.java](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java), [Converter.java](src/chess/io/Converter.java)) | No indexed/queryable store, no game-id, no provenance, no `crtk pgn` area ŌĆö the keystone gap for the entire study mission. |
| **Game-review router** | **absent** | ŌĆö (primitives: [GameAnalyzer.java](src/chess/tag/game/GameAnalyzer.java), [RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java)) | No verb turns a reviewed game into study units; engine-graded `quality=`/`turning_point` verdicts are deferred/TODO. |
| **Repertoire / SRS** | **absent** | ŌĆö | No spaced-repetition or repertoire structures anywhere; needs the PGN store + study-unit producer + schemas first. |
| **Local API server / SDK** | **absent** | ŌĆö (seam: [Main.java](src/application/Main.java), in-process engine APIs) | No daemon, no programmatic catalog, no SDK; every CLI call pays JVM startup. |
| **Plugins** | **absent (rejected)** | [Protocol.java](src/chess/uci/Protocol.java) (sufficient config-as-extension) | Explicit non-goal ([TODO.txt](TODO.txt):632); fights determinism and the no-deps build. |
| **Platform sync / OTB / OCR** | **absent (reject/defer)** | ŌĆö | Boundary-gated; the in-boundary answer is always "export a PGN and import it." |

---

## 5. Market-gap analysis

This table positions CRTK against the tools its target users (study / research / ML / publishing / chess-programming) actually reach for today. The recurring theme: the established platforms own *engagement* (play, ratings, social, cloud convenience) but treat **local, deterministic, scriptable, owned data** as a second-class concern ŌĆö which is precisely the lane CRTK already lives in. CRTK's preserved values (one shared core, deterministic outputs, plain `javac --release 17`, stable JSON/JSONL contracts, grounded explanations, no cloud) map onto the structural weaknesses of every commercial offering below.

| Tool / category | Does well | Users struggle with | What CRTK should learn | What CRTK should avoid | Opportunity for CRTK |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Chess.com** | Mass play, integrated lessons, "Game Review" with one-click coach narration, huge puzzle library, polished apps | Closed ecosystem; your games/analysis live on their servers; opaque "accuracy"/"game review" numbers; subscription-gated depth; no scriptable export of *your* analysis | One-click "review my game ŌåÆ here's what to study" is the killer onboarding hook (CRTK has the parts but no router ŌĆö see [TagsCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/TagsCommand.java) `--analyze-game`, [RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java)) | Online play, matchmaking, ratings, social, "coach" gamification, paywalled analysis | Be the *local, inspectable* game-review-to-study tool: grounded tags instead of a black-box accuracy %, your data in your files |
| **Lichess** | Free, open-source, real Stockfish cloud eval, studies, opening explorer, broad API | Analysis quality depends on their cloud queue; studies are server-hosted; no local-first reproducible pipeline; explanations are eval bars, not grounded prose | Studies-as-a-first-class-artifact; opening explorer UX; the value of *free and open* as a trust signal | Account-centric storage, cloud eval dependency, online play | A fully offline, reproducible alternative: export your Lichess PGN, run the same analysis deterministically forever, no queue |
| **ChessBase** | The de-facto serious game **database** (search by position/player/material, reference DB, huge corpora) | Expensive, Windows-centric, proprietary binary formats, clunky scripting, no clean machine-readable contract for automation/ML | Position-keyed indexing and queryable game stores are *the* power-user feature CRTK is missing (digest theme **A** is `partial`/in-memory only ŌĆö [PgnExplorerModel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java) has no CLI peer) | Proprietary formats, paid-license lock-in, Windows-only, GUI-only workflows | A free, JSON/JSONL-backed, position-`signatureCore()`-indexed local PGN database with a `crtk pgn` CLI area ŌĆö ChessBase's core value without the lock-in |
| **Chessable** | Spaced-repetition (MoveTrainer) for openings/endgames; "learn by repetition" is genuinely effective | Content is purchased courses, not *your* games/mistakes; closed scheduler; no way to turn your own blunders into SRS cards | SRS over study units works; an explanation-first repertoire trainer is a real category (digest theme **D** is `absent`) | Marketplace/course-selling model, cloud accounts, locked content | Turn *your reviewed mistakes* into local SRS cards (D depends on A+C+F) ŌĆö repertoire/SRS seeded from your own games, not bought courses |
| **ChessTempo** | Tactics with **human-calibrated puzzle ratings**, theme tagging, large rated puzzle set | Ratings are their corpus/userbase; not reproducible offline; no provenance on how a puzzle was scored | Human-calibrated rating is the bar CRTK's heuristic [Scorer.java](src/chess/puzzle/Scorer.java) is *not* validated against (it self-warns "Elo-like only inside the puzzle corpus") | Presenting heuristic ratings as human Elo; cloud-only puzzle DB | Be honest *and* reproducible: deterministic difficulty features + grounded motif tags, with a documented calibration gap rather than a fake number |
| **Lucas Chess** | Free desktop GUI, training modes, bundles engines, beginner-friendly | Sprawling/dated UX; not built for scripting or ML; no stable data contract | A friendly desktop entry point lowers onboarding (CRTK's Workbench already mirrors the CLI) | Becoming a kitchen-sink GUI; UI features that the CLI can't reproduce (CRTK's "CLI is source of truth" invariant is a strength to keep) | A *coherent* desktop Workbench that is a thin mirror of a scriptable, contract-stable CLI ŌĆö the inverse of Lucas's GUI-first sprawl |
| **SCID vs PC** | Free local game database, position search, fast on huge bases | Tcl/Tk UX, fragile binary `.si4` format, niche, hard to automate, aging codebase | Local position search at scale is exactly the gap; SCID proves there's a free-DB audience | Bespoke binary formats nobody else can read; single-maintainer Tcl rot | A modern, plain-Java, JSON-contract local DB that ML/agents can consume directly (no format reverse-engineering) |
| **Arena (GUI)** | Classic free engine-testing/UCI GUI on Windows | Windows-only, dated, manual; no SPRT/gauntlet automation or reproducible match records | Engine A/B testing has a real audience (CRTK already has [Gauntlet.java](src/chess/engine/Gauntlet.java) + [Sprt.java](src/chess/engine/Sprt.java)) | GUI-driven, non-reproducible manual matches | Scriptable, deterministic gauntlet/SPRT with *persisted, provenance-tagged* match records (a gap even CRTK has today ŌĆö results are printed, not stored) |
| **Chessvision.ai** | Best-in-class **diagram/scoresheet OCR** (image ŌåÆ FEN/PGN) from books, videos, screenshots | Cloud service, subscription, your scans go to their servers; not local | The *output* (a clean PGN/FEN) is the only thing CRTK needs to consume | Building an in-repo CV/OCR model ŌĆö impossible under no-third-party-deps + `javac` build (digest theme **O** correctly `reject`) | Stay the *destination*: "OCR it elsewhere, import the PGN into CRTK" ŌĆö OCR reduces to theme A's import path |
| **DGT / OTB boards** | Physical-board capture, live tournament relay/broadcast | Hardware/serial/realtime streaming; tournament-organizer audience, not study/research | Nothing structurally ŌĆö this is a different product | Real-time device I/O, live feeds, broadcast relay (digest theme **N** correctly `reject`; pulls toward the forbidden live/online space) | None worth pursuing; the in-boundary answer is "export the PGN, study it in CRTK" |
| **python-chess** | The reference *library*: legal moves, PGN/FEN, UCI driver, perft ŌĆö the ML/research community's default building block | It's a library, not a toolkit: you write the pipeline, the eval, the dataset export, the determinism guarantees yourself; Python-only | This is CRTK's closest *spiritual* competitor and the bar for a clean programmatic surface; an SDK + machine-readable command catalog would let CRTK serve the same scripters (themes **F**, **E**) | Trying to *replace* python-chess as a library import inside Python projects | Offer a **deterministic, batteries-included** alternative: dataset export, puzzle mining, grounded tags, publishing ŌĆö the pipeline python-chess users hand-roll. Pair with a thin Python SDK over a stable CLI catalog so they can call CRTK from notebooks |
| **Lichess API / berserk** | Programmatic access to games, puzzles, studies, cloud eval; `berserk` is a clean Python client | Online dependency, rate limits, account scope; you're renting Lichess's compute and data | A clean client SDK over a stable contract is what makes an API adopted; CRTK has the metadata in [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) but never serializes it | Becoming a network API to a remote service; account/OAuth surface | A *local* SDK: `crtk help --json` catalog + JSON Schemas (theme **F**) ŌåÆ generated Python/TS stubs over a localhost daemon (theme **E**), no rate limits, no account, no network |
| **Chessify / cloud engines** | Rent huge cloud Stockfish/Lc0 horsepower on demand | Pay-per-minute, online, non-reproducible (depth/queue vary), your positions leave your machine | Nothing about the *cloud* model | Cloud credits, hosted compute, chasing Stockfish strength (explicit CRTK product boundary) | The anti-cloud stance *is* the pitch: deterministic local analysis routed through your own external UCI engine ([Engine.java](src/chess/uci/Engine.java)) ŌĆö same answer every time, offline, private |

### The single biggest opening

**A free, local-first, reproducible game database + game-review-to-study loop that nobody else offers as an open, scriptable, machine-readable whole.** Every commercial tool splits this value across silos: ChessBase owns the *database* but is proprietary/Windows/paid; Chess.com owns *game review* but as a cloud black box; Chessable owns *SRS* but over bought courses, not your games; Lichess owns *open* but is cloud-bound. CRTK already has the hard parts in the repo ŌĆö a shared deterministic core, PGN/Game parsing ([Pgn.java](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java)), whole-game tagging, eval-delta detection, a puzzle miner, and an in-memory PGN explorer ŌĆö but they are unconnected, CLI-less, and unindexed (themes **A** and **C** are `partial`, with no `crtk pgn` area at all). Wiring "import your games ŌåÆ index them ŌåÆ review them ŌåÆ spin mistakes into grounded study units and SRS cards, all offline and in plain JSON" turns a pile of strong primitives into the one thing the market structurally cannot sell: a study toolkit you fully own.

---

## 6. Product-positioning recommendation

**One-sentence positioning:** CRTK is the local-first, deterministic chess *toolkit* ŌĆö one shared rules core that turns your own games and positions into grounded analysis, reproducible datasets, study material, and print-ready books, entirely offline and fully scriptable; it is not an online play, coaching, or cloud platform.

**README tagline ŌĆö evolution.** The current tagline, *"A deterministic chess programming toolkit,"* is accurate but undersells the product to everyone who isn't already a chess programmer: it reads as a library for engine hackers, not a study/research/publishing tool. It also buries the two most defensible differentiators ŌĆö *local-first* and *your data*. Suggested evolution:

> **A local-first, deterministic chess toolkit ŌĆö your games, your analysis, your datasets, offline.**

(Keep "deterministic"; it is a genuine, testable promise ŌĆö [Result.java](src/chess/engine/Result.java) and the regression suite enforce same-input-same-output. Drop the narrowing word "programming" from the *headline* but keep the programmer audience front-and-center in the body and the chess-programmers bullet block below.)

**Homepage hero copy (2-3 sentences):**

> ChessRTK (`crtk`) is a local-first chess toolkit built on one shared, deterministic rules core: import your own games, analyze them with your own engines, mine puzzles, export reproducible ML datasets, and publish print-ready books ŌĆö all offline, all from a scriptable command line that the desktop Workbench mirrors exactly. Every answer is reproducible to the byte and grounded in detectable chess facts, so nothing is a black box and nothing leaves your machine. ChessRTK is **not** an online play, matchmaking, or cloud-analysis platform ŌĆö when you need reference-grade strength, it drives your external UCI engine locally rather than renting someone else's cloud.

---

**For normal users (study / play-review / improvement):**

- Review your *own* games offline: import a PGN, get grounded move-by-move annotations (what each move creates, threatens, and the turning points) instead of an opaque cloud "accuracy %".
- Practice with mined tactical puzzles tagged by deterministic motif and difficulty features ŌĆö generated from positions you actually play, not a generic set.
- Build study material from your mistakes (planned: review ŌåÆ study units ŌåÆ spaced repetition), so what you practice is what *you* get wrong.
- Print your own puzzle and study books as real PDFs ([book-publishing.md](wiki/book-publishing.md)) ŌĆö no LaTeX, no online service.
- *Not* a place to play games or earn ratings: CRTK studies the chess you bring it; you keep playing wherever you already play.

**For researchers / ML practitioners:**

- One deterministic, dependency-free Java 17 core: the same legality, perft-honest movegen, and `signatureCore` keys back every dataset, so labels never drift between tools.
- Reproducible dataset export to NumPy/JSONL ([RecordDatasetExporter.java](src/chess/io/RecordDatasetExporter.java), [RecordLc0Exporter.java](src/chess/io/RecordLc0Exporter.java)) with train==serve encoding ŌĆö the pipeline python-chess users hand-roll, batteries included.
- Grounded, engine-free position tags and explanations ([Generator.java](src/chess/tag/Generator.java), [ClassicalPositionDescriptionGenerator.java](src/chess/describe/ClassicalPositionDescriptionGenerator.java)) for interpretable features and labels.
- Strength experiments without cloud credits: deterministic self-play gauntlet + pentanomial SPRT ([Gauntlet.java](src/chess/engine/Gauntlet.java), [Sprt.java](src/chess/engine/Sprt.java)) over your own engine builds.
- *Not* a cloud-compute or hosted-inference service: CRTK runs on your hardware, and reference-grade eval routes through an external UCI engine you control ŌĆö never a rented cloud.

**For chess programmers:**

- A noun-then-verb CLI (`crtk <area> <action>`) with stable JSON/JSONL contracts and meaningful exit codes ŌĆö scriptable and agent-friendly ([ai-agents.md](wiki/ai-agents.md)).
- Plain `javac --release 17` build, zero third-party Java deps, no Maven/Gradle ŌĆö clone and compile, no toolchain archaeology.
- Strict, inspectable primitives: 4-or-6-field FEN parsing ([Fen.java](src/chess/core/Fen.java)), single-source castling validation, Chess960 support, and `engine perft-suite` honesty gates.
- Drive any UCI engine as a child process via a data-driven TOML protocol ([Protocol.java](src/chess/uci/Protocol.java)) ŌĆö a new engine is a config change, not code.
- *Not* a playing engine competing on strength: CRTK is the *toolbox around* engines and chess data, deliberately not chasing Stockfish-level play.

**For coaches / study authors:**

- Turn analyzed positions into typeset puzzle and study books with a native, dependency-free PDF writer ([book/render/Writer.java](src/chess/book/render/Writer.java)) ŌĆö manifests render byte-stable, so a book is diffable like source.
- Validated content: every FEN and solution line is replayed through the shared core before a byte is written ([BookValidator.java](src/chess/book/model/BookValidator.java)), so a published line is never illegal.
- Author annotated studies with hints, comments, and figurine SAN diagrams from one TOML/JSON manifest, mirrored in the Workbench.
- Grounded explanations you can trust in front of students: the prose states only facts present in the position, never invented motifs or hallucinated lines.
- *Not* an online classroom or coaching marketplace: CRTK produces the material you teach from; it does not host lessons, students, or accounts.

---

## 7. Prioritized roadmap overview

One table, every initiative the theme verdicts marked `build-now` or `build-later`, plus the highest-value items salvaged from the existing [TODO.txt](TODO.txt) and [URGENT.md](URGENT.md). Rows are sorted P0 ŌåÆ P1 ŌåÆ P2 ŌåÆ P3. `reject` themes (L plugins, N OTB/broadcast, O OCR) and `defer` themes (B platform-sync, K editor tooling) appear only where a non-trivial in-boundary slice survives; the rest are summarized in the closing note.

Priorities reflect a single ordering principle: **bounded correctness + onboarding fixes first, then the product foundation (schemas ŌåÆ game store ŌåÆ review router) the existing roadmap never addressed, then the internal GUI/research polish that currently dominates [TODO.txt](TODO.txt).** Complexity is small / medium / large / xlarge.

| Priority | Initiative | User value | Market pain addressed | Why now | Complexity | Dependencies | Main packages / files affected | Acceptance criteria (1 line) |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **P0** | Close URGENT OTIS-weights landmine | Anyone using real OTIS weights stops getting silently wrong (geometrically inverted) policy | Hidden correctness bug erodes trust in the ML pillar | The channel-10 pawn fix shipped, but any pre-2026-06-02 weights are still wrong; tracked only in a stray file | small | none | [URGENT.md](URGENT.md), [Model.java](src/chess/nn/otis/Model.java) | Pre-fix weights re-exported or none in use; URGENT.md deleted or converted to a tracked issue |
| **P0** | Theme F ŌĆö machine-readable command catalog + JSON Schemas + fail-loud validation | Agents/SDKs/editors consume a stable contract instead of scraping prose; corrupt records fail loudly not silently | No `crtk help --json`/`crtk schema`; zero `*.schema.json` files; [Record.java](src/chess/struct/Record.java) has no schema version; malformed input is silently dropped | Precondition for E, K, A, C, I ŌĆö nothing can build a stable contract on prose tables; metadata already lives in memory | medium | none | [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java), [CliCommand.java](src/application/cli/CliCommand.java), [Record.java](src/chess/struct/Record.java), [RecordIO.java](src/application/cli/RecordIO.java), [Validation.java](src/application/cli/Validation.java) | `crtk help --json` emits the full area/action/flag/exit-code catalog; published JSON Schemas for .record + training-jsonl + dataset meta.json; a `--strict` path that errors on malformed records |
| **P0** | TODO/URGENT reconciliation against HEAD | Contributors plan against reality instead of rebuilding finished code | [TODO.txt](TODO.txt) is stale and self-contradictory ŌĆö actively dangerous as a plan | Verified: [Threats.java](src/chess/tag/Threats.java) is a real 278-line impl (TODO calls it an "11-byte stub"); OTIS CUDA lib already built (TODO says "add an implementation") | small | none | [TODO.txt](TODO.txt), [URGENT.md](URGENT.md) | Stale "rebuild Threats"/"add OTIS CUDA" blocks struck; shipped items marked DONE; absent product themes (A/C/F) added to the roadmap |
| **P1** | Theme A ŌĆö local PGN game database (`crtk pgn` area) | Store, index, and query your own games locally ŌĆö the substrate every study workflow stands on | Biggest missing link to "best local-first study toolkit"; [PgnExplorerModel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java) logic is in-memory, workbench-only, no CLI peer, no game-id/provenance | The review loop, repertoire/SRS, and explanation-in-context all depend on this; the GUI index logic already exists to promote into core | large | F | [Pgn.java](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java), [Game.java](src/chess/struct/Game.java), [Record.java](src/chess/struct/Record.java), [Reader.java](src/chess/io/Reader.java)/[Writer.java](src/chess/io/Writer.java), [Converter.java](src/chess/io/Converter.java), [PgnExplorerModel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java) | `crtk pgn import/index/query/show/stats` over an on-disk store keyed on game-id + `Position.signatureCore()`; same logic backs CLI and workbench |
| **P1** | Theme C ŌĆö game-review-to-study router | Turn a played game into study units: blunder ŌåÆ puzzle of the refutation, annotated lines | Primitives exist (`fen tags --analyze-game`, `record analysis-delta`, the miner) but no verb connects them; mining can't say "human played X, puzzle is the refutation" | The grounded dynamic tag layers are shipped ([GameAnalyzer.java](src/chess/tag/game/GameAnalyzer.java) et al.); only the router and engine-graded turning-point verdicts are missing | large | A, F | [GameAnalyzer.java](src/chess/tag/game/GameAnalyzer.java), [LineAnalyzer.java](src/chess/tag/game/LineAnalyzer.java), [RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java), [Engine.java](src/chess/uci/Engine.java), [MineCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/MineCommand.java), [GameReviewPanel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/GameReviewPanel.java) | A CLI verb ingests a PGN game, flags blunders/turning-points (graded via external UCI), and emits puzzle/study Records validated against F's schema |
| **P1** | Theme I ŌĆö uniform dataset provenance + fix broken classifier path | Reproducible datasets that can actually prove what produced them; default classifier loads out of the box | [datasets.md](wiki/datasets.md) promises byte-exact provenance but `record dataset npy` writes no meta.json; no meta captures version/git/checksums; `classifier` default-weights path is broken (`classifier_` vs shipped `puzzle-classifier_`) | Cheap, high ROI, directly defends the "reproducible datasets" core value; pairs with F's schema work | medium | F | [RecordDatasetExporter.java](src/chess/io/RecordDatasetExporter.java), [ClassifierDatasetExporter.java](src/chess/io/ClassifierDatasetExporter.java), [RecordLc0Exporter.java](src/chess/io/RecordLc0Exporter.java), [RunManifest.java](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java), [Model.java](src/chess/nn/classifier/Model.java), [fetch_lc0_net.sh](scripts/fetch_lc0_net.sh) | Every exporter writes a meta.json with crtk version + git commit + input/weights checksums; classifier `loadDefault()` works against the shipped tree; install.sh verifies weight sha256 |
| **P1** | TODO #5 ŌĆö register dynamic tag families in Sort/Literals + document in SCHEMA.md | Game-review tags become sortable/dedupable/filterable like static tags | MOVE_EFFECT/LINE/VARIATION/GAME bypass the canonical pipeline (absent from [Sort.java](src/chess/tag/Sort.java) `FAMILY_ORDER` and [Literals.java](src/chess/tag/core/Literals.java)); inline string literals | Real unfinished tag work (new motifs have plateaued) and a hard prerequisite for C's study-unit output | medium | none | [Sort.java](src/chess/tag/Sort.java), [Literals.java](src/chess/tag/core/Literals.java), [MoveEffect.java](src/chess/tag/MoveEffect.java), [GameAnalyzer.java](src/chess/tag/game/GameAnalyzer.java), [SCHEMA.md](tag/SCHEMA.md) | The four dynamic families are in `FAMILY_ORDER`, use `Literals` constants, parse through `Line.java`, and are documented in SCHEMA.md |
| **P1** | Theme G ŌĆö deepen grounded explanation ("why"/plan + wire the working T5) | Explanations say *why* ("backward d6 pawn ŌåÆ plan Nd5") not just *what* ("White is better"); fluent grounded prose | [PositionDescriptionExtractor.java](src/chess/describe/PositionDescriptionExtractor.java) collects KingSafety/Structure/passer tags but never turns them into sentences; describe-T5 is a dead stub | Highest-value after C gives whole-game context; the documented inference-time grounding/verification pass is unimplemented and must land before any T5 to prevent hallucination | medium | C | [ClassicalPositionDescriptionGenerator.java](src/chess/describe/ClassicalPositionDescriptionGenerator.java), [PositionDescriptionExtractor.java](src/chess/describe/PositionDescriptionExtractor.java), [Runner.java](src/chess/nn/t5/Runner.java), [TagPrompt.java](src/chess/nn/t5/TagPrompt.java), [Generator.java](src/chess/tag/Generator.java) | Prose names a plan/causation field grounded in detected tags; the working `chess.nn.t5` path replaces the dead describe stub behind a legal-SAN verification pass |
| **P1** | TODO #3/#8 ŌĆö finish docs site, fix doc/code drift, fix live-NN regression | New users aren't misled on first run; live search visualization advances incrementally | [getting-started.md](wiki/getting-started.md) claims a prebuilt `crtk.jar` ships in repo root but `crtk.jar` is gitignored (clean clone fails `java -jar`); [workbench.md](wiki/workbench.md) shows 12 tabs vs shipped 8 | Small, bounded, removes live onboarding footguns; the NN-only-shows-start/end-frame item is a regression (bug), not a feature | small | none | [getting-started.md](wiki/getting-started.md), [workbench.md](wiki/workbench.md), [build_docs_site.py](scripts/build_docs_site.py), [VersionCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/VersionCommand.java) | Docs match shipped tabs/jar reality; version single-sourced; live NN view advances frame-by-frame (fix only the regression, not the graph canvas) |
| **P1** | OTIS CPUŌåöCUDA policy parity fix | OTIS CUDA backend returns the same policy ordering as CPU | Native path returns raw policy-head logits, skips per-legal-move refinement ([Backend.java](src/chess/nn/otis/cuda/Backend.java)) ŌĆö CPU/GPU disagree at the policy level | Correctness, not speed; the one item worth keeping from the OTIS CUDA theme | medium | none | [Backend.java](src/chess/nn/otis/cuda/Backend.java), [otis_gpu_impl.inl](native/common/otis_gpu_impl.inl), [OtisBackendRegressionTest.java](src/testing/OtisBackendRegressionTest.java) | Parity test asserts CPU == CUDA on *policy* (not just WDL) within tolerance |
| **P2** | Theme E ŌĆö localhost analysis/automation daemon + generated SDK stubs | Interactive agents skip per-invocation JVM startup; programmatic access to engine/tag/describe | No server exists anywhere (verified: no `ServerSocket`/`HttpServer` in src); every CLI call pays cold-start | Useful but premature ŌĆö must expose F's catalog/schemas or it hard-codes contracts F would replace; **boundary: localhost analysis only, never online play/cloud** | large | F | [Main.java](src/application/Main.java), [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java), [AlphaBeta.java](src/chess/engine/AlphaBeta.java)/[Mcts.java](src/chess/engine/Mcts.java)/[MateProver.java](src/chess/engine/MateProver.java), [Engine.java](src/chess/uci/Engine.java), [CommandRunner.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java) | A localhost JSON-RPC daemon fronts `application.Main`; SDK stubs are generated from the F catalog and kept in sync by a regression |

| **P2** | Theme J ŌĆö cross-platform packaging (defer the big slice) | Windows/macOS users get a real install path, not just the portable jar | Packaging is Ubuntu/apt only; release packager ships CUDA only; no Win/macOS bundle despite a desktop workbench | Cheap correctness bugs (doc-drift, version single-source, checksums) fold into I/M now; broad jpackage/jlink work doesn't advance the study mission and the jar runs today | medium | I | [install.sh](install.sh), [make_release_linux_cuda.sh](scripts/make_release_linux_cuda.sh), [DoctorCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/DoctorCommand.java), [VersionCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/VersionCommand.java) | `crtk doctor --json`; version single-sourced; (later) jpackage/jlink bundles for Linux/Win/macOS with checksums |
| **P2** | Theme K ŌĆö VSCode tasks/completion + thin Jupyter wrapper | Editor completion + schema-validated outputs; notebook cells without per-cell JVM cold-start | Absent (no notebook integration; only `.npy` bridge); value is parasitic on F's catalog and benefits from E's daemon | Downstream consumer, not a foundation; cheap once F (and ideally E) exist | medium | F, E | [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java), [RecordDatasetExporter.java](src/chess/io/RecordDatasetExporter.java), [Main.java](src/application/Main.java) | A VSCode extension offers catalog-driven completion/tasks; a Jupyter helper invokes the daemon and parses schema'd JSON |
| **P3** | Theme D ŌĆö repertoire / SRS (explanation-first) | Spaced-repetition study of your own openings/mistakes, with grounded explanations | Absent everywhere; in-boundary but genuinely downstream | Needs A (store + review state), C (study-unit producer), F (card schema), G (explanations), and a reusable `chess.eco` line-continuation API; the CLI now has `eco continuations`, but repertoire should not depend on CLI-local logic | large | A, C, F, G | [Encyclopedia.java](src/chess/eco/Encyclopedia.java), [Entry.java](src/chess/eco/Entry.java), [OpeningBook.java](src/application/gui/workbench/play/OpeningBook.java), [Record.java](src/chess/struct/Record.java) | A scheduler tracks per-card review state keyed on `signatureCore()`; cards are produced by C and explained by G; ECO gains a shared line-continuation API |
| **P3** | Theme B ŌĆö read-only PGN/folder import (boundary-gated) | Convenience import of a user's exported games from a file or public export | Absent; closest to the hard product boundary | A "folder import" is just A's `pgn import` over local files; lichess/chess.com fetch adds dependency + boundary risk for marginal value over "export PGN, import it" | medium | A | [Pgn.java](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java), [Reader.java](src/chess/io/Reader.java), A's `crtk pgn import` | Read-only import from a user-supplied export file or public read-only API; **no account linking, sync, matchmaking, or social features** |

### Themes deliberately not in the table

- **L (plugins) ŌĆö reject.** Explicitly a NON-GOAL in [TODO.txt](TODO.txt); a dynamic registry fights determinism, the no-deps build, and reproducibility. The legitimate extension need (a new UCI engine) is already met by config-as-extension via [Protocol.java](src/chess/uci/Protocol.java) (a TOML, not code).
- **N (OTB/broadcast) ŌĆö reject.** Pulls toward the forbidden live/online space; real-time device/serial/network I/O contradicts the deterministic, process-per-invocation, local-artifact architecture. Out-of-boundary answer: export the PGN, use A/C.
- **O (OCR/scan) ŌĆö reject.** A self-contained CV research project incompatible with the plain-`javac`/no-third-party-deps constraint. If ever pursued, it belongs in the external playground; crtk only consumes its FEN/PGN output via A.
- **Internal-polish TODO items demoted below all product-foundation work:** the Workbench MCTS graph canvas, NN view polish, OTIS CUDA *kernel* optimization (the network ships only a random placeholder, so throughput is premature), T5 *weights* work (the model cannot ship without weights that do not exist), new tactical/checkmate motifs (plateaued), and "Workbench UI Foundation" as a standalone theme (fold into UX Redesign). Run SonarLint hygiene as a *capped* continuous background stream ŌĆö never let "scan until zero warnings" gate product work.

---

## 8. Deep-dive plans

The ten deep-dives below (8AŌĆō8J) expand each `build-now`/`build-later` theme into issue-sized, grounded work. Each carries its own priority, complexity, dependency chain, proposed CLI/Workbench surface, schema implications, reuse list, testing plan, risks, and acceptance criteria. Cross-cutting concerns that several deep-dives touch ŌĆö the Workbench redesign, the data/schema contracts, the review-to-study pipeline, the ML plan, grounded explanation, and packaging ŌĆö are surfaced once in Sections 10ŌĆō15 and cross-referenced here rather than repeated.

### 8A. Local PGN database / modern ChessBase-lite layer

**Classification:** P1 ┬Ę complexity **large** ┬Ę short-term *(MVP)* ŌåÆ medium-term *(full)* ┬Ę depends on **F (schemas/validation)** for the on-disk store contract; is a hard dependency of **C (review-to-study router)**, **D (repertoire/SRS)**, and partially **B (read-only PGN import)**.

> Verdict from the theme map: *build-now, P1, large*. This section turns that verdict into issue-sized work. The one-shared-core, deterministic-output, plain-`javac` values are treated as hard constraints, not aspirations.

---

#### Goal

Give CRTK a **local, indexed, queryable game store** ŌĆö the substrate a study/research toolkit needs and the single biggest missing product foundation. Today the repo can *parse, merge, and round-trip* PGN ([`Pgn.java`](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java), [`Game.java`](src/chess/struct/Game.java), [`Converter.java`](src/chess/io/Converter.java)) and the Workbench can *search a single loaded file in memory* ([`PgnExplorerModel.java`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java)), but there is **no persistent store, no game id, no provenance, no position index, and no `crtk pgn`/`crtk db` CLI area** (verified: [`CliRegistry.java`](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) registers only stateless `fen pgn`, `record export pgn`, `puzzle pgn` conversions at lines 402, 242, 749). The goal is to make "store my games, find any position across all of them, find duplicates, attach provenance" a first-class, deterministic, CLI-first capability that the Workbench mirrors.

#### User story

> *"I have 8,000 of my own games as PGN exports from three sources. I want to import them once, then ask: which games reached this exact pawn structure? Which are duplicates? Which are my losses in the Najdorf as Black since 2024? Show me game #4127 with full headers and the mainline. And I want every answer to be byte-identical when I re-run it tomorrow."*

That whole loop is impossible today without re-parsing every file on every query and writing custom Java. CRTK should answer it from one `crtk db` area over one local store.

#### Non-goals

- **No online play / sync / matchmaking / social / cloud.** Hard product boundary. The store is local files only.
- **No SQL engine / no third-party DB dependency.** Violates the plain-`javac --release 17`, no-Maven/Gradle, minimal-deps value. (See *Architecture* below for the SQLite/DuckDB rejection.)
- **No re-implementation of search/parse logic in the GUI.** The Workbench mirrors the CLI; one shared store layer in `chess.*`.
- **No new "tolerant-and-silent" data loss.** Unlike [`Record.fromJson`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) (line 454, returns `null` on bad input) and [`Reader.readJsonFile`](src/chess/io/Reader.java) (line 55, skips malformed), the importer must report per-game errors. This is where theme F's fail-loud principle lands.
- **No engine analysis inside the DB layer.** The DB stores games + provenance + indexes. Analysis is a separate pass (theme C) that *reads* the DB and *writes* `.record` study units.

---

#### MVP (smallest shippable)

A single new core package `chess.db` plus a `crtk db` CLI area that operates on **one sharded JSONL store directory** (the recommended format ŌĆö see *Architecture*). MVP scope:

1. `crtk db import <pgn...>` ŌĆö parse PGN via [`Pgn.read`](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java#L60) / `Pgn.parseGames` (line 162), assign a stable `gameId`, stamp provenance, append game rows + a position index. Per-game parse failures reported to stderr with a count, **not** silently dropped.
2. `crtk db find --fen <FEN>` ŌĆö list games whose mainline reaches a position, using the same counter-insensitive position key the Workbench already uses ([`PgnExplorerModel.positionKey`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java#L274), strips fields 5ŌĆō6).
3. `crtk db show <gameId> [--format pgn|json]` ŌĆö print one game (PGN via [`Pgn.toPgn`](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java#L387), JSON via theme-F schema).
4. `crtk db stats` ŌĆö counts: games, unique positions, duplicates, by-result, by-ECO.

MVP store = a directory of append-only JSONL shards + one position-index JSONL. No daemon, no in-memory residency requirement, streamable. This is shippable in isolation and immediately useful.

#### Full version

- Structured query language for headers (`--white`, `--black`, `--result`, `--eco`, `--date-from/--date-to`, `--event`, free-text `--query`) combined with `--fen` position filter and `--mainline-only|--with-variations` indexing scope.
- **Variation indexing** (index positions reached in sidelines, not just the mainline ŌĆö see below).
- **Duplicate detection** with `db dedupe` (preview + apply), reusing [`PgnExplorerModel.duplicateKey`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java#L163) semantics promoted into core.
- **Provenance queries** (`db sources`, filter by import batch / source file).
- **ECO auto-tagging on import** via [`Encyclopedia`](src/chess/eco/Encyclopedia.java) (`getNode(Position)` line 234, `signatureCore`-keyed lookup line 239) so a `--eco B90` filter works even on PGNs lacking the `[ECO]` tag.
- **Incremental re-import / idempotency** (re-importing the same file is a no-op by `gameId`).
- **Compaction** (`db compact` rewrites shards dropping tombstoned games, rebuilds index ŌĆö the only "mutation" that touches existing bytes).
- `db export` back to a single PGN or `.record` array for the rest of the pipeline.
- Chess960 games stored and indexed correctly (see below).

---

#### Proposed CLI surface (`crtk db ...`, noun-then-verb)

All paths default to a local store under `dump/db/` via [`PathOps.dumpPath`](src/application/cli/PathOps.java#L112), overridable with `--store <dir>`. No engine budgets apply to the DB layer itself (it does no search); the one command that *could* invoke analysis is `db analyze`, which delegates to the external-UCI path and therefore carries the standard explicit budgets.

```
crtk db import <file.pgn|dir...> [--store DIR] [--source NAME] [--recursive]
```
