```
                                 [--index mainline|variations] [--dedupe]
                                 [--on-error skip|fail] [-v|--verbose]
    Parse PGN, assign gameId, stamp provenance, append rows + index.
    --on-error fail  ŌåÆ abort + nonzero exit on first unparseable game (fail-loud, theme F)
    --on-error skip  ŌåÆ import the rest, report dropped count to stderr (default)
    --dedupe         ŌåÆ skip games whose duplicateKey already exists in the store

crtk db find [--store DIR] [--fen FEN | --startpos]
             [--white S] [--black S] [--player S] [--result 1-0|0-1|1/2-1/2|*]
             [--eco CODE] [--event S] [--date-from YYYY.MM.DD] [--date-to YYYY.MM.DD]
             [--query TEXT] [--scope mainline|variations]
             [--limit N] [--format table|json|jsonl] [-o FILE]
    AND-combine all predicates. --fen uses the counter-insensitive position index.
    Default output is one row per game; --jsonl is the machine contract (theme F).

crtk db show <gameId...> [--store DIR] [--format pgn|json|jsonl] [-o FILE]
    Emit full game(s): headers, start position, mainline + variations, comments, NAGs.

crtk db stats [--store DIR] [--by result|eco|source|year] [--format text|json]
    Counts: games, unique positions, duplicates, indexed plies, store bytes.

crtk db sources [--store DIR] [--format text|json]
    List import batches: source name, file, sha256, import time, game count.

crtk db dedupe [--store DIR] [--apply] [--format text|json]
    Preview (default) or apply duplicate removal by duplicateKey. --apply tombstones.

crtk db compact [--store DIR] [-v]
    Rewrite shards dropping tombstones, rebuild the position index. The only
    command that rewrites existing bytes; everything else is append-only.

crtk db export [--store DIR] [--fen FEN | --eco CODE | <gameId...>]
               [--format pgn|record] [-o FILE]
    Materialize a query result back to PGN or a .record JSON array for the
    downstream pipeline (record export, puzzle mine, theme C).

crtk db analyze [--store DIR] [--fen FEN | <gameId...>]
                -P|--protocol-path TOML
                [--max-nodes N] [--max-duration Ns] [--multipv N]
                [--threads N] [--hash N] [-o FILE]
    Optional: run external-UCI analysis over stored games' positions and write
    .record rows (NOT into the DB). Carries the standard explicit engine budgets.
    This is the seam theme C builds on; ships behind db, not as DB core.
```

**Naming note (issue-worthy decision):** the theme map calls this initiative `crtk pgn`. I recommend **`crtk db`** as the area noun because (a) `fen pgn`/`record export pgn`/`puzzle pgn` already exist as *format-conversion* verbs and a `pgn` area would collide conceptually, and (b) "db" names the *capability* (a queryable store) not the *format*. Import still accepts PGN; the area is the database. This is a one-line debate to settle before the first issue.

#### Proposed Workbench surface (mirror, no second impl)

The Workbench already has the *display* half built ([`PgnExplorerDialog.java`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerDialog.java), [`GameReviewPanel.java`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/GameReviewPanel.java)) but it runs over an in-memory single file. Productization:

- Promote `PgnExplorerModel`'s parse/filter/dedupe/position-key logic **down into `chess.db`** so both the CLI and the existing dialog call the same core. The current static methods (`entries`, `filter`, `filterByPosition`, `deduplicate`) become thin views over the store.
- A **Database view** in the registry-driven shell ([`WindowLifecycle.java`](src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowLifecycle.java) `ViewRegistry`): import button ŌåÆ spawns `crtk db import` via the existing child-JVM [`CommandRunner`](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java) (so the GUI literally runs the CLI, preserving "CLI is source of truth"); query panel mirrors `db find` flags; double-click a result routes to the board.
- Add `db find`/`db show`/`db stats` to [`CommandTemplates.java`](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java) so the command preview is the exact runnable CLI string. **No GUI-only query path** ŌĆö every Workbench query must be expressible as a `crtk db` command, enforced by `WorkbenchCommandRegression`.

ASSUMPTION: the "Database" Workbench surface is a mode/view, not a net-new top-level tab competing with the 13ŌåÆ6 consolidation; it should land *after* the CLI store exists (theme H is build-later and should be a beneficiary of A, per the theme map).

---

#### Data model / schema implications (concrete fields)

Two record kinds, both JSONL, both schema-versioned (theme F). These are *new* schemas; they do **not** overload [`Record.java`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) (which stays the analysis/puzzle row). The digest's "Record schema is thin ŌĆö no game id, no provenance, no schema version" gap is addressed here by a purpose-built game row rather than by stretching `Record`.

**Game row** (`crtk.db.game.v1`), one JSON object per line in a shard:
```
{
  "schema": "crtk.db.game.v1",
  "gameId": "<16-hex>",          // stable: see hashing below
  "source": { "name": "lichess-export", "file": "games.pgn",
              "fileSha256": "<64-hex>", "importedAt": 1718000000000,
              "importBatch": "<8-hex>" },
  "tags": { "Event": "...", "White": "...", "Black": "...",
            "Result": "1-0", "Date": "2024.05.01", "ECO": "B90", ... },
  "result": "1-0",
  "startFen": "rnbq.../...",     // 6-field; non-standard ŌćÆ Chess960/FEN-start
  "chess960": false,
  "ply": 84,
  "mainlineSan": "e4 c5 Nf3 ...",
  "pgn": "<full single-game PGN incl. variations/comments/NAGs>",
  "duplicateKey": "<positionKey>|<sanline-lc>|<result>",
  "ecoDetected": "B90",          // from Encyclopedia, may differ from tags.ECO
  "tombstoned": false
}
```
Storing the full `pgn` string verbatim is the one redundancy I accept: it guarantees lossless `db show` round-trip without re-serializing the [`Game.Node`](src/chess/struct/Game.java#L206) tree, and it sidesteps any `Pgn.toPgn` formatting drift. The structured fields are the *index keys*; the `pgn` blob is the *source of truth* for display.

**Position-index row** (`crtk.db.posindex.v1`), one per (position-key, gameId) edge:
```
{ "schema": "crtk.db.posindex.v1", "key": "<positionKey>",
  "sig": <signatureCore-long>, "gameId": "<16-hex>",
  "ply": 14, "scope": "mainline" }   // scope Ōłł mainline|variation
```
`key` is the human-readable counter-insensitive FEN prefix (fields 1ŌĆō4) already used by `PgnExplorerModel.positionKey`; `sig` is the numeric [`Position.signatureCore()`](src/chess/core/Position.java#L457) for fast equality. Both stored so lookups can collide-check (sig) and remain debuggable (key).

**Source/batch manifest** (`crtk.db.manifest.v1`): one per store, lists every import batch with file sha256, game count, schema versions present, and `crtkVersion` ŌĆö the provenance backbone (mirrors the [`RunManifest`](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java) sha256 pattern).

#### Architecture implications

**Store format ŌĆö recommend sharded JSONL + a JSONL position index. Reject SQLite, DuckDB, and a bespoke binary index.** Reasoning, grounded in the preserved values:

- **SQLite / DuckDB** are JNI/native third-party dependencies. They violate "plain `javac --release 17`, no Maven/Gradle, minimal/no third-party Java deps" *and* the determinism value (their on-disk bytes, page layout, and `ROWID` ordering are not byte-reproducible across versions/platforms). A pure-Java JDBC (e.g. H2) is still a third-party jar the build cannot pull without a dependency manager. **Hard no.**
- **Bespoke binary index** would be fast but opaque, non-diffable, and another hand-rolled format to version ŌĆö exactly the "no stable on-disk record format spec" debt the digest already flags for `.record`.
- **Sharded JSONL** fits every value: it is plain text (diffable, greppable, byte-stable), append-only (reuses the [`Writer.appendJsonObjects`](src/chess/io/Writer.java#L65) seek/rewrite pattern, though see the concurrency risk below), streamable (reuses [`RecordIO.streamRecordFile`](src/application/cli/RecordIO.java#L87) / `isJsonArrayFile` auto-detect at line 190), and needs zero dependencies. Queries stream the index JSONL once and resolve game rows by `gameId` ŌåÆ shard offset.

  Shard layout: `dump/db/games/shard-0001.jsonl` (ŌēżN games each, e.g. 5000), `dump/db/index/positions.jsonl`, `dump/db/manifest.json`. A small in-memory `gameId ŌåÆ (shard, byteOffset)` map is built by one streaming pass on open; for very large stores this map is itself persisted as `dump/db/index/games.jsonl` and rebuilt by `db compact`.

**Keeping the DB optional / out of the core build:** `chess.db` is a *new package in the same source tree* ŌĆö it adds no dependency, so "optional" here means **optional at runtime, not optional at compile time**. There is no third-party dep to isolate (that's the whole point of choosing JSONL). The CLI area is additive in `CliRegistry.buildRoot()`; if a user never runs `crtk db`, no store is created and nothing changes. This is strictly simpler than the digest's framing of "isolate any optional dep" ŌĆö by choosing JSONL we *have no optional dep to isolate*. Mark this as the deliberate tradeoff.

**Position hashing ŌĆö reuse the existing FNV digest; do NOT add Zobrist for this initiative.** The core already exposes [`Position.signatureCore()`](src/chess/core/Position.java#L457) (64-bit FNV-1a over board+turn+960-flag+castling-rights+rook-squares+EP+king-squares, counter-insensitive, lazily cached) and `signature()` (line 438, adds halfmove/fullmove). The DB index needs *counter-insensitive* keys so transpositions and clock-stripped imports collapse ŌĆö that is exactly `signatureCore()`. The digest correctly notes this is FNV, not a real incremental Zobrist, and flags collision risk "for large ML/dedup workloads." **Mitigation without scope creep:** store both the numeric `sig` *and* the human `key` (FEN fields 1ŌĆō4) per index row; a `find --fen` first filters by `sig` then *verifies* by `key` string equality, so a 64-bit FNV collision can never return a wrong game. Real incremental Zobrist is a separate, larger initiative (it would touch make/undo in [`Position.java`](src/chess/core/Position.java)); do not couple it to A. **Mark as ASSUMPTION** that FNV+key-verify is acceptable collision handling for a local single-user store (Ōēż low millions of positions); revisit if A ever backs a shared multi-million-position corpus.

**Variation indexing:** the existing `PgnExplorerModel.mainlineInfo` (line 235) only walks the mainline (`current.getNext()`). The full version must also descend `node.getVariations()` ([`Game.Node`](src/chess/struct/Game.java#L279)) when `--index variations` is set, emitting `scope:"variation"` index rows. This is a bounded recursive replay through the shared core ([`SAN.fromAlgebraic`](src/chess/core/SAN.java) ŌåÆ `Position.play`), identical machinery to the mainline walk. Default to `mainline` for store size; variation indexing is opt-in.

**Chess960 handling:** [`Position`](src/chess/core/Position.java) already round-trips 960 (`isChess960()` line 1714, `chess960Castling` field folded into `signatureCore` at line 468), [`Fen`](src/chess/core/Fen.java) parses Shredder/X-FEN castling, and [`Setup`](src/chess/core/Setup.java) knows all 960 starts. The DB stores `startFen` verbatim and a `chess960` boolean derived from `Position.isChess960()`. Because `signatureCore` already includes the 960 flag and rook squares, the position index is correct for 960 with **no special-casing**. The one gotcha: ECO auto-tagging must be skipped for 960 (the [`Opening`](src/chess/tag/position/Opening.java) tagger already skips 960 ŌĆö mirror that). Mark this as a low-risk, mostly-free win because the core did the hard part.

**Duplicate detection:** promote [`PgnExplorerModel.duplicateKey`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java#L163) (`positionKey(start) | sanline-lowercase | result`) into `chess.db` unchanged. It already collapses true duplicates while distinguishing same-opening different-game. `db import --dedupe` checks the key against an in-memory `Set` built from the store; `db dedupe` reports/tombstones after the fact. Tradeoff (issue-worthy): exact-mainline duplicate only ŌĆö it will *not* catch a game that is a prefix of another or differs only in trailing comments. Document that limit; do not try to be ChessBase's fuzzy matcher in MVP.

**Source provenance storage:** every game row carries a `source` object with the file's **sha256** (compute once per import file, reuse the [`RunManifest.sha256(Path)`](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java#L427) helper pattern), the file name, the user-supplied `--source NAME`, the import epoch-ms, and an `importBatch` id (sha of name+file+time). This is the provenance the digest says `Record` entirely lacks, and it is what makes "where did this game come from / re-import is idempotent" answerable. The batch manifest aggregates these for `db sources`.

---

#### Existing components to reuse (real files)

- [`chess.struct.Pgn`](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java) ŌĆö `read`/`parseGames`/`parseGame`/`toPgn`/`toPgnString` (the parse+serialize layer; do not rewrite).
- [`chess.struct.Game`](src/chess/struct/Game.java) ŌĆö the `Node` tree (tags, mainline, variations, comments, NAGs) walked for indexing.
- [`application.gui.workbench.game.PgnExplorerModel`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java) ŌĆö `positionKey`, `duplicateKey`, `mainlineInfo`, `filter`, `deduplicate`: **promote to `chess.db`**, leave a thin Workbench adapter.
- [`chess.core.Position`](src/chess/core/Position.java) ŌĆö `signatureCore()`, `signature()`, `isChess960()` for index keys and 960 correctness.
- [`chess.io.Writer.appendJsonObjects`](src/chess/io/Writer.java#L65) and [`chess.io.Reader`](src/chess/io/Reader.java) ŌĆö append/stream JSONL shards (with the concurrency caveat below).
- [`application.cli.RecordIO`](src/application/cli/RecordIO.java) ŌĆö `streamRecordFile`/`isJsonArrayFile` streaming pattern for index/shard reads.
- [`chess.eco.Encyclopedia`](src/chess/eco/Encyclopedia.java) ŌĆö `getNode(Position)` for `ecoDetected` on import.
- [`application.cli.PathOps`](src/application/cli/PathOps.java) ŌĆö `dumpPath` for the default `dump/db/` store (respects the local-artifact contract).
- [`application.gui.workbench.command.CommandRunner`](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java) ŌĆö child-JVM CLI invocation so the Workbench Database view has no second impl.

#### Files / packages likely affected

- **New:** `src/chess/db/` (e.g. `GameStore.java`, `GameRow.java`, `PositionIndex.java`, `ImportResult.java`, `DuplicateKey.java`, `package-info.java`).
- **New:** `src/application/cli/command/DbCommand.java` (the `crtk db` handlers).
- **Edit:** [`src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java`](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) ŌĆö register the `db` group in `buildRoot()` (additive; watch the duplicate-token guard).
- **Edit:** [`src/application/cli/Constants.java`](src/application/cli/Constants.java) ŌĆö `CMD_DB`, `OPT_STORE`, `OPT_SOURCE`, `OPT_SCOPE`, etc.
- **Edit:** [`src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java) ŌĆö re-point at `chess.db`.
- **Edit:** [`src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowLifecycle.java`](src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowLifecycle.java) + `CommandTemplates.java` ŌĆö Database view + templates (medium-term, theme H).
- **New (theme F overlap):** `chess/db/SCHEMA.md` + JSON Schema files for the three schemas; a `crtk db` entry in the `crtk help --json` catalog.

#### Testing plan (in-house harness style ŌĆö `main()` + `TestSupport`, no JUnit)

New `src/testing/DbStoreRegressionTest.java` (and friends), wired into the `cli`/`core` targets of [`scripts/run_regression_suite.sh`](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh) (avoid the digest's "unwired test" rot ŌĆö explicitly add it to the runner, not just the source tree):

- **Round-trip:** import a known PGN ŌåÆ `db show <id> --format pgn` byte-equals the canonical `Pgn.toPgn` of the same game (golden string in source).
- **Determinism:** import the same fixture twice into fresh stores ŌåÆ game shard bytes and index bytes are **byte-identical** (asserts `gameId` and ordering are not time/RNG-dependent ŌĆö `importedAt` must be injectable/strippable for the assertion, mirroring the `Result.elapsedMillis` determinism trap the digest flags).
- **Position find:** import a Najdorf game, `db find --fen <a B90 position>` returns exactly that game; a never-reached position returns empty; counter-insensitive (different halfmove clock in the query FEN still matches).
- **Chess960:** import a 960 game with a non-standard `[FEN]`/`[Variant]` start; `chess960:true` stored, `db find` by a 960 position hits, ECO auto-tag skipped.
- **Duplicates:** import a file with one exact-duplicate game ŌåÆ `db stats` reports 1 duplicate, `db dedupe --apply` then `db stats` reports 0, game count drops by 1.
- **Provenance:** `db sources` lists the import file with a stable sha256; re-import of the same file with `--dedupe` adds 0 games (idempotency).
- **Fail-loud:** import a PGN with one unparseable game; `--on-error fail` ŌåÆ nonzero exit + the bad game named; `--on-error skip` ŌåÆ others imported, dropped count on stderr (contrast with current silent-skip in `Reader`/`Record.fromJson`).
- **Variation index:** `--index variations` makes a sideline-only position findable; `--index mainline` does not.
- **Schema/JSONL contract (theme F):** every emitted row carries its `schema` field; `db find --jsonl` rows parse and contain the documented keys.
- **Workbench mirror:** extend `WorkbenchCommandRegression` so the Database view's command preview resolves to a runnable `crtk db` path.

#### Docs plan

- **New** `wiki/database.md` (or `wiki/pgn-database.md`): the `crtk db` area, store layout, position-key semantics, duplicate rules, provenance, Chess960 notes, determinism guarantees.
- **New** `chess/db/SCHEMA.md`: the three schemas (game/posindex/manifest) ŌĆö the canonical, source-wins contract (mirroring the `tag/SCHEMA.md` convention).
- **Edit** [`wiki/command-reference.md`](wiki/command-reference.md): add the `db` area table.
- **Edit** [`wiki/ai-agents.md`](wiki/ai-agents.md): `db find --jsonl` row contract + exit codes (this is exactly the "agent should never guess" surface).
- **Edit** [`wiki/use-cases.md`](wiki/use-cases.md): a "manage my own games" persona recipe.
- **Edit** [`wiki/workbench.md`](wiki/workbench.md): the Database view (and fix the already-stale tab list while there).

#### Risks / tradeoffs

- **Concurrency.** [`Writer.appendJsonObjects`](src/chess/io/Writer.java#L65) is a single-writer seek-and-rewrite-trailing-bracket scheme; the digest already flags it as not concurrency-safe. For JSONL shards we should append **line-at-a-time with no trailing bracket** (plain `\n`-terminated appends, not a JSON array), which is safer and removes the bracket-rewrite hazard entirely. Decision: DB shards are **JSONL (line-delimited), not JSON arrays**, precisely to avoid `Writer`'s fragility. Single-writer is still assumed; document it.
- **No real Zobrist ŌåÆ collision risk** at very large scale; mitigated by sig+key double-check, but a known ceiling (see hashing above).
- **Storing full `pgn` per row inflates the store** vs. reconstructing from the node tree. Accepted for lossless round-trip and to dodge `toPgn` formatting drift; revisit if store size becomes a problem (a `--no-blob` mode could reconstruct on `show`).
- **Duplicate detection is exact-mainline only** ŌĆö not fuzzy. Documented limit, not a bug.
- **Scope creep magnet.** A "ChessBase-lite" can balloon into opening trees, repertoire matching, and stats dashboards. Keep A to *store + index + query + provenance + dedupe*; opening-tree/repertoire is **D** (depends on A), review routing is **C** (depends on A). Enforce the boundary in the issue set.
- **PGN `SetUp` / Chess960 import policy.** Status 2026-06-16: focused
  regressions now cover explicit `SetUp "0"` ignoring stray FEN tags,
  FEN-without-SetUp as a documented compatibility import path, and
  Variant-tagged Chess960 X-FEN normalization. The remaining risk is scale:
  run broader real-world import trials before declaring A ready for broad
  imports.

#### Acceptance criteria (checkable)

1. `crtk db import games.pgn` creates `dump/db/` with sharded JSONL game rows + a JSONL position index; exit 0; imported/dropped counts printed.
2. Re-running the same import with `--dedupe` adds **0** games (idempotent by `gameId`); without `--dedupe` and with a duplicate present, `db dedupe --apply` reduces the count and `db stats` confirms.
3. Two fresh imports of the same fixture (with `importedAt` injected/fixed) produce **byte-identical** shard and index files.
4. `crtk db find --fen <FEN>` returns exactly the games whose indexed line reaches that position, counter-insensitive to move counters; `--jsonl` rows carry the `crtk.db.posindex`/game contract and a `schema` field.
5. `crtk db show <id> --format pgn` byte-equals the canonical PGN of the imported game (lossless round-trip incl. variations/comments/NAGs).
6. A Chess960 game imports with `chess960:true`, is position-findable, and is **not** auto-ECO-tagged.
7. `crtk db sources` reports each import file with a stable sha256 and game count.
8. `--on-error fail` aborts with nonzero exit and names the bad game; `--on-error skip` imports the rest and reports the dropped count ŌĆö **no silent loss**.
9. `DbStoreRegressionTest` is referenced by `scripts/run_regression_suite.sh` (cli/core target) and passes; the Workbench Database view's command preview resolves to a runnable `crtk db` path under `WorkbenchCommandRegression`.
10. The build still compiles with `javac --release 17` and **zero new third-party dependencies**.

#### Future expansion

- **Theme C (review-to-study router):** `db analyze` + the dynamic game-analysis tag layers ([`GameAnalyzer`](src/chess/tag/game/GameAnalyzer.java)) read the store and emit `.record` study units.
- **Theme D (repertoire/SRS):** opening-tree API over the position index + an [`Encyclopedia`](src/chess/eco/Encyclopedia.java) line-continuation extension; SRS card identity keyed on `signatureCore`.
- **Theme B (read-only import):** `db import` of a user-supplied lichess/chess.com PGN *export file* is already covered; a *fetch* front-end is a thin, boundary-gated, P3 add-on that reduces to "download a PGN, then `db import`."
- **Theme E (local API/SDK):** a localhost `db find`/`db show` JSON-RPC endpoint once F's catalog exists ŌĆö strictly local analysis, never play/sync.
- **Real incremental Zobrist** as a separate core initiative if A ever needs to back a shared/multi-million-position corpus (would replace the FNV+key-verify mitigation).

---

### 8B. Platform import / sync (Lichess, Chess.com, folders)

> **Verdict: defer ┬Ę Priority P3 ┬Ę Complexity medium ┬Ę Depends on A (local PGN database).**
> This is the theme that sits closest to the hard product boundary. It is worth building *only* as read-only, on-demand ingestion of games into the local store from initiative A. Everything that looks like account linking, continuous bidirectional sync, matchmaking, presence, or social features is explicitly out of scope and would violate the stated boundary ("CRTK must NOT become an online play / matchmaking / social / anti-cheat / cloud-credit platform"). Scoped this way, the theme reduces almost entirely to "fetch a PGN export, then run initiative A's `pgn import`."

#### Goal

Let a user pull their own (or any public) games into the local CRTK game store without leaving the toolkit, so the rest of the study/review/dataset pipeline (initiatives A, C, I) has real games to operate on. The networked part is a thin, optional fetch front-end; the durable value lives in initiative A's store and is identical whether games arrive by file or by API.

#### User story

- "I played 40 blitz games on Lichess last night. I run `crtk import lichess --user lenni --since 2026-06-14 --output games/` and they land in my local store, deduped, with provenance, ready for `crtk pgn query` / game review."
- "My club emails me a folder of `.pgn` files. `crtk import folder ./club-pgns --recursive` ingests all of them in one pass with a per-file report of how many games parsed and how many were duplicates."
- "I want last week's new games only, on a schedule, without re-downloading everything. `crtk sync lichess --user lenni` remembers the last imported game and fetches only newer ones."

#### Non-goals (boundary-critical ŌĆö these are forbidden, not just deferred)

- **No account linking / OAuth-for-play, no posting moves, no matchmaking, no challenge/seek, no chat, no presence, no follow/social graph.** Read-only game retrieval only.
- **No anti-cheat, no cloud credits, no server-side compute.** All analysis stays local via the existing in-house engine and external-UCI path.
- **No continuous background daemon as a core deliverable.** A `watch`/`sync` convenience is allowed but must be a thin loop over the same one-shot import path; it must never hold a live socket or stream game events in real time (that drifts toward broadcast/OTB, theme N, which is rejected).
- **No bundling of platform PGN dumps or credentials in the repo.**
- **No write-back to platforms.** CRTK never mutates a Lichess/Chess.com account.

#### MVP (smallest shippable)

`crtk import folder` only. This is pure local file ingestion ŌĆö *zero networking* ŌĆö and it is the 80% case: most users can already export their games as a `.pgn` from any platform's web UI. It is a direct, thin wrapper over initiative A's importer:

1. Walk a file/dir (`--recursive`) for `*.pgn`.
2. Parse each with the existing [`Pgn.parseGames(String)`](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java) / [`Pgn.read(Path)`](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java).
3. Hand each `Game` to initiative A's `pgn import`/store (dedupe by game-id + start/position signature).
4. Emit a per-file JSONL report: `{file, games_parsed, imported, duplicates, malformed}`.

If initiative A ships `crtk pgn import`, then `crtk import folder` is a ~150-line alias that adds the multi-file/recursive walk and the report shape. **The MVP has no new dependency and no network code at all.**

#### Full version

Add `lichess` and `chesscom` source adapters behind one shared `GameSource` seam, plus a `sync` mode that persists a per-source cursor for incremental re-import. Both adapters fetch a **PGN export** (both platforms expose public read-only PGN/NDJSON export endpoints for a user's games) and feed the identical parseŌåÆstore path as `folder`. No platform-specific game model ŌĆö everything normalizes to `chess.struct.Game` immediately after fetch.

#### Proposed CLI surface (noun-then-verb)

New area `import` and convenience verb `sync`. All three import verbs converge on the same parseŌåÆstore path; engine budgets appear only when import is asked to *also* analyze on ingest (off by default ŌĆö import must stay fast and deterministic).

```
crtk import folder <path>
    [--recursive]                      # descend subdirectories
    [--output/-o <store-dir>]          # initiative-A store root (default: config 'output')
    [--dedupe on|off]                  # default on; keys on game-id + signatureCore
    [--max-games N]                    # cap intake (bounded work)
    [--on-malformed skip|fail]         # default skip; 'fail' for strict pipelines
    [--report jsonl|summary]           # per-file ingest report
    [--analyze]                        # optional: tag/analyze on ingest (see budgets below)
    [--quiet] [-v/--verbose]

crtk import lichess
    --user <handle>                    # required; the account whose games to fetch
    [--since <ISO-date|epoch-ms>]      # only games after this time
    [--until <ISO-date|epoch-ms>]
    [--max-games N]                    # default 100; hard cap on intake
    [--rated | --casual]              # filter (passed through as query params)
    [--perf blitz,rapid,classical,...] # platform time-control filter
    [--token-env CRTK_LICHESS_TOKEN]   # name of env var holding a read-only token (optional)
    [--output/-o <store-dir>]
    [--dedupe on|off] [--report jsonl|summary]
    [--retries N] [--retry-backoff-ms MS] [--rate-limit-rps R] [--timeout-ms MS]
    [--cache <dir>]                    # cache raw PGN responses for reproducible re-import
    [--analyze] [--quiet] [-v]

crtk import chesscom
    --user <handle>                    # required
    [--month YYYY-MM | --since/--until]# chess.com archives are month-bucketed
    [--max-games N] [--output/-o] [--dedupe] [--report]
    [--retries] [--retry-backoff-ms] [--rate-limit-rps] [--timeout-ms]
    [--cache <dir>] [--analyze] [--quiet] [-v]
    # NOTE: chess.com's public archive API is unauthenticated/read-only; no token flag.

crtk sync lichess  --user <handle> [all the import lichess flags] [--state <file>]
crtk sync chesscom --user <handle> [all the import chesscom flags] [--state <file>]
    # 'sync' == 'import' that reads/writes a cursor file and fetches only games newer
    # than the last-imported timestamp/id. Idempotent: re-running with no new games is a no-op.

crtk sync watch <source> --user <handle> [--interval 15m] [...same flags]
    # thin convenience loop: sleep, then run 'sync <source>' once, repeat. NOT a streaming
    # connection. Bounded by --max-games per pass. Documented as a politeness-throttled poller.
```

**Engine budgets** are relevant only under `--analyze`, and they reuse the exact existing flag vocabulary so import never invents its own engine surface:

```
crtk import folder ./pgns --analyze \
    --protocol-path/-P <engine.toml> \
    --max-nodes N --max-duration <Ns> --multipv N --threads N --hash N --wdl/--no-wdl
```

`--analyze` should be documented as "delegates to the same per-position analysis as `engine analyze`/`puzzle mine`, with the same `--max-nodes`/`--max-duration` bounds," not as a new analysis path. Default import does **not** analyze (keeps ingest deterministic and offline-capable).

#### Proposed Workbench surface (mirrors CLI, no second implementation)

- A **"Import games" action** in the command palette and on the Dashboard, opening a small form: source (folder / Lichess / Chess.com), user/path, since/until, max-games, output store, dedupe toggle. The form builds the exact `crtk import ŌĆ”` command and runs it through the existing child-JVM [`CommandRunner`](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java), exactly like every other Workbench command. No in-process HTTP in the GUI ŌĆö the GUI shells the CLI so there is one code path.
- The existing [`PgnExplorerDialog`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerDialog.java) / [`PgnExplorerModel`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java) become the natural landing surface after import: once games are in the store, the explorer (index/filter/position-lookup, already built) is the read view. Import is the producer; PgnExplorer is the consumer. This is the productization win ŌĆö import gives the already-built explorer real data.
- Mirror enforcement: add the import templates to `CommandTemplates` and let [`WorkbenchCommandRegression`](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java) assert the "All CLI" template covers `import folder/lichess/chesscom` and `sync`, the same way it covers every other runnable leaf today.

#### Data model / schema implications (concrete fields)

Import does not define a new on-disk format ŌĆö it writes initiative A's store rows. But it **requires** A's `Game`/store row to carry provenance fields that [`Record.java`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) does not have today (the digest confirms Record has only `created/engine/parent/position/description/tags/analysis` and **no game id, no source, no schema version**). Import is the concrete forcing function for these A-owned fields:

- `game_id` ŌĆö stable identity. For platform games, prefer the platform's own id (Lichess game id; Chess.com game URL/UUID) so re-import is idempotent. For folder PGN with no id, derive a deterministic id from a digest of normalized tags + start position [`signatureCore()`](src/chess/core/Position.java) + mainline UCI moves.
- `source` ŌĆö `{kind: "lichess"|"chesscom"|"folder"|"pgn", handle?, endpoint?, fetched_at_epoch_ms, query?}`. This is the provenance block. Folder imports record the absolute source path.
- `import_run_id` ŌĆö ties a batch of games to one `crtk import` invocation (parallels [`RunManifest`](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java) v1's per-run provenance, which already does SHA-256 input/output stamping ŌĆö reuse that pattern).
- `pgn_tags` ŌĆö the full original tag map from `Game.getTags()` preserved verbatim (Event/Site/Date/White/Black/Result/WhiteElo/BlackElo/TimeControl/ECO/etc.) so nothing is lost on import.
- `schema_version` ŌĆö owned by initiative F; import must write whatever F mandates.

A **dedupe key** = `game_id` (when authoritative) else `(start signatureCore, full mainline move sequence hash)`. A **sync cursor** persisted as a tiny JSON state file: `{schema, source, handle, last_game_id, last_played_epoch_ms, last_import_run_id}`.

#### Architecture implications (respect plain javac / no third-party deps; isolate the optional dep)

- **`crtk import folder` introduces no dependency.** It is plain file I/O + existing parsers.
- **`lichess`/`chesscom` need an HTTP client. Use `java.net.http.HttpClient` (JDK 11+, in the standard library).** This is **not** a third-party dependency ŌĆö it is part of the JDK that `javac --release 17` already targets, so it preserves the "no Maven/Gradle, no third-party Java deps, plain javac --release 17" value verbatim. **Answer to the posed question: yes, `java.net.http` is acceptable in core because it is JDK-bundled; it adds nothing to the classpath.** Do **not** pull in OkHttp/Apache HttpClient/Retrofit/Gson ŌĆö they would break the no-deps invariant for zero benefit here.
- **Isolate all networking in one optional package**, e.g. `chess.platform` (or `application.platform`), with a single `GameSource` interface:
  ```
  interface GameSource { Stream<chess.struct.Game> fetch(FetchRequest req) throws IOException; }
  ```
  `FolderSource` (no net), `LichessSource` (HttpClient), `ChesscomSource` (HttpClient). The shared chess core (`chess.core`, `chess.struct`, `chess.io`) **must not import** this package ŌĆö only the CLI command layer and the new package do. This keeps the per-area import bans in [`SourceHeaderRegressionTest`](src/testing/SourceHeaderRegressionTest.java) satisfiable (the network code stays out of `chess.core`/`chess.struct`).
- **Offline build/CI must stay green.** Networked adapters compile against JDK classes only; CI never hits the network. The platform-adapter tests run against a **local fixture HTTP server** (the same pattern UCI tests already use ŌĆö see below), so `core`/`ci` suites stay hermetic.

##### rate-limit / retry / backoff representation

Represent as explicit, bounded, deterministic parameters on the request (no hidden defaults that vary by run):

- `--rate-limit-rps R` ŌåÆ a simple token-bucket / minimum-inter-request-sleep computed from `R` (e.g. one request per `1000/R` ms). Default conservative (e.g. 1 rps) to be a polite client.
- `--retries N` (default 3) + `--retry-backoff-ms MS` (default 1000) ŌåÆ exponential backoff with a cap: `delay = min(MS * 2^attempt, ceiling)`. Retry only on transient classes (timeouts, HTTP 429, 5xx). Never retry on 4xx-other (bad user ŌåÆ fail fast with a clear message).
- On HTTP 429, honor a `Retry-After` header if present; otherwise use the backoff schedule.
- Surface every retry on **stderr** (diagnostics), never stdout (which carries data) ŌĆö consistent with the documented "stdout=data / stderr=diagnostics" contract.

##### caching

`--cache <dir>` stores the **raw fetched PGN/NDJSON response bodies** keyed by a digest of `(source, handle, query, page)`. Two purposes: (1) avoid re-downloading on a retry/re-run; (2) **reproducible re-import** ŌĆö a cached corpus replays byte-identically with no network. A cache hit must produce exactly the same store rows as the original fetch (the only non-reproducible field is `fetched_at_epoch_ms`, which should be recorded as the *original* fetch time when replaying from cache).

##### reproducible re-import

Import is deterministic *given the input bytes*: same PGN text + same flags ŌåÆ same store rows (dedupe is signature-keyed, parsing is deterministic). The only nondeterminism is the network itself, which `--cache` removes. Document this explicitly the way `wiki/mining.md` documents mining determinism ("capture the inputs and it reproduces"). The `import_run_id`/`fetched_at` fields are provenance, not part of the dedupe key, so they do not break re-import idempotence.

##### token handling

- Tokens are **read-only** and **optional**. Lichess game export of public games does not require a token; a token only raises rate limits / accesses a user's own private games. Chess.com's public archive API needs none.
- **Never accept a token as a CLI argument** (it would leak into shell history / process listings / `RunManifest`). Accept only `--token-env <VARNAME>` naming an environment variable the user sets, defaulting to `CRTK_LICHESS_TOKEN`. The token is read from the env at runtime, sent only as an `Authorization: Bearer` header, and **must never** be written to any store row, cache file, report, log, or RunManifest. Add a regression that asserts no flag/field carries a literal token.
- `crtk doctor` should report token presence as a boolean only ("Lichess token: set / not set"), never the value.

#### Existing components to reuse (real files)

- [`Pgn.parseGames(String)`](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java) / [`Pgn.parseGame(String)`](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java) ŌĆö parse an HTTP response body or file block straight into `Game`. The string-input overload is exactly what an HTTP body needs (confirmed present at lines 162/182).
- [`Pgn.read(Path, LongConsumer)`](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java) ŌĆö folder ingestion with byte-progress for a progress bar.
- [`Game`](src/chess/struct/Game.java) ŌĆö the normalized in-memory model; tags map, start position, mainline/variation tree, result. All sources converge here.
- [`Reader.readJsonFile`](src/chess/io/Reader.java) + [`Json.streamTopLevelObjects`](src/utility/Json.java) ŌĆö tolerant re-read of the store for dedupe lookups and sync-cursor checks.
- [`Writer.appendJsonObjects`](src/chess/io/Writer.java) ŌĆö append-safe write into A's store (single top-level JSON array via seek/bracket-rewrite). Reuse, but see the concurrency risk below.
- [`PgnExplorerModel`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java) / [`PgnExplorerDialog`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerDialog.java) ŌĆö the read/query surface that import feeds.
- [`RunManifest`](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java) (schema `crtk.workbench.run-manifest.v1`) ŌĆö the SHA-256 provenance pattern to mirror for `import_run_id`.
- [`CommandRunner`](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java) ŌĆö child-JVM execution so the Workbench import form reuses the CLI with no second implementation.
- [`CliCommand.group(...)`](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) ŌĆö how to register the new `import` area and `sync` verb (same pattern as the existing 10 groups at lines 199ŌĆō768).
- For `--analyze`: [`chess.uci.Engine`](src/chess/uci/Engine.java) + [`application.Pool`](src/application/Pool.java) ŌĆö the existing external-UCI orchestration; do not write a new analysis path.

#### Files / packages likely affected (real paths)

- **New:** `src/chess/platform/GameSource.java`, `FolderSource.java`, `LichessSource.java`, `ChesscomSource.java`, `FetchRequest.java`, `SyncCursor.java` (or `application.platform` ŌĆö keep out of `chess.core`/`chess.struct`).
- **New CLI handlers:** `src/application/cli/command/ImportCommand.java`, `SyncCommand.java` (mirroring the structure of existing command handlers).
- **Edited:** [`src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java`](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) ŌĆö register `import` group (`folder`/`lichess`/`chesscom`) + `sync` (`lichess`/`chesscom`/`watch`).
- **Edited:** [`src/application/cli/Constants.java`](src/application/cli/Constants.java) ŌĆö new option constants (`--user`, `--since`, `--token-env`, `--rate-limit-rps`, `--retries`, `--retry-backoff-ms`, `--cache`, `--state`, `--dedupe`, `--on-malformed`).
- **Edited (A-owned, import forces them):** [`src/chess/struct/Record.java`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) provenance/game-id/schema-version fields (coordinate with initiatives A and F).
- **Workbench:** `src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java` (import/sync templates); a small import form panel wired through `CommandRunner`.
- **Config:** [`src/application/Config.java`](src/application/Config.java) ŌĆö optional default cache dir, default `--token-env` name; [`src/application/cli/command/DoctorCommand.java`](src/application/cli/command/DoctorCommand.java) ŌĆö token-present boolean + reachability note.

#### Testing plan (in-house harness style ŌĆö `public static void main`, `testing.TestSupport` asserts)

- **`ImportFolderRegressionTest`** ŌĆö point `import folder` at a `testdata/import/` fixture dir of small `.pgn` files (incl. one malformed game block); assert games imported, duplicates detected on a deliberate repeat file, `--on-malformed skip` vs `fail` behavior, and JSONL report shape. No network.
- **`ImportDedupeRegressionTest`** ŌĆö import the same game twice (once via folder, once via a cached "platform" fixture); assert exactly one store row and a stable derived `game_id`.
- **`PlatformSourceRegressionTest`** ŌĆö drive `LichessSource`/`ChesscomSource` against a **local fixture HTTP server** bound to `127.0.0.1:0` (a tiny `com.sun.net.httpserver.HttpServer`, JDK-bundled) serving canned PGN/NDJSON + canned 429/`Retry-After` and 5xx responses. Assert: correct request URL/params, retry-on-429/5xx with backoff (use injected/virtual time so the test is fast and deterministic), no-retry-on-404, token sent only as a header and only when the env var is set, and that the parsed games equal the fixture. This mirrors the existing UCI approach of testing protocol behavior against a generated fake engine + `commands.log` ([`UCIRegressionTest`](src/testing/UCIRegressionTest.java)) ŌĆö same "fake the external dependency locally, assert the wire behavior" discipline.
- **`SyncCursorRegressionTest`** ŌĆö first sync imports N; second sync against a fixture with no newer games is a no-op; a fixture with one newer game imports exactly one; cursor file round-trips.
- **`ReproducibleImportRegressionTest`** ŌĆö run a cached import twice; assert byte-identical store rows except provenance timestamps; assert a token literal appears in no output artifact.
- **Wire these into the runner** (the digest flags that several ML tests rot precisely because they are *not* wired): add `import` cases to the `cli` suite in [`scripts/run_regression_suite.sh`](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh) and let [`WorkbenchCommandRegression`](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java) cover the new templates. The hermetic fixture-server tests run in `core`/`ci` with no network.

#### Docs plan

- **New:** `wiki/import-and-sync.md` ŌĆö the boundary statement (read-only, no play/social), the folder MVP, platform adapters, token handling (env-only), rate-limit/backoff/cache/reproducibility, and the precise output contracts. Lead with the boundary so expectations are set.
- **Edit:** `wiki/use-cases.md` ŌĆö add an "import my games then review them" recipe chaining `import` ŌåÆ A's `pgn query` ŌåÆ C's review.
- **Edit:** `wiki/ai-agents.md` ŌĆö add `import folder/lichess/chesscom` and `sync` to the commandŌåÆcontract table with their JSONL report shapes.
- **Edit:** `wiki/configuration.md` ŌĆö document `CRTK_LICHESS_TOKEN`, default cache dir, `rate-limit-rps`/retry defaults.
- **Edit:** `wiki/faq.md` ŌĆö "Does CRTK connect to my account?" answered explicitly: read-only game export only, never play/post, token optional and env-only.

#### Risks / tradeoffs

- **Boundary creep is the dominant risk.** Each adapter is a small temptation toward "just add a challenge button / live game stream / account dashboard." Mitigate by encoding the boundary in the `GameSource` interface (it can only *fetch games*, returns `Stream<Game>`, no write/play/stream methods exist) and by a `wiki` non-goals section that reviewers can point at.
- **External-service fragility.** Platform endpoints, rate limits, and PGN/NDJSON formats change; CI must never depend on them (hence fixture-server tests). Adapters should degrade gracefully: a fetch failure must not corrupt the store (write only after successful parse), and partial pulls must be resumable via the sync cursor.
- **`Writer.appendJsonObjects` is single-writer / not concurrency-safe** (digest risk) and assumes a well-formed trailing `]`. `import --analyze` with a parallel `Pool` or a `watch` loop racing a manual import could corrupt the array. Mitigate: serialize all store writes through one writer; or, better, push initiative A toward a JSONL store (append-only newline rows) which sidesteps the bracket-rewrite hazard entirely. **Flag this to initiative A as a store-format decision.**
- **`watch`/`sync` could be misread as "always-on sync."** Document it as a politeness-throttled poller that runs one bounded `sync` per interval; never a streaming connection. If users want real-time, the honest answer is "no" (that is broadcast/OTB, rejected theme N).
- **Token leakage.** Mitigated by env-only tokens + a regression asserting no literal token in any artifact, but it must be tested, not assumed.
- **Tradeoff: folder MVP alone covers most users.** The platform adapters add network code, retry/cache complexity, and ongoing maintenance for a convenience over "export PGN from the web UI, then `import folder`." This is precisely why the theme is **P3/defer**: ship `folder` cheaply with A, evaluate demand before building `lichess`/`chesscom`.

#### Acceptance criteria (checkable)

- [ ] `crtk import folder ./testdata/import --recursive` imports all parseable games, reports counts as JSONL, and is a no-op on a second run (full dedupe).
- [ ] No third-party JAR appears on the classpath; `core` and `ci` suites pass with the machine offline (fixture-server tests only).
- [ ] `chess.core` / `chess.struct` do not import the new platform package (verified by [`SourceHeaderRegressionTest`](src/testing/SourceHeaderRegressionTest.java) bans).
- [ ] `crtk import lichess --user X` against the fixture server: retries 429/5xx with bounded backoff, fails fast on 404, honors `--rate-limit-rps`, and sends a token only when the named env var is set.
- [ ] No store row, cache file, report, log, or RunManifest contains a literal token value (asserted by `ReproducibleImportRegressionTest`).
- [ ] `crtk sync lichess --user X` run twice with no new games produces zero new rows; the cursor file round-trips.
- [ ] Cached re-import produces byte-identical store rows except `fetched_at`/`import_run_id`.
- [ ] Every store row written by import carries `game_id`, `source`, `import_run_id`, full original `pgn_tags`, and the `schema_version` mandated by initiative F.
- [ ] Workbench "Import games" form builds a command string identical to the documented CLI and runs it via `CommandRunner` (no second impl); [`WorkbenchCommandRegression`](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java) covers the new leaves.
- [ ] `wiki/import-and-sync.md` exists and leads with the read-only / no-play boundary.

#### Sequencing, priority, complexity, dependencies

- **Short-term:** ship `import folder` *with* initiative A (it is a thin alias over A's `pgn import`; near-zero marginal cost, zero network). Reconcile the provenance/game-id fields with A and F.
- **Medium-term:** add `lichess`/`chesscom` adapters + `sync` cursor behind the `GameSource` seam, fixture-server tests, token-env handling, cache.
- **Long-term:** `sync watch` polling convenience; richer platform filters; optional `--analyze`-on-ingest wired to the existing `Pool`/external-UCI path.
- **Priority:** P3 (the folder slice is effectively P1-cheap riding on A; the networked adapters are P3 and demand-gated).
- **Complexity:** medium overall ŌĆö `folder` is small, each platform adapter is small/medium, `sync`/`watch`/cache add the medium weight.
- **Dependencies:** **A (local PGN database)** is a hard prerequisite ŌĆö import has nowhere to put games without A's store and its game-id/provenance fields. **F (schemas/validation)** owns `schema_version` and the store row contract import must honor. Feeds **C (game-review-to-study router)** and **I (dataset provenance)** by supplying real, provenanced games. No dependency on E/G/D.

#### Future expansion (in-boundary only)

- Additional read-only sources behind the same `GameSource` interface: a local Lichess/SCID database dump, an EPD/EPD-list importer, a study/`.pgn` URL fetch.
- An incremental "new games since last sync" report that hands deltas straight to C's review router (auto-surface the games you just played for mistake review).
- Provenance-aware dataset export: because every imported game carries `source` + `import_run_id`, initiative I can stamp dataset manifests with exactly which games (and which fetch) produced them ŌĆö closing the reproducibility gap the digest flags for the ML pillar.

---

### 8C. Game review & study router

**Priority:** P1 ┬Ę **Complexity:** large ┬Ę **Horizon:** medium-term
**Depends on:** A (local PGN database ŌĆö supplies game ids, provenance, and the on-disk store the router reads from and writes study units back into) and F (schemas/validation ŌĆö supplies the `schemaVersion` field and the published JSON Schema for the review/study-unit rows). Soft-couples to G (grounded explanations ŌĆö a future consumer of the structured review output) and I (dataset provenance ŌĆö the reproducibility-metadata block is the same stamp).

This is the single biggest *missing connective tissue* in the toolkit. Every primitive a review router needs already exists and is real on disk; nothing wires them into a "give me a game, get back what to study" flow. The router is the verb that turns analysis into study units.

---

#### Goal

Take a played game (a PGN, or a game already in the local store from initiative A), find the moves where a side went materially wrong, and emit two grounded artifacts: (1) a per-ply **review JSONL** stream (one row per analyzed ply with the engine verdict, cp/WDL loss, mistake category, severity, and the grounded tag delta), and (2) a set of **study units** ŌĆö puzzle [`Record`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) objects whose `parent` is the position the human faced and whose `position` is the refutation/best continuation, so the study material is literally "you played X here; the punishment was Y."

The mining pipeline ([`MineCommand`](src/application/cli/command/MineCommand.java)) already turns a FEN into a puzzle. The review router is the piece that decides *which* FENs from a real game are worth turning into puzzles, and frames them as the player's own mistakes rather than abstract positions.

#### User story

> "I exported my five rapid games from last night as a PGN. I run `crtk review game --pgn last-night.pgn`. crtk tells me I had one blunder (move 23, hung a rook), two mistakes, and four inaccuracies across the five games, classified and rated. It writes a `.review.jsonl` I can scan, and a `.puzzles.json` of my own mistakes I can drill or publish as a study book. The verdicts came from my configured Stockfish at a fixed node budget, and the row tells me exactly which engine and budget produced each call so I can reproduce it."

#### Non-goals

- **Not** an accuracy/ACPL percentage scoreboard mimicking lichess/chess.com "game review" gamification. We emit cp loss and categories; a single "accuracy %" headline can be a derived convenience field but is not the product.
- **Not** an online importer. Input is a local PGN file or a game already stored by initiative A. Fetching games from a platform account is initiative B and is explicitly downstream/boundary-gated.
- **Not** a new search engine. All reference-grade verdicts route through an external UCI engine via [`chess.uci.Engine`](src/chess/uci/Engine.java); the in-house [`AlphaBeta`](src/chess/engine/AlphaBeta.java) is a fallback for offline determinism, never the default for grading.
- **Not** a coaching narrator. The router emits *structured* review rows and *grounded tag deltas*; turning those into prose is initiative G consuming this output. We must not let the router grow an ungrounded English-explanation layer.
- **Not** a repertoire/SRS scheduler (initiative D). We emit study units; scheduling them for review is D's job.

---

#### MVP (smallest shippable)

`crtk review game --pgn <file>` that:

1. Parses the PGN via [`Pgn`](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java) ŌåÆ [`Game`](src/chess/struct/Game.java).
2. For each ply of each game's mainline, sends the *pre-move* position to the configured external engine via [`chess.uci.Engine.analyse`](src/chess/uci/Engine.java) (or the [`Pool`](src/application/Pool.java) for parallelism) at an explicit node/time budget, capturing the best move + eval, then evaluates the position *after the played move* (one more bounded analyse, or reuse the next ply's pre-move analysis ŌĆö see "deterministic vs engine-dependent").
3. Computes cp loss and (when the engine reports WDL) WDL loss from the *moving side's* perspective.
4. Classifies each ply into `ok | inaccuracy | mistake | blunder` using thresholds (below), with the "only-move" and "already-lost/already-winning" guards that stop every engine diff being called a mistake.
5. Writes one review JSONL row per ply (full schema below) to `<stem>.review.jsonl`.
6. With `--to-study`, writes `<stem>.study.jsonl` study-unit rows plus `<stem>.study.record.json` [`Record`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) objects for plies classified `mistake`/`blunder` (parent = pre-move FEN, position = post-best-move FEN, description = "you played <san>, best was <san>", tags = grounded mistake tags plus `META:` linkage).

MVP uses the *engine's own analysis at each ply* ŌĆö no whole-game tag layer yet, no Workbench. It is shippable and useful on its own and exercises the full [`Engine`](src/chess/uci/Engine.java) ŌåÆ [`Record`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) ŌåÆ mining-handoff path.

#### Full version

- Attaches the grounded **tag delta** per mistake by running [`chess.tag.Generator.tags`](src/chess/tag/Generator.java) on the pre- and post-move positions and diffing via [`chess.tag.Delta`](src/chess/tag/Delta.java) / [`chess.tag.Identity`](src/chess/tag/Identity.java) ŌĆö so a blunder row carries `tags_added: ["THREAT: type=mate ...", "TACTIC: motif=hanging ..."]` derived without trusting the engine's prose.
- Runs the whole-game structured layer [`chess.tag.game.GameAnalyzer.analyze(Game)`](src/chess/tag/game/GameAnalyzer.java) once per game to attach `GAME:` phase/opening/result-cause context and `LINE:`/`VARIATION:` motif tags to the review, giving each mistake a phase (opening/middlegame/endgame) and ECO label for free.
- `crtk review batch` over a directory of PGNs or over the initiative-A store.
- `--to-study` flag that writes study units directly into the A store as linked records (game id ŌåÆ ply ŌåÆ puzzle) rather than a loose `.puzzles.json`.
- ECO tagging: pull `meta:eco`/`meta:opening` from the tagger's [`Opening`](src/chess/tag/position/Opening.java) output (skipped for Chess960, per that class) into the row.
- `--severity-min` to filter which mistakes become study units.
- "Recommended action" enrichment: tactic-shaped mistakes ŌåÆ drill puzzle; opening-phase mistakes ŌåÆ repertoire note (a hook for initiative D); strategic mistakes ŌåÆ describe-position study (a hook for initiative G).

---

#### Proposed CLI surface

Noun-then-verb under a new `review` area. Engine budgets are explicit and mirror the existing external-engine option block in [`EngineSupport`](src/application/cli/command/EngineSupport.java) (`--protocol-path/-P`, `--max-nodes`, `--max-duration`, `--multipv`, `--threads`, `--hash`, `--wdl/--no-wdl`).

```
crtk review game
    --pgn <file>                 # input PGN (one or many games)
    --input/-i <file>            # OR a game id / .record from the initiative-A store
    --game <id>                  # select one game from a multi-game input
    --color white|black|both     # which side's mistakes to review (default both)
    -o/--output <stem>           # default dump/<input-stem>.review.jsonl
    --to-study                   # also write <stem>.study.jsonl and <stem>.study.record.json
    --study-output <file>         # override study JSONL output
    --record-output <file>        # override Record JSON output
    --severity-min inaccuracy|mistake|blunder   # study-unit gate (default mistake)
    --time-control auto|classical|rapid|blitz   # threshold profile (default auto from PGN tags)
    --inaccuracy-cp <int>        # override threshold (default 50)
    --mistake-cp <int>           # default 120
    --blunder-cp <int>           # default 300
    --wdl-blunder <float>        # WDL-share loss for a blunder (default 0.30)
    --engine-search <best-only|symmetric>   # how the post-move eval is obtained (see below; default best-only)
    # external engine budgets (explicit, bounded):
    -P/--protocol-path <toml>    # default config/default.engine.toml
    --max-nodes <int>            # per-position node cap (default from cli.config.toml)
    --max-duration <dur>         # per-position time cap, e.g. 800ms
    --multipv <int>              # >=2 required for only-move detection (default 2)
    --threads <int> --hash <int>
    --wdl/--no-wdl
    --engine-instances/-E <int>  # parallel engines via Pool (default from config)
    --offline                    # use in-house AlphaBeta instead of external UCI (deterministic, weaker)
    --json | --jsonl             # default jsonl
    -v/--verbose

crtk review batch
    --input/-i <dir-or-glob>     # directory of PGNs or the A store
    --recursive
    --max-records <int>          # cap games processed
    (+ all review game engine/threshold/output flags)

crtk review summary
    --input/-i <file.review.jsonl>   # roll up an existing review into per-game/per-player counts
    --json
```

`review summary` is deliberately a *separate, engine-free* command that operates on an already-produced review JSONL, so the expensive engine pass and the cheap roll-up are decoupled (same separation [`RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand`](src/application/cli/command/RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java) uses today ŌĆö it reads stored analysis and emits a derived JSONL without re-running the engine).

#### Proposed Workbench surface

The Workbench mirrors the CLI through the existing child-JVM model ŌĆö [`CommandRunner.javaInvocation`](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java) spawns `application.Main` with the current classpath, so there is **no second implementation**. Concretely:

- Add `review game`/`review batch`/`review summary` as command templates in [`CommandTemplates`](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java); the "All CLI" template picks them up automatically from [`CliRegistry`](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) (enforced by [`WorkbenchCommandRegression`](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java)).
- The existing **Review mode** on the Board surface ([`WindowBoardLayer`](src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowBoardLayer.java), board detail tab "Review") and [`GameReviewPanel`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/GameReviewPanel.java) become *consumers* of the produced `.review.jsonl`: load the file, render the per-ply verdict timeline, jump to a mistake, and offer "send to puzzle drill" (which just runs the same `review game --to-study`). The panel must not recompute verdicts in-process; it reads the manifest the CLI produced.
- A "Review this game" action in the command palette / [`PgnExplorerModel`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java) context that builds and runs the `review game` command for the selected game.

This keeps the value preserved: CLI is source of truth, Workbench previews the exact runnable command.

---

#### Data model / schema implications

The review JSONL is a **new contract** and must ship with a published JSON Schema under initiative F. The study-unit output reuses [`Record`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) directly ŌĆö but [`Record`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) today has only 7 fixed fields (`created/engine/parent/position/description/tags/analysis`) and **no game id, ply, or provenance**, so the study units must encode game/ply linkage in `tags` until initiative A extends the Record schema (mark this an explicit ASSUMPTION: review depends on A adding `gameId`/`ply`/`schemaVersion` fields to Record; absent that, we carry them as `META:` tags, which is lossy and stringly-typed).

**Exact review JSONL row schema** (`schemaVersion: "crtk.review.ply.v1"`, one object per analyzed ply):

```jsonc
{
  "schemaVersion": "crtk.review.ply.v1",
  "game_id": "lastnight-0003",          // from A store, or derived hash(PGN tags + movetext) for loose PGNs
  "source": "pgn:last-night.pgn#3",     // provenance of the game
  "event": "Rated Rapid game",          // PGN Event tag (nullable)
  "white": "AxelC", "black": "opponent",// PGN player tags (nullable)
  "eco": "B23", "opening": "Sicilian, Closed",  // from Opening.java tags (null for Chess960)
  "ply": 45,                            // 0-based ply index from start
  "move_number": 23, "color": "white",  // human-readable move number + mover
  "fen": "<pre-move FEN>",              // position the mover faced
  "played_uci": "f1d3", "played_san": "Bd3",
  "best_uci": "g1f3",  "best_san": "Nf3",
  "eval_before": { "cp": 35, "mate": null, "wdl": [520,300,180] },  // best line, mover's perspective
  "eval_after":  { "cp": -210, "mate": null, "wdl": [180,260,560] },// after played move, mover's perspective
  "cp_loss": 245,                       // max(0, eval_before.cp - eval_after.cp), mate-aware
  "wdl_loss": 0.34,                     // win-share drop, mover's perspective (null if engine gave no WDL)
  "pv_best": ["g1f3","b8c6","..."],     // best line PV (uci), capped
  "second_best_cp": 28,                 // multipv 2 eval, for only-move detection (null if multipv<2)
  "is_only_move_position": false,       // best vs 2nd-best gap >= ONLY_MOVE_GAP_CP
  "tags_before": ["FACT: ...","CAND: ..."],   // Generator.tags on pre-move FEN
  "tags_after":  ["THREAT: type=hanging ...","TACTIC: motif=hanging ..."], // on post-played-move FEN
  "tags_delta":  { "added": [...], "removed": [...], "changed": [...] },   // via Delta.diff
  "game_phase": "middlegame",           // from GameAnalyzer GAME: phase, full version only
  "mistake_category": "blunder",        // ok|inaccuracy|mistake|blunder (see classification)
  "mistake_motif": "hanging_piece",     // optional grounded motif from tags_delta (nullable)
  "severity": 0.87,                     // normalized 0..1 (see severity)
  "recommended_action": "drill_puzzle", // drill_puzzle|repertoire_note|describe_study|none
  "study_unit_id": "lastnight-0003.p45",// id of the emitted Record (null if below severity gate)
  "repro": {                            // reproducibility metadata block (shared with initiative I stamp)
    "engine": "Stockfish 16.1",         // Engine name string (falls back to protocol path)
    "protocol_path": "config/default.engine.toml",
    "max_nodes": 800000, "max_duration_ms": 800,
    "multipv": 2, "threads": 1, "hash": 64,
    "search_mode": "best-only",
    "crtk_version": "1.0.0", "deterministic": false
  }
}
```

Notes on fields tied to real code:
- `eval_before`/`eval_after` come from [`Analysis.getBestOutput`](src/chess/uci/Analysis.java) ŌåÆ [`Output.getEvaluation`](src/chess/uci/Output.java) ([`Evaluation`](src/chess/uci/Evaluation.java) carries the mate flag) and WDL from `Output` (parsed via the `wdl` token at [`Output`](src/chess/uci/Output.java) line ~312). `cp_loss` must be mate-aware: a `mate` eval maps to a large sentinel before subtraction, exactly as [`RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand`](src/application/cli/command/RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java) already handles `DELTA_CP`/`DELTA_MATE`/`DELTA_MIXED`.
- `pv_best` from [`Output.getMoves`](src/chess/uci/Output.java).
- `tags_*`/`tags_delta` from [`Generator`](src/chess/tag/Generator.java) + [`Delta`](src/chess/tag/Delta.java) + [`Identity`](src/chess/tag/Identity.java).
- `study_unit_id` references the emitted [`Record`](src/chess/struct/Record.java); the Record's `analysis` field stores the raw engine info lines so the study unit is self-describing.

---

#### Mistake classification, thresholds, and false-positive avoidance

**Classification by cp loss (mover's perspective), with WDL escalation:**

| Category | cp_loss range | WDL escalation |
|---|---|---|
| `ok` | `< inaccuracy-cp` (default 50) | ŌĆö |
| `inaccuracy` | `[50, 120)` | ŌĆö |
| `mistake` | `[120, 300)` | escalate from `inaccuracy` if `wdl_loss >= 0.20` |
| `blunder` | `>= 300` | escalate from `mistake` if `wdl_loss >= 0.30` |

WDL is the *more honest* signal near decisive evals (a +900 ŌåÆ +400 swing is 300cp but changes nothing about the result), so when WDL is present, a row is only a `blunder` if **both** `cp_loss >= blunder-cp` **and** `wdl_loss >= wdl-blunder`. Centipawn-only thresholds are the fallback when the engine reports no WDL (`--no-wdl` or a non-WDL engine).

**Guards that stop every engine diff being called a mistake** (each is a checkable rule, not a heuristic vibe):

1. **Only-move / forced-position suppression.** Require `--multipv >= 2`. If `eval_before.cp - second_best_cp >= ONLY_MOVE_GAP_CP` (the position has one good move and the human found a *different* one, fine), but conversely if the *played* move's loss is below threshold relative to the *spread of reasonable moves*, do not flag. Concretely: a move is never a mistake if it is within `inaccuracy-cp` of best. (`is_only_move_position` is recorded for transparency.)
2. **Already-decided suppression.** If `|eval_before.cp| >= DECIDED_CP` (default 600) and the played move keeps the same result band (WDL win-share stays `>= 0.90` or `<= 0.10`), downgrade by one category. Throwing away half a winning advantage while still winning is not a blunder.
3. **Dead-draw suppression.** If both `eval_before` and `eval_after` are inside `[-DRAW_BAND, +DRAW_BAND]` (default ┬▒30cp) the row is `ok` regardless of raw cp arithmetic.
4. **Theory suppression.** Plies still inside the ECO book (the position has an `Opening` tag from [`chess.tag.position.Opening`](src/chess/tag/position/Opening.java)) are not flagged as mistakes; an "out-of-book" deviation is reported as a neutral `game_phase: opening` note, not a blunder, unless cp_loss is itself blunder-grade.
5. **Engine-noise floor.** With low node budgets, two near-equal moves can flip sign. The `inaccuracy-cp` floor (50) plus requiring WDL agreement for higher categories absorbs this. Document that sub-threshold flapping is expected at small `--max-nodes`.

**Severity** is a normalized `0..1` blend: `0.5 * clamp(cp_loss / blunder_ref) + 0.5 * wdl_loss` (when WDL present; cp-only otherwise), so the study-unit ranking and `--severity-min` gate are comparable across games. Severity is deterministic given the eval inputs.

**Blitz vs classical handling.** `--time-control` selects a threshold profile; `auto` reads the PGN `TimeControl`/`Event` tags (classical/rapid/blitz/bullet) and widens thresholds for faster games (blitz: inaccuracy 80 / mistake 180 / blunder 400) because punishing a 60cp slip in bullet produces noise, not insight. The profile chosen is recorded implicitly via the resolved thresholds; the row stores the absolute thresholds used in `repro` so a reviewer can see why a ply was/wasn't flagged. ASSUMPTION: PGN TimeControl tag parsing is best-effort; absent/unknown ŌåÆ classical profile.

#### Deterministic vs engine-dependent

- **Engine-dependent (not byte-reproducible across engine builds/budgets):** every `eval_*`, `best_*`, `cp_loss`, `wdl_loss`, `pv_best`, and therefore `mistake_category`/`severity`. This is unavoidable ŌĆö verdicts come from an external UCI engine ([`Engine.analyse`](src/chess/uci/Engine.java) issues `go nodes`, per that class) and are reproducible **only** with the same engine binary + protocol + budget. The `repro` block exists precisely so a reviewer can reproduce: it records engine string, protocol path, node/time cap, multipv, threads, hash, and `deterministic:false`.
- **Deterministic given the eval inputs:** `tags_before/after/delta` (from the engine-free [`Generator`](src/chess/tag/Generator.java)), `eco`/`opening`, `game_phase`, the classification *function* (thresholds ŌåÆ category), severity arithmetic, and `recommended_action`. Two reviewers feeding the *same* engine outputs get identical rows.
- The `--offline` path uses [`AlphaBeta`](src/chess/engine/AlphaBeta.java) single-threaded at a fixed depth, which **is** byte-reproducible (`deterministic:true`), at the cost of weaker verdicts. This is the path the regression suite uses so tests do not depend on a Stockfish install.
- **Engine-call count caveat (`--engine-search`):** `best-only` mode reuses the *next* ply's pre-move analysis as `eval_after` (the position after the played move *is* the next pre-move position), halving engine calls but making `eval_after` the opponent-to-move eval inverted. `symmetric` mode runs a dedicated bounded analyse on the post-move position for a cleaner same-side eval at double the cost. Default `best-only`; document the inversion precisely so cp_loss math is auditable.

---

#### Architecture implications

- **Plain javac / no third-party deps preserved.** Everything reuses existing in-repo packages: PGN parse ([`chess.struct.Pgn`](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java)), external engine ([`chess.uci.Engine`](src/chess/uci/Engine.java), [`application.Pool`](src/application/Pool.java)), tagging ([`chess.tag.*`](src/chess/tag/Generator.java)), record output ([`chess.struct.Record`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) + the JSON-array append writer [`chess.io.Writer`](src/chess/io/Writer.java)), JSON emission via [`utility.Json`](src/application/cli/command/RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java) (already imported there). No optional dep is introduced.
- **One shared core respected.** The router never reimplements legality, SAN, or eval; it only orchestrates. Mistake classification is pure arithmetic over engine outputs.
- **CLI is source of truth.** Core logic lands in a new `chess.review` package (engine-free classification + row assembly + study-unit construction) so that both the CLI command and the Workbench panel call the *same* core. The CLI command [`ReviewCommand`](src/application/cli/command/) is a thin orchestrator; classification/severity/category live in `chess.review.Classifier`/`chess.review.ReviewRow` and are unit-testable without an engine.
- **JSON-by-hand risk.** Like [`EngineBatchCommand`](src/application/cli/command/EngineBatchCommand.java), avoid hand-built JSON drift ŌĆö route row emission through a single `ReviewRow.toJson()` using [`utility.Json`](src/application/cli/command/RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java) string helpers, and pin the shape with a golden regression.

#### Existing components to reuse

- [`chess.struct.Pgn`](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java) / [`chess.struct.Game`](src/chess/struct/Game.java) ŌĆö game parse, mainline walk (`getMainline()`, `getStartPosition()`, `getTags()`, `getResult()`).
- [`chess.uci.Engine`](src/chess/uci/Engine.java) (`analyse(Position, Analysis, Filter, nodes, ...)`) + [`application.Pool`](src/application/Pool.java) (`analyseAll`/`analyseEach`) ŌĆö bounded external grading.
- [`chess.uci.Analysis`](src/chess/uci/Analysis.java) / [`Output`](src/chess/uci/Output.java) / [`Evaluation`](src/chess/uci/Evaluation.java) ŌĆö best/2nd-best eval, WDL, PV, mate-awareness.
- [`chess.tag.Generator`](src/chess/tag/Generator.java) + [`chess.tag.Delta`](src/chess/tag/Delta.java) + [`chess.tag.Identity`](src/chess/tag/Identity.java) ŌĆö grounded tag delta per ply.
- [`chess.tag.game.GameAnalyzer`](src/chess/tag/game/GameAnalyzer.java) (`analyze(Game)`) ŌĆö `GAME:`/`LINE:`/`VARIATION:` whole-game context (full version).
- [`chess.tag.position.Opening`](src/chess/tag/position/Opening.java) ŌĆö ECO/opening labels.
- [`chess.struct.Record`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) + [`chess.io.Writer`](src/chess/io/Writer.java) ŌĆö study-unit emission, same as the miner.
- [`application.cli.command.EngineSupport`](src/application/cli/command/EngineSupport.java) (`UciOptions`) ŌĆö the exact external-engine option block to mirror.
- [`application.cli.command.RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand`](src/application/cli/command/RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java) ŌĆö the eval-delta arithmetic pattern (mate-aware cp delta) to lift/share.
- [`application.cli.PathOps`](src/application/cli/command/RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java) (`deriveOutputPath`, `ensureParentDir`) ŌĆö default `dump/` output naming.

#### Files / packages likely affected

- New: `src/chess/review/Classifier.java`, `src/chess/review/ReviewRow.java`, `src/chess/review/StudyUnitFactory.java`, `src/chess/review/package-info.java` (engine-free core).
- New: `src/application/cli/command/ReviewCommand.java` (orchestrator for `review game|batch|summary`).
- Edit: [`src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java`](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) ŌĆö register the `review` group + leaves.
- Edit: [`src/application/cli/Constants.java`](src/application/cli/Constants.java) ŌĆö `CMD_REVIEW*`, threshold option flags.
- Edit: [`src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java`](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java) ŌĆö review templates.
- Edit: [`src/application/gui/workbench/game/GameReviewPanel.java`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/GameReviewPanel.java) ŌĆö consume `.review.jsonl`.
- Schema (initiative F): `crtk.review.ply.v1` JSON Schema file + study-unit Record schema bump.

#### Testing plan (in-house harness style ŌĆö `main()` + `testing.TestSupport`)

- [x] `src/testing/ReviewClassifierRegressionTest.java` ŌĆö pure-function tests of [`Classifier`](src/chess/review): a 300cp/0.4-WDL drop ŌåÆ blunder; a 250cp drop with WDL win-share staying 0.95 ŌåÆ downgraded (already-decided guard); a within-50cp-of-best move ŌåÆ `ok`; a dead-draw pair ŌåÆ `ok`; theory suppression and blitz thresholds are pinned. No engine.
- [x] `src/testing/ReviewCommandRegressionTest.java` ŌĆö drives `application.Main` (via `TestSupport.runMain`/`runMainExpectFailure`) on a fixed PGN with `--offline` (deterministic [`AlphaBeta`](src/chess/engine/AlphaBeta.java)) and with a fake external UCI engine, asserting: exact `.review.jsonl` row count = analyzed plies, the known blunder ply is categorized `blunder`, the row validates as `crtk.review.ply.v1`, grounded `THREAT:`/`TACTIC:` tags survive, external review sends bounded `go nodes`, the `repro` block records protocol/budget metadata, and `--to-study` emits one valid `crtk.review.study_unit.v1` row plus one valid `Record`.
- [x] `src/testing/ReviewRowSchemaRegressionTest.java` ŌĆö golden byte-stable row for one deterministic offline review-shaped fixture, pinning the `crtk.review.ply.v1` field set, `schemaVersion`, tag delta, and `repro` block against accidental drift.
- [x] UCI path: fake-UCI coverage asserts the router issues bounded `go nodes` per ply and the `repro` block records the protocol path, node budget, duration budget, MultiPV, threads, hash, WDL, and `deterministic=false`.
- [x] Wire `ReviewClassifierRegressionTest`, `ReviewRowSchemaRegressionTest`, and `ReviewCommandRegressionTest` into `scripts/run_regression_suite.sh` under the `cli` target.
- [x] Wire the UCI-path review assertions into `ReviewCommandRegressionTest` under the `cli` target.

#### Docs plan

- New `wiki/game-review.md` ŌĆö the router's workflow, threshold table, the only-move/already-decided guards, blitz-vs-classical profiles, and the deterministic-vs-engine-dependent contract.
- Extend [`wiki/ai-agents.md`](wiki/ai-agents.md) ŌĆö add `review game`/`batch`/`summary` to the command-to-contract table with the `crtk.review.ply.v1` JSONL shape.
- Extend `wiki/use-cases.md` ŌĆö a "review my own games" recipe under the researcher/study persona.
- Extend `wiki/outputs-and-logs.md` ŌĆö `.review.jsonl` default naming + the study-unit `.puzzles.json` fan-out.
- Update [`wiki/command-reference.md`](wiki/command-reference.md) ŌĆö the `review` area table (kept in sync with [`CliRegistry`](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java)).

#### Risks / tradeoffs

- **Engine cost.** Two bounded analyses per ply ├Ś full games is expensive; mitigated by `best-only` reuse, the [`Pool`](src/application/Pool.java), and explicit `--max-nodes`/`--max-duration`. A 40-move game at 800ms/ply is ~30s ŌĆö acceptable, but `review batch` over many games must surface progress (reuse [`application.console.Bar`](src/application/cli/command/RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java)).
- **False positives are the product-killer.** If the router cries "blunder" at noise, users stop trusting it. The four suppression guards + WDL gating are the defense and must be regression-pinned, not just documented.
- **Record schema is too thin (depends on A).** Without game-id/ply/provenance fields on [`Record`](src/chess/struct/Record.java), study units carry linkage as `META:` tags ŌĆö stringly-typed and brittle. Flag as a hard dependency on A; do not ship `--to-study` into the A store until A adds the fields.
- **`Engine.analyse` issues `go nodes` only.** Per the digest, depth/movetime templates are inert for external analysis; the router's `--max-duration` is the watchdog cap, not a `go movetime`. Document that node budget is the real lever.
- **Determinism honesty.** The headline verdicts are engine-dependent; overclaiming "reproducible game review" would repeat the wiki's existing determinism-overclaim debt. The `repro.deterministic` flag and docs must be explicit.

#### Acceptance criteria (checkable)

1. `crtk review game --pgn <fixture> --offline` produces a `.review.jsonl` with exactly one row per mainline ply and a `schemaVersion: "crtk.review.ply.v1"` field on every row.
2. A fixture game with a known hung-piece blunder yields exactly one `mistake_category: "blunder"` row at the correct ply, with `tags_after` containing a grounded `THREAT:`/`TACTIC:` hanging tag.
3. A fixture where a side keeps a +900 eval after a "300cp loss" yields **no** blunder (already-decided guard) ŌĆö pinned in [`ReviewClassifierRegressionTest`](src/testing).
4. [x] `--to-study` emits study-unit [`Record`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) objects whose `parent` is the pre-move FEN and `position` is the best-line FEN, re-importable by the puzzle/mining tooling.
5. Every row's `repro` block records engine, protocol path, node cap, multipv, threads, and a correct `deterministic` flag (`true` under `--offline`, `false` under external UCI).
6. [x] Workbench `review game` template produces a command string byte-identical to the CLI invocation (enforced by [`WorkbenchCommandRegression`](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java)).
7. [x] The Review panel renders the produced JSONL without recomputing verdicts.
8. All three new regression tests run under `scripts/run_regression_suite.sh cli` and gate CI.

#### Future expansion
