- Feed mistakes by category into initiative D (repertoire/SRS): opening-phase mistakes become repertoire gaps, tactical mistakes become drill cards.
- Feed `tags_delta` + `eval` into initiative G so `position describe` can narrate *why* a move was a mistake ("this dropped the d6 pawn and exposed the king") ŌĆö grounded strictly in the recorded tags, never invented.
- Multi-game player report: aggregate `review batch` into per-opponent/per-opening weakness profiles (a careful, local-only analog of "player prep", reusing [`PgnPrepReport`](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnPrepReport.java)).
- Publish a "your mistakes" puzzle book directly via `book collection` from the `.puzzles.json` the router emits.

---

### 8D. Repertoire & spaced repetition (explanation-first, time-budgeted)

**Verdict:** build-later ┬Ę **Priority:** P2 ┬Ę **Complexity:** large ┬Ę **Horizon:** medium-to-long-term
**Depends on:** A (local PGN database), C (game-review-to-study router), F (schemas/validation), G (grounded explanations). Soft dependency on the ECO `Encyclopedia` for opening-line seeding.

This is the *capstone* of the study loop, not a foundation. It schedules review of material that A stores, C produces, and G explains. Building it before those exist means inventing a study-unit format and a position/game store that A/C/F would supersede ŌĆö so it is sequenced last among the study-loop themes. The merit is real; the timing is dependent. Everything below is gated on at least A and F shipping.

---

#### Goal

A local, file-backed spaced-repetition trainer for **chess lines and the moves inside them**, where every card carries a *grounded explanation* of why the move is right (sourced from the tag engine / `position describe`, never invented), and every review session is bounded by an explicit **time budget** and a **max-new-cards** cap so review can never balloon. Repertoires are imported from and exported to plain PGN with zero lock-in. This is **not** a course marketplace, not a content store, not an online play/social feature ŌĆö it is a local file format plus a deterministic scheduler over the user's own lines.

#### User story

> "I keep my White repertoire as a PGN with variations. I import it, the tool turns each of my intended replies into a review card, weights the lines I actually reach in my own games higher, and each morning gives me a 12-minute session of due cards. When I blank on `9...Nbd7` it shows me the grounded reason (`TACTIC: ŌĆ”`, `IDEA: king_safety`, the engine PV) rather than just flipping the answer. When I lose a game in a line I "knew", the review router (initiative C) drops the refutation in as a new card. I never get a 200-card pileup because the session is time-capped and new cards are rate-limited."

#### Non-goals

- **NOT a course marketplace / content store.** No bundled "courses", no shareable paid decks, no remote catalog. Repertoires are the user's own PGN files on disk. (This is the line the product boundary draws and we hold it.)
- **No online sync / accounts / leaderboards.** Review state is a local file. Sharing = "send the PGN", same as any other artifact.
- **No new chess rules engine.** Legality, SAN, position identity all route through the one shared core ([Position.java](src/chess/core/Position.java), [SAN.java](src/chess/core/SAN.java)). Determinism is preserved.
- **Not a strength estimator.** A card's "difficulty" is scheduling state, not an Elo. (Same honesty caveat the puzzle rating carries.)
- **No third-party SRS dependency** (no Anki/FSRS library jar). The scheduler is a small in-house deterministic function under the plain `javac --release 17` build.

---

#### "Line learned" vs "move learned" ŌĆö the core modeling decision

This distinction drives the whole schema. A na├»ve SRS makes one card per position-and-answer. That over-counts: a 14-ply mainline you know cold should not be 14 independent daily cards. CRTK models **both**, explicitly:

- **Move card (atomic unit).** Keyed on `(position signatureCore, expected reply move)`. This is what actually gets scheduled and reviewed. The prompt is the position (from the *opponent's* last move, i.e. it is the user's turn); the answer is the user's intended move from the repertoire. Grounded explanation attaches here.
- **Line (aggregate).** A named path through the repertoire tree (e.g. "Najdorf ŌĆö English Attack ŌĆö main"). A line is *not* itself scheduled; it is `learned` when **all** of its move cards are at or above a `learnedInterval` threshold. Line state is **derived**, never stored as ground truth, so it cannot drift out of sync with its moves.

Why this split:
- It lets the trainer report "Line learned: 6/8 main lines" (motivating, line-level) while scheduling at move granularity (correct, no over-counting of memorized prefixes).
- A position reachable by transposition produces **one** move card (signatureCore is transposition-aware ŌĆö confirmed: `Encyclopedia` already collapses transpositions on `pos.signatureCore()`, [Encyclopedia.java](src/chess/eco/Encyclopedia.java) line 239 `byCoreSignature.get(pos.signatureCore())`). So if two named lines converge, the shared move is studied once. This is a direct payoff of reusing the existing core hashing rather than FEN-string keys.

ASSUMPTION: `signatureCore()` (FNV-1a, not Zobrist ŌĆö confirmed [Position.java](src/chess/core/Position.java)) has acceptable collision risk for a single user's repertoire (thousands of positions, not millions). The digest flags FNV collision risk only for ML-scale dedup. For a personal repertoire this is fine; we document it and key cards on `signatureCore` + a stored canonical FEN so a collision is detectable on load (two distinct FENs hashing equal ŌåÆ fail loud, per F's strict-mode philosophy).

---

#### Minimal SRS data model

Deterministic, additive, and JSON ŌĆö mirroring the existing `Record` shape ([Record.java](src/chess/struct/Record.java)) so it streams through the same `Writer.appendJsonObjects` / `RecordIO` plumbing rather than a new file format.

A **repertoire deck** is a JSON array (or JSONL) of move cards. One card object:

```
{
  "schema": "crtk.repertoire.card.v1",          // F: explicit schema version (Record has none today)
  "id": "<signatureCore-hex>:<expected-uci>",   // stable transposition-aware key
  "deck": "white-najdorf",                        // deck/repertoire name (a file stem, no marketplace)
  "side": "white",                                // which side this repertoire trains
  "position": "<canonical FEN>",                  // for collision detection + replay; parsed via Fen
  "core_sig": 7458123900112233,                   // Position.signatureCore() as long
  "expected_uci": "e2e4",                         // the user's intended reply
  "expected_san": "e4",                           // rendered via SAN.toAlgebraic (display only)
  "line_ids": ["najdorf-english-main"],           // aggregate membership (a move may sit on many lines)
  "ply": 17,                                       // depth in the repertoire tree (for ordering only)
  "frequency_weight": 0.83,                        // 0..1, line-frequency weighting (see below)
  "source": "import:repertoire-white.pgn",        // provenance (F/I): where the card came from
  "explanation_tags": ["IDEA: king_safety", "TACTIC: fork move=g1f3 ..."],  // grounded, from chess.tag
  "review": {
    "schema": "crtk.repertoire.review.v1",
    "interval_days": 6,                            // current spacing
    "ease": 250,                                   // permille (250 = 2.50), integer to stay byte-stable
    "reps": 4,                                      // successful reviews in a row
    "lapses": 1,                                    // times forgotten
    "due_epoch_day": 20631,                         // due date as integer days since epoch (NOT millis)
    "last_grade": "good",                           // again|hard|good|easy
    "introduced_epoch_day": 20602
  }
}
```

Determinism-critical schema choices:
- **`due_epoch_day` is an integer day count, never a wall-clock millisecond.** All scheduling math is integer-day arithmetic seeded by a `--today <epoch-day>` (or `--today YYYY-MM-DD`) input. Tests pass a fixed `--today`; production defaults to the system date floored to UTC day. This is the analog of the engine rule that `Result.equals` must strip `elapsedMillis` ([Result.java](src/chess/engine/Result.java)) ŌĆö *no live clock in the comparable state*.
- **`ease` is integer permille**, not a float, so two runs serialize byte-identically (avoids the float-formatting determinism trap the dataset exporters live with).
- **Tie-breaking in due-card ordering uses `deterministicUnit(core_sig)`** ŌĆö reuse the exact splitmix64 jitter pattern already in [Scorer.java](src/chess/puzzle/Scorer.java) line 1198 (`deterministicUnit(long)`). Same `--today` + same deck file ŌćÆ identical session order, no `Random` without a seed.

Scheduler: a small, in-house SM-2-style integer function (`crtk.repertoire.Scheduler`). We deliberately do **not** vendor FSRS ŌĆö it would be either a third-party jar (violates no-deps) or a large reimplementation with its own training data we cannot reproduce. SM-2 integer math is ~40 lines, fully testable, and good enough for a personal repertoire. We mark this as a tradeoff, not a limitation we hide.

---

#### Preventing review overload (the hard requirement)

Three independent caps, all explicit CLI flags with conservative defaults (mirroring the conservative-defaults posture of [Defaults.java](src/application/gui/workbench/Defaults.java)):

1. **Time budget** `--time 12m` ŌĆö the session stops queuing new cards once the *estimated* remaining time (a fixed per-card cost estimate, e.g. 15s/new card, 8s/review card ŌĆö constants, not learned) would exceed the budget. The budget is advisory on the *plan*, not a stopwatch on the human (so it stays deterministic: the plan is computed up front from card counts, not from how long the user actually took).
2. **Max new cards** `--max-new 10` ŌĆö caps how many never-introduced cards enter today. This is the primary overload valve; without it, importing a 400-move repertoire would make day 1 unreviewable.
3. **Max total** `--max-cards 60` ŌĆö hard ceiling on session size regardless of due backlog. Backlog beyond this rolls forward (oldest-due first, frequency-weighted).

When backlog exceeds capacity, ordering is: (a) lapsed cards first, (b) then by `due_epoch_day` ascending, (c) then by `frequency_weight` descending, (d) then by `deterministicUnit(core_sig)`. Deterministic and explainable.

#### Line frequency weighting (from user games + mistakes)

A flat repertoire treats the Sicilian sideline you face once a year the same as your main e4 reply. We weight by **how often the user actually reaches each line**, computed offline from the user's own game database (initiative A) and review router (initiative C):

- `frequency_weight` for a move card = normalized count of how many of the user's stored games (A's PGN store) pass through that card's `core_sig`, blended with a **mistake boost**: positions where C flagged the user's actual move as a blunder/inaccuracy in that line get a multiplicative bump (you most need to drill where you've actually erred).
- This is a **batch recompute** (`crtk repertoire weight`), not live: it reads the game store + the C-produced mistake records, recomputes weights deterministically, and rewrites the deck. No hidden state.
- ASSUMPTION: A exposes a position-frequency query (or at least a streamable position index keyed on `signatureCore`) ŌĆö this is exactly the `PgnExplorerModel.filterByPosition` / `positionKeys` logic ([PgnExplorerModel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java) lines 83, 321) promoted into core by A. If A is not yet shipped, `repertoire weight` degrades to uniform weights and prints a notice (fail-soft, documented).

---

#### MVP (smallest shippable)

Ships with **A and F present**, before C/G are needed:

- Import a repertoire PGN (with variations) ŌåÆ a deck JSON keyed on `core_sig`. One move card per `(position, user reply)` on the user's side.
- `crtk repertoire review` produces a **deterministic, time-budgeted, max-new-capped** session as JSONL (prompt FEN, expected SAN/UCI, the stored grounded explanation tags). No interactive TUI in MVP ŌĆö it emits the session plan and accepts a graded-results file back (so it's scriptable and testable without a UI).
- `crtk repertoire grade` applies an again/hard/good/easy result file to the deck, advancing the SM-2 state with integer-day math.
- Export deck ŌåÆ PGN (round-trip; the lines come back out as PGN variations). **No lock-in** is a release gate.
- Explanations in MVP are whatever `fen tags` already produces (grounded, engine-free). G-quality prose is a later enhancement.

MVP explicitly *excludes*: frequency weighting (needs A's game store mature), mistake-driven cards (needs C), the "why/plan" prose layer (needs G), and the Workbench surface.

#### Full version

- **Frequency + mistake weighting** wired to A's game store and C's mistake records (`crtk repertoire weight`).
- **C integration**: `crtk review ŌĆ”` (initiative C) can emit a study unit that `crtk repertoire add` ingests as a new card with `source: "review:<game-id>"` ŌĆö closing the loop "lost a game ŌåÆ it's a card tomorrow".
- **G integration**: cards render the grounded *explanation* (causation/plan) from the deepened `position describe`, not just raw tags. The explanation must still pass the grounding rule ŌĆö every move it names is a legal candidate.
- **Workbench Repertoire surface** (below), as an Inspector/View, not a new shell.
- **Line dashboards**: "lines learned", due-forecast histogram, weakest cards by lapse count.

---

#### Proposed CLI surface (noun-then-verb, explicit budgets)

New area `repertoire` (alias `rep`). All file paths default under the configured output dir (`dump/`, [Config.java](src/application/Config.java) `K_OUTPUT`).

- `crtk repertoire import --pgn <file> --side white|black --deck <name> [--output <deck.json>] [--explain none|tags] [--max-ply N]`
  Parse PGN variations, generate move cards for `--side`'s replies. `--explain tags` runs the engine-free tagger per card; `none` skips. `--max-ply` bounds tree depth.
- `crtk repertoire review --input <deck.json> [--today YYYY-MM-DD|<epoch-day>] [--time 12m] [--max-new 10] [--max-cards 60] [--format jsonl|text] [--output <session.jsonl>]`
  Emit the due session plan. Deterministic given `--input` + `--today` + caps. No engine budget needed (pure scheduling); if `--explain` regeneration is requested it would take the standard external-engine block ŌĆö but default review uses stored explanations only.
- `crtk repertoire grade --input <deck.json> --results <graded.jsonl> [--today YYYY-MM-DD] [--output <deck.json>]`
  Apply grades (`{"id":ŌĆ”, "grade":"good"}` per line), advance SM-2 state, rewrite deck. In-place write guarded against output==input clobber (reuse the existing per-command guard pattern in `RecordCommands`).
- `crtk repertoire weight --input <deck.json> --games <pgn-or-store> [--mistakes <records.json>] [--output <deck.json>]`
  Recompute `frequency_weight` from the user's games (A) and optional C mistake records.
- `crtk repertoire add --input <deck.json> --fen <FEN> --move <uci|san> [--deck <name>] [--source <str>] [--explain none|tags]`
  Insert a single card (the seam C calls).
- `crtk repertoire export --input <deck.json> --output <pgn>` ŌĆö back to PGN, no lock-in.
- `crtk repertoire stats --input <deck.json> [--today YYYY-MM-DD]` ŌĆö due today, new available, lines learned (derived), lapse leaderboard. `--json` for automation (F).

Engine budgets: only `import --explain` and any explanation *re-generation* touch an engine, and only if the user opts into engine-enriched tags; those reuse the standard `--protocol-path/-P --max-nodes --max-duration --multipv --threads --hash` block from [EngineSupport.java](src/application/cli/command/EngineSupport.java). Plain review/grade/weight are engine-free and therefore fast and reproducible.

#### Proposed Workbench surface (mirrors CLI, no second impl)

A **Repertoire view** registered in the existing `ViewRegistry` ([WindowLifecycle.java](src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowLifecycle.java)), reusing the one shared board (`BoardController`/`BoardStage` from the UX redesign). It does **not** reimplement scheduling ŌĆö it shells out to `crtk repertoire ŌĆ”` via [CommandRunner.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java) (child JVM running `application.Main`) exactly like every other workbench surface, and the command preview shows the exact runnable command (the CLI-is-source-of-truth contract enforced by `WorkbenchCommandRegression`).
- Review panel: shows the prompt position on the shared board, "Show answer" reveals expected move + grounded explanation; the four grade buttons write a results JSONL that the panel feeds to `repertoire grade`.
- Repertoire Inspector: deck stats, lines-learned, due forecast ŌĆö populated from `repertoire stats --json`.
- Reuse [OpeningBook.java](src/application/gui/workbench/play/OpeningBook.java)'s "replay every ECO entry" pattern for an optional "seed from ECO" affordance.

---

#### Architecture implications

- **Plain javac / no deps.** New package `chess.repertoire` (core: `Card`, `Deck`, `Scheduler`, `LineState` derivation) + `application.cli.command.RepertoireCommand`. The scheduler is pure integer math. JSON via the existing dependency-free `utility.Json` and `Record`-style tolerant parsing. No optional dep is needed at all for MVP ŌĆö the only place an optional dep could appear is FSRS, which we explicitly reject.
- **One shared core.** Card generation replays SAN through `SAN.playLine` ([SAN.java](src/chess/core/SAN.java) line 175, returns `PlayedLine` with `getResult()`/`getInvalidToken()`), so an illegal repertoire move fails at import, not silently. Position identity is `Position.signatureCore()`. Nothing forks legality.
- **Stable on-disk contract under F.** The card/review schemas get versions and published JSON Schema files alongside A's store schema, and load uses a *fail-loud* strict path (unlike today's silently-dropping `Record.fromJson`/`Reader`). A `core_sig` collision (same hash, different stored FEN) is a hard error.
- **Layering.** `chess.repertoire` must not import `application.*` or `testing.*` (enforced by [SourceHeaderRegressionTest.java](src/testing/SourceHeaderRegressionTest.java)). The CLI command lives in `application.cli.command`.

#### Existing components to reuse (real)

- [Encyclopedia.java](src/chess/eco/Encyclopedia.java) + [Entry.java](src/chess/eco/Entry.java) ŌĆö `getMoves()`/`getPosition()`/`getMovetext()` and the `signatureCore`-keyed transposition map; the model for "replay a line, key positions on core sig". **Gap:** the shared `chess.eco` layer still exposes endpoint entries, not a reusable opening tree; `crtk eco continuations` can walk next moves, but that continuation builder is CLI-local and should be promoted before repertoire depends on it.
- [OpeningBook.java](src/application/gui/workbench/play/OpeningBook.java) ŌĆö already replays every ECO entry's parsed moves into a position-keyed book; directly reusable for ECO seeding.
- [Pgn.java](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java) (`parseGames`/`parseGame`/`write`/`toPgnString`) + [Game.java](src/chess/struct/Game.java) (`Node`, `getMainline`, `getVariations`) ŌĆö import/export with variation trees.
- [PgnExplorerModel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java) ŌĆö `filterByPosition`, `deduplicate`, `positionKeys`; the frequency-weighting query (to be promoted into A's core).
- [SAN.java](src/chess/core/SAN.java) `playLine`/`toAlgebraic`/`fromAlgebraic` ŌĆö replay + render.
- [Record.java](src/chess/struct/Record.java) + [Writer.java](src/chess/io/Writer.java) `appendJsonObjects` + [RecordIO.java](src/application/cli/RecordIO.java) ŌĆö JSON-array/JSONL streaming and append-safe writes; card decks reuse this plumbing.
- [Scorer.java](src/chess/puzzle/Scorer.java) `deterministicUnit(long)` (line 1198) ŌĆö the splitmix64 tie-break for deterministic ordering.
- [Generator.java](src/chess/tag/Generator.java) ŌĆö engine-free grounded tags for `--explain tags`.

#### Files / packages likely affected

- **New:** `src/chess/repertoire/Card.java`, `Deck.java`, `Scheduler.java`, `LineState.java`, `package-info.java`; `src/application/cli/command/RepertoireCommand.java`.
- **Edit:** [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) (`repertoireGroup()` + `rep` alias), [Constants.java](src/application/cli/Constants.java) (flag/token constants), [HelpCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/HelpCommand.java) + [command-reference.md](wiki/command-reference.md) (mirrored docs).
- **Workbench:** new `src/application/gui/workbench/repertoire/RepertoirePanel.java` + Inspector; register in [WindowLifecycle.java](src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowLifecycle.java); add a `CommandTemplates` entry ([CommandTemplates.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java)).
- **F coupling:** new `*.schema.json` for `crtk.repertoire.card.v1` / `crtk.repertoire.review.v1`, wherever F lands published schemas.

#### Testing plan (in-house harness style)

New `src/testing/RepertoireRegressionTest.java` (static `main`, `import static testing.TestSupport.*`, prints `RepertoireRegressionTest: all checks passed`), wired into the `core` (or a new `repertoire`) target of [run_regression_suite.sh](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh) ŌĆö critically *wired in*, unlike the six orphaned ML tests the digest flags. Specific cases:

- **Scheduler determinism:** grade a card `good` four times with fixed `--today` increments; assert exact `interval_days`/`ease`/`due_epoch_day` golden integers. Re-run; assert byte-identical deck JSON.
- **No live clock:** run `review` twice with the same `--today` but real wall clock advancing between calls; assert identical session plan (proves no `System.currentTimeMillis` leaks into comparable state).
- **Move vs line:** import a 3-move shared-prefix repertoire where two named lines transpose; assert the shared position yields **one** card (`core_sig` collapse) and that "line learned" is derived = false until all member cards reach `learnedInterval`, then flips to true.
- **Overload caps:** import 100 cards, `--max-new 5 --max-cards 20`; assert session Ōēż20, exactly 5 new, deterministic ordering (lapsed ŌåÆ due ŌåÆ frequency ŌåÆ splitmix64 tie-break) via golden id sequence.
- **Illegal-move import fails loud:** a PGN with an illegal repertoire move ŌåÆ nonzero exit and the offending token reported (`PlayedLine.getInvalidToken()`), not a silently dropped card.
- **PGN round-trip / no lock-in:** import ŌåÆ export ŌåÆ re-import; assert deck card set (by id) is identical.
- **Collision guard:** craft two cards with equal stored `core_sig` but different FEN ŌåÆ strict load throws (F fail-loud).
- **Frequency weighting (with A stub):** feed a tiny game store hitting line X 3├Ś and line Y once; assert `frequency_weight(X) > frequency_weight(Y)` and that a C-flagged mistake on Y applies the documented multiplicative boost. Deterministic.
- **CLI surface:** extend [CLICommandRegressionTest.java](src/testing/CLICommandRegressionTest.java) ŌĆö `repertoire review --json` shape, `--max-new`+`--time` parse, `--json`/`--jsonl` mutual-exclusion (the standard `resolveOutputMode` exit-2 contract).
- **Workbench mirror:** `WorkbenchCommandRegression` must cover the new runnable paths (its `testCommandControllerCoversCliRegistry` walks the registry and will fail if the Repertoire template is missing ŌĆö free enforcement).

#### Docs plan

- New **`wiki/repertoire.md`** ŌĆö model (move vs line), the three overload caps, frequency/mistake weighting, the determinism contract (`--today`, integer ease), and an explicit "**This is not a course marketplace; repertoires are your own PGN files**" statement.
- Update [command-reference.md](wiki/command-reference.md) (new `repertoire` area table) and [ai-agents.md](wiki/ai-agents.md) (the `--json` review/stats contract for automation).
- Update [use-cases.md](wiki/use-cases.md) (student persona: import ŌåÆ daily timed review ŌåÆ loss-driven cards via C).
- Mention in [workbench.md](wiki/workbench.md) once the view ships.

#### Risks / tradeoffs

- **SM-2 vs FSRS.** In-house SM-2 is weaker than modern FSRS but keeps no-deps + determinism + reproducibility. We state this openly rather than hide it; the scheduler is pluggable behind `Scheduler` if a deterministic FSRS-lite is ever hand-written.
- **FNV `signatureCore` collisions.** Acceptable at personal scale, guarded by stored-FEN cross-check, documented. Not acceptable to silently key cards on a hash alone ŌĆö hence the dual key.
- **Frequency weighting hard-depends on A.** Without A it degrades to uniform (fail-soft) ŌĆö but then a headline feature is hollow, which is exactly why D is sequenced after A.
- **Explanation quality is borrowed.** Until G deepens `position describe`, card explanations are raw grounded tags ŌĆö truthful but not yet "why/plan" prose. Don't oversell card explanations before G.
- **Time budget is advisory, not enforced.** Computing the plan from card-count estimates (not a live stopwatch) is the price of determinism. A user who is slow still gets the planned set; we document this is a *plan budget*.
- **Scope creep toward "courses."** The single strongest pull is "let users share/sell decks." We reject it at the boundary; sharing is "send the PGN."

#### Acceptance criteria (checkable)

- [ ] `crtk repertoire import --pgn r.pgn --side white --deck w` produces a versioned `crtk.repertoire.card.v1` deck; one card per `(core_sig, reply)`; transpositions collapse to one card.
- [ ] `crtk repertoire review --input w.json --today 2026-06-15 --time 12m --max-new 10 --max-cards 60` is **byte-identical across reruns** with the same flags and a moving wall clock.
- [ ] `grade` advances SM-2 state with integer-day arithmetic; golden interval/ease/due values match.
- [ ] Overload caps are hard: session never exceeds `--max-cards`; new cards never exceed `--max-new`.
- [ ] `export` ŌåÆ `import` round-trips the card set (no lock-in); export is plain PGN openable in any tool.
- [ ] Illegal repertoire move at import ŌåÆ nonzero exit + offending token reported.
- [ ] `RepertoireRegressionTest` is wired into the regression runner and CI (not orphaned).
- [ ] Workbench Repertoire view's command preview equals the runnable `crtk repertoire ŌĆ”` command (`WorkbenchCommandRegression` green).
- [ ] `wiki/repertoire.md` exists and contains the explicit "not a course marketplace" boundary statement.

#### Future expansion

- Deterministic FSRS-lite scheduler (hand-written, no jar) behind the `Scheduler` seam.
- "Punish blind spots": auto-bias `--max-new` toward lines where C reports recent losses (tighter C loop).
- Repertoire *coverage* report: which opponent replies in the user's games hit a position with **no** repertoire card ("you have no prepared answer to 3...Bb4 ŌĆö you've faced it 4 times").
- Cross-deck transposition awareness (White and Black decks sharing a reversed-color motif ŌĆö research-y, low priority).
- Export review history as a dataset (initiative I) for studying one's own retention ŌĆö strictly local, provenance-stamped.

---

### 8E. Local API server + SDKs (and dev workflows / Theme K)

**Initiative:** E (local API server + SDKs), with Theme K (VSCode / Jupyter / dev workflows) attached as a downstream consumer.
**Term:** medium-term (server MVP), long-term (full SDKs + Theme K).
**Priority:** P2.
**Complexity:** large (server + two SDK languages + sync discipline); Theme K is medium.
**Dependencies:** **F is a hard prerequisite** (machine-readable command catalog + JSON Schemas). Theme K depends on E and F. Do not start E before F lands a `crtk help --json` catalog, or the server will hard-code contracts F is meant to own.

---

#### Goal

Expose CRTK's existing CLI surface as a **localhost-only analysis/automation daemon** so that an agent, notebook, or editor can drive the toolkit without paying JVM startup per call, and ship thin clients (Python first, TypeScript second) that wrap that daemon. The non-negotiable design rule: the server **calls the exact same handler code as the CLI** ŌĆö it dispatches through [CliRegistry](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) and the `Consumer<Argv>` handlers in [CliCommand](src/application/cli/CliCommand.java), never a second implementation. Today every command is process-per-invocation via [Main.run(String[])](src/application/Main.java) (which already returns an exit code rather than calling `System.exit`, lines 71-85 ŌĆö the seam we exploit).

#### User story

- *As an AI agent*, I open one long-lived `crtk serve` daemon and issue `move list`, `engine bestmove --max-nodes 200000`, `fen tags`, `position describe` over JSON-RPC, getting back the same documented JSON shapes the CLI emits, without 15├Ś JVM cold-starts in a loop.
- *As a researcher in a Jupyter notebook*, I call `crtk.engine_bestmove(fen, max_nodes=200_000)` from a Python cell and render the board inline, all backed by the same deterministic core.
- *As a VSCode user*, I hover a FEN in a `.epd`/`.pgn` file and see legal-move count, ECO name, and a one-line `position describe` summary.

#### Non-goals (product-boundary critical)

These are **forbidden**, not merely deprioritized ŌĆö the daemon must never drift toward the hard product boundary:

- No online play, matchmaking, accounts, social, anti-cheat, or cloud credit.
- No binding to non-loopback by default. Default bind is `127.0.0.1`; binding `0.0.0.0` requires an explicit `--bind` flag plus a printed warning.
- No multi-tenant auth/user system. Optional single shared token only (`--token`), aimed at "don't let another local app poke my engine," not identity.
- No attempt to be faster than the CLI's core. The daemon's only performance claim is *amortizing JVM/JIT/engine-pool warmup*, not better search.
- No new analysis capability that does not already exist as a CLI command. If the server can do something the CLI cannot, that is a bug in the design.

#### MVP (smallest shippable)

A single command, **HTTP on loopback**, that dispatches arbitrary CLI argv and returns captured stdout + exit code as JSON. This is deliberately the thinnest possible thing that proves the "one impl" rule:

- `crtk serve --port 8088` starts an in-process [com.sun.net.httpserver.HttpServer](https://docs.oracle.com/en/java/javase/17/docs/api/jdk.httpserver/com/sun/net/httpserver/package-summary.html) bound to `127.0.0.1`.
- One endpoint: `POST /run` with body `{"args":["engine","bestmove","--fen","...","--max-nodes","200000"]}`.
- Server validates argv (no `serve`, no `workbench`/`gui` recursion), captures `System.out`/`System.err` for that invocation, calls `application.Main.run(args)`, returns `{"ok":<exit==0>,"exit_code":N,"stdout":"...","stderr":"...","args":[...]}`.
- `GET /catalog` returns the F-produced command catalog (proxy of `crtk help --json`).
- `GET /healthz` returns `{"ok":true,"version":"1.0.0","java":"..."}` (reuse the [VersionCommand](src/application/cli/command/VersionCommand.java) JSON shape).

The MVP intentionally does **not** parse stdout into typed objects ŌĆö it returns the documented JSON the command already prints. That keeps the server a transport, not a parser, and means *every command that already supports `--json`/`--jsonl` works on day one* with zero per-command work.

The MVP blocker to solve cleanly: `Main.run` and command handlers write to the static `System.out`. The in-house test harness already proves this is capturable ŌĆö [TestSupport.captureStdout](src/testing/TestSupport.java) (lines 107-114) redirects `System.out` around a `Runnable`. The server must serialize invocations behind a single lock (see Risks) or, better, do the same redirect under a per-request lock. **ASSUMPTION:** handlers do not cache a reference to `System.out` at class-load; they call `System.out.println(...)` live. This is true for the handlers I read ([EngineBatchCommand](src/application/cli/command/EngineBatchCommand.java) builds strings then prints) but must be asserted by a regression test before relying on it.

#### Full version

1. **stdio JSON-RPC mode** in addition to HTTP: `crtk serve --stdio` speaks newline-delimited JSON-RPC 2.0 on stdin/stdout. This is the right transport for editor extensions and notebook kernels that spawn a child and own its lifetime (no port allocation, no firewall surface, dies with the parent). HTTP is the right transport for ad-hoc agents and multi-client polling. **Ship both** ŌĆö they share one dispatch core; only the framing differs.
2. **Warm engine pool reuse.** The daemon holds an [application.Pool](src/application/Pool.java) of external UCI engines (already a "fixed-size pool of engine workers that lease Engine instances," lines 33-44) and the built-in searcher's JIT-warm state, so the second `engine bestmove` is fast. This is the entire performance justification for E.
3. **Long-running jobs** for `puzzle mine`, `record dataset *`, `engine gauntlet`: `POST /jobs` returns a job id immediately; `GET /jobs/{id}` polls status; `GET /jobs/{id}/stream` (HTTP chunked) or a JSON-RPC `$/progress` notification streams output. Reuse the existing [RunManifest](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java) schema (`crtk.workbench.run-manifest.v1`, SHA-256 input/output provenance) as the job record ŌĆö the Workbench already records exactly this for child-JVM runs, so the daemon and Workbench converge on one job contract.
4. **Streaming analysis** via the existing [Engine.analyseInfinite(..., Consumer<Analysis> onUpdate)](src/chess/uci/Engine.java) hook (line 476; `onUpdate.accept(analysis)` at line 545). Exposed as `GET /analyze/stream` (SSE-style chunked) and JSON-RPC progress notifications ŌĆö the one capability that genuinely cannot be a single CLI invocation, so it earns a bespoke endpoint rather than going through `/run`.
5. **Schema-validated requests.** `POST /run` argv is validated against the F catalog before dispatch (unknown flags rejected with exit-2 semantics matching the CLI's `Argv.ensureConsumed()` contract), so a client gets a structured error instead of a stack trace.

#### Proposed CLI surface (noun-then-verb)

```
crtk serve [--port 8088] [--bind 127.0.0.1] [--stdio] [--token <secret>]
           [--engine-instances 4] [--protocol-path config/default.engine.toml]
           [--max-nodes 50000000] [--max-duration 1000000]
           [--allow-jobs] [--job-dir dump/serve-jobs] [-v|--verbose]
```

- `--stdio` switches off HTTP entirely and speaks JSON-RPC on stdin/stdout (mutually exclusive with `--port`/`--bind`; conflict ŌåÆ exit 2, mirroring the `--json`+`--jsonl` rejection in `CommandSupport.resolveOutputMode`).
- `--engine-instances`, `--protocol-path`, `--max-nodes`, `--max-duration` set **daemon-wide budget ceilings**. A per-request budget may *lower* but never *raise* these (see Architecture ŌåÆ engine-budget enforcement). These names are taken verbatim from existing config keys in [Config.java](src/application/Config.java) (`engine-instances`, `max-nodes`, `max-duration`) and the external-engine pool so there is no new vocabulary.
- `--allow-jobs` gates the long-running-job endpoints off by default (a daemon an agent left running should not silently spawn unbounded `puzzle mine` work).

`serve` is registered as a new root leaf in `CliRegistry.buildRoot()` next to `doctor`/`clean`/`version`. It must be **excluded from the F catalog's "runnable over the wire" set** (a client cannot ask the daemon to start another daemon), exactly as `workbench`/`gui` are already excluded from the Workbench "All CLI" template per `WorkbenchCommandRegression`.

#### Proposed Workbench surface (mirror, no second impl)

The Workbench already shells out to a child JVM via [CommandRunner.javaInvocation()](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java) (builds `java -cp <classpath> application.Main <args>`, lines 505-511). To mirror E without a hidden second implementation:

- Add a **"Serve" control** in the Dashboard / Console area that starts/stops a local daemon **as a child process** using the same `CommandRunner` invocation it already uses for everything else (`application.Main serve --port ...`), and shows the bound URL + health status. The Workbench does not embed its own HTTP server; it launches the same `crtk serve` a terminal user would.
- The command preview must show the exact runnable `crtk serve ...` line (the Workbench's existing "generated command preview must equal the runnable command" contract from `wiki/cli-command-guide.md`).
- No GUI-only daemon defaults: every field maps to a real `serve` flag.

#### Data model / schema implications (concrete fields)

These belong to **F** but E is the first consumer, so define them here:

- **`/run` request:** `{"args": string[], "stdin"?: string, "timeout_ms"?: int}`.
- **`/run` response:** `{"ok": bool, "exit_code": int, "args": string[], "stdout": string, "stderr": string, "duration_ms": long}`. Exit-code taxonomy is the CLI's: `0` ok, `2` usage/input, `3` invalid FEN, `1` config-warnings ŌĆö surfaced unchanged so clients map errors identically to the CLI.
- **`/catalog` response:** the F catalog object ŌĆö `{"schema":"crtk.cli.catalog.v1","version":"1.0.0","areas":[{"path":"engine","actions":[{"path":"engine bestmove","aliases":[...],"summary":"...","flags":[{"name":"--max-nodes","takesValue":true,"valueType":"long"}, ...],"exitCodes":[0,2,3]}]}]}`. Produced by serializing `CliRegistry.root()` (all metadata ŌĆö `name`/`summary`/`aliases`/`examples` ŌĆö already lives on `CliCommand`; per-flag typing is the new F work).
- **Job record:** reuse `RunManifest` fields verbatim (`schema`, `jobId`, `createdAt`, `completedAt`, `status`, `exitCode`, `durationMillis`, `command`, `args[]`, `stdin{present,bytes,sha256}`, `inputs[]`, `outputs[]`, `logPath`, `summary`, `outputBytes`, `outputPreview`). New `serve` jobs write `run-%05d-<status>.json` into `--job-dir`, identical naming to the Workbench's `dumpPath("workbench-runs")`.
- **No new on-disk store.** The daemon is stateless across restarts except for job manifests on disk (which already have a schema). It does **not** become a database ŌĆö that is Theme A.

#### Architecture implications

- **`com.sun.net.httpserver` is sufficient and is the right choice.** It ships in the JDK (`jdk.httpserver` module), needs no third-party dependency, and preserves the plain-`javac --release 17`, zero-Maven/Gradle, zero-deps build. Verified: a grep for `com.sun.net.httpserver|ServerSocket|HttpServer` over `src/` returns **no files today**, so this is greenfield and there is no competing server to reconcile. It is bare (no routing, no JSON), but the daemon only needs a handful of paths and CRTK already has an in-house JSON layer ([utility.Json](src/utility/Json.java): `esc`, `stringArray`, `streamTopLevelObjects`, `parseStringField`, `parseLongField`, `parseStringArrayField`). **Caveat:** `utility.Json` is emit/parse-helpers, not an object builder ŌĆö request parsing will need a small tolerant object reader; reuse `Json.parseStringField`/`parseStringArrayField` rather than introducing Jackson/Gson.
- **HTTP vs stdio:** both, sharing one dispatch function `dispatch(String[] args, byte[] stdin) -> RunResult`. HTTP for agents/poll/multi-client; stdio JSON-RPC for editor/notebook child processes. Do not pick one; the framing layer is ~50 lines each over a shared core.
- **localhost default, always.** Bind `127.0.0.1` unless `--bind` overrides with a warning. No TLS (loopback only). Optional `--token` checked as a constant-time-compared header/`Authorization` value; absence = no auth (acceptable on loopback).
- **Server calls the same code as the CLI.** Dispatch path: parse JSON ŌåÆ build `String[] args` ŌåÆ `application.Main.run(args)` under a redirect of `System.out`/`System.err`. This guarantees the server can never diverge from the CLI because there is no parallel handler set. The alternative (re-walking `CliRegistry` and calling `handler().accept(new Argv(tail))` directly) is also acceptable and slightly cleaner for capturing structured results, but `Main.run` already encapsulates the greedy token-match + help-flag + exit-code mapping in `dispatch(...)` (lines 93-153), so reusing it avoids duplicating that logic.
- **Concurrency / stdout capture is the central risk.** `System.out` is a single static stream; handlers print to it live. Two simultaneous `/run` calls would interleave output. MVP: serialize all `/run` dispatch behind one `ReentrantLock` (correctness over throughput ŌĆö the engine pool, not request parallelism, is where concurrency belongs). Full version: investigate per-request `System.out` redirection is process-global, so the lock stays; true parallelism only for the streaming-analysis endpoints which use the engine pool's own locking. **This single-flight constraint must be documented**, because an agent expecting parallel `/run` will be surprised.
- **Engine-budget enforcement.** Daemon ceilings (`--max-nodes`/`--max-duration`/`--engine-instances`) are injected into every dispatch as the *maximum* allowed. If a request's `--max-nodes` exceeds the ceiling, clamp to the ceiling and note it in the response (`"budget_clamped":true`). If a request omits a budget, apply the daemon default. This prevents a runaway agent from issuing `engine bestmove --max-duration 600s` and pinning the box. Budgets remain explicit and bounded ŌĆö the core preserved value. **ASSUMPTION:** clamping is implemented in the `serve` dispatch wrapper, not by editing each handler; verify that injecting/overriding `--max-nodes` in the argv before `Main.run` is honored by `EngineSupport.UciOptions` resolution (it reads from `Argv`, so prepending a clamped flag works).
- **Long-running jobs** run on the daemon's executor (reuse `Pool`'s `ExecutorService` pattern, daemon threads, lines 55-59), write `RunManifest` job files, and are cancellable (SIGTERM-equivalent: interrupt + the existing `Engine` stall/`destroyForcibly` path).

#### Existing components to reuse

- [application.Main](src/application/Main.java) ŌĆö `run(String[]) -> int` is the dispatch seam (returns exit code, does not `System.exit`).
- [application.cli.CliRegistry](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) + [CliCommand](src/application/cli/CliCommand.java) ŌĆö catalog source and dispatch tree (already holds name/summary/aliases/examples).
- [application.Pool](src/application/Pool.java) ŌĆö warm external-UCI engine pool with leasing.
- [chess.uci.Engine.analyseInfinite + onUpdate](src/chess/uci/Engine.java) ŌĆö streaming-analysis hook (line 476).
- [chess.engine.AlphaBeta](src/chess/engine/AlphaBeta.java) / `Mcts` / `MateProver` / [chess.eval.See](src/chess/eval/See.java) ŌĆö in-process SDK surface for an eventual embedded-Java client.
- [utility.Json](src/utility/Json.java) ŌĆö dependency-free JSON emit/parse.
- [application.gui.workbench.session.RunManifest](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java) ŌĆö job-record schema + SHA-256 provenance.
- [application.gui.workbench.command.CommandRunner](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java) ŌĆö the child-process invocation model the Workbench "Serve" control reuses.
- [testing.TestSupport.captureStdout](src/testing/TestSupport.java) ŌĆö proves stdout redirect works; the server uses the same technique under lock.
- [VersionCommand](src/application/cli/command/VersionCommand.java) ŌĆö `/healthz` payload shape.

#### Files / packages likely affected

- New: `src/application/serve/Server.java` (HTTP), `src/application/serve/StdioRpc.java` (JSON-RPC), `src/application/serve/Dispatch.java` (shared `argsŌåÆRunResult` under lock + budget clamp), `src/application/serve/JobRunner.java`.
- New CLI handler: `src/application/cli/command/ServeCommand.java`; registration in `CliRegistry.buildRoot()`.
- F-owned: a catalog serializer (e.g. `src/application/cli/CliCatalog.java`) consumed by `/catalog` and `crtk help --json`.
- Touched: `src/application/cli/Constants.java` (new `CMD_SERVE`, `OPT_PORT`, `OPT_BIND`, `OPT_STDIO`, `OPT_TOKEN`); `wiki/ai-agents.md`, `wiki/command-reference.md`.
- Workbench: a small "Serve" panel/action under the existing Console/Dashboard surface that drives `CommandRunner`.

#### Testing plan (in-house harness style ŌĆö `public static void main`, `testing.TestSupport` asserts, no JUnit)

- `src/testing/ServeRegressionTest.java`:
  - Start `Server` on an ephemeral loopback port; `POST /run {"args":["move","list","--startpos","--jsonl"]}`; assert `exit_code==0` and that `stdout` parses to the same JSONL the CLI produces (compare against `TestSupport.runMain("move","list","--startpos","--jsonl")` captured output ŌĆö **proves one-impl equivalence byte-for-byte**, time fields excluded).
  - `POST /run {"args":["fen","validate","--fen","<bad>"]}` ŌåÆ assert `exit_code==3` (invalid-FEN taxonomy preserved over the wire).
  - `POST /run {"args":["serve","--port","9"]}` ŌåÆ rejected (no recursive daemon), and `["workbench"]` ŌåÆ rejected.
  - Budget clamp: daemon `--max-nodes 1000`, request `--max-nodes 9999999` ŌåÆ response `budget_clamped:true` and the engine actually ran Ōēż ceiling (assert via reported `nodes`).
  - Concurrency: fire two `/run` engine calls; assert outputs are not interleaved (each is valid JSON), proving the single-flight lock.
  - `GET /catalog` parses and contains `engine bestmove` with a `--max-nodes` flag entry; assert it covers the same runnable set as `CliRegistry.root()` (mirror of `WorkbenchCommandRegression.testCommandControllerCoversCliRegistry`).
  - `GET /healthz` returns `ok:true` with the `VersionCommand` version string.
  - stdio: spawn `Dispatch` in stdio mode, write one JSON-RPC line, read one response line, assert id/result correlation.
- Wire `ServeRegressionTest` into `scripts/run_regression_suite.sh` under a new `serve` target **and** into the `recommended`/`ci` aggregates (the digest flags that six existing ML tests rot precisely because they are unwired ŌĆö do not repeat that mistake).

#### Docs plan

- `wiki/ai-agents.md` ŌĆö add a "Daemon mode" section: when to use `serve` vs per-process CLI, the `/run`/`/catalog`/`/healthz` contract, budget-ceiling behavior, single-flight caveat. This is the natural home; the file already frames automation and says "a program driving crtk should never have to guess."
- `wiki/configuration.md` ŌĆö `serve` flags and daemon-ceiling config keys.
- `wiki/command-reference.md` ŌĆö the `serve` leaf row.
- New `wiki/sdk.md` (Theme K) ŌĆö Python/TS client install + examples.
- Update `wiki/outputs-and-logs.md` exit-code table note: same codes apply over HTTP.

#### Risks / tradeoffs

- **Static-stdout single-flight** caps `/run` to one-at-a-time. Acceptable (concurrency lives in the engine pool), but must be documented or agents will assume parallelism. The only true fix is process-isolation per request, which defeats the daemon's purpose.
- **Product-boundary creep.** A localhost JSON server is one careless flag away from "host this for my friends." Mitigations baked in: loopback default, explicit `--bind` warning, no auth/identity model, no play endpoints. Review any future `serve` PR against the boundary.
- **Premature contract lock-in.** If E ships before F's catalog/schemas, the daemon hard-codes JSON shapes F would otherwise own ŌåÆ the exact drift F exists to kill. Hence the hard dependency.
- **Streaming complexity.** SSE/chunked HTTP and JSON-RPC `$/progress` are more code than the value for an MVP; gate behind the full version.
- **Determinism caveat surfaces over the wire too:** `Result.equals` includes `elapsedMillis` and external-engine analysis is order-sensitive without `newGame` between leased tasks ŌĆö the daemon must issue `ucinewgame` between unrelated requests on a leased engine, or it inherits the Pool's documented determinism leak.

#### Acceptance criteria (checkable)

- `crtk serve --port N` binds only `127.0.0.1` by default (assert connection from a non-loopback address is refused unless `--bind`).
- `POST /run` of any `--json`/`--jsonl`-capable command returns byte-identical (time-stripped) JSON to the same CLI invocation ŌĆö proven by `ServeRegressionTest` diffing against `TestSupport.runMain`.
- No file under `src/application/serve/` imports a non-JDK third-party package (assert via `SourceHeaderRegressionTest`-style import scan).
- `serve` and `workbench`/`gui` are not dispatchable through `/run`.
- Daemon budget ceilings clamp request budgets downward and never upward.
- `ServeRegressionTest` runs in the `recommended` and `ci` suite targets (not orphaned).
- Build remains plain `javac --release 17` with no Maven/Gradle/deps.

#### Future expansion

- Embedded-Java SDK (no subprocess): expose `AlphaBeta.search`/`MateProver.proveMate`/`See.see` directly for JVM consumers.
- Unix-domain-socket transport for lower-latency editor integration.
- A `crtk serve --catalog-only` mode for completion tooling that needs the catalog without engine warmup.

---

#### Theme K: VSCode / Jupyter / dev workflows

Theme K is **verified absent** today (no notebook/IDE integration in `src/`; the only bridge is framework-agnostic `.npy` export from `chess.io.RecordDatasetExporter` etc.). Its entire value is parasitic on F (catalog/schemas for completion + validated outputs) and E (a warm daemon so a notebook cell or hover does not cold-start a JVM). Recommended ordering and what is premature:

1. **Python client (build first, P2, small).** A thin wrapper that prefers the running daemon and falls back to spawning the CLI. `crtk.run(*args) -> dict`, plus typed convenience methods generated from `/catalog` (`engine_bestmove(fen, max_nodes=...)`, `fen_tags(fen)`, `position_describe(fen)`). Pure-Python, no chess deps ŌĆö it shells to CRTK, which owns the one chess core. This is the highest-leverage K deliverable because researchers (the ML pillar) live in Python.
2. **Jupyter board rendering (build second, P2, small).** A `_repr_svg_` helper that calls `fen render`/`fen relations` (CRTK already emits SVG via `chess.images.render.Render`) so a FEN object renders inline. Reuses the Python client; no new server work.
3. **TypeScript client (P3, medium).** Same generated-from-`/catalog` shape as Python. Lower priority ŌĆö the agent/notebook audience is Python-first; TS matters mainly if a web/Node tool consumes the daemon.
4. **VSCode extension (P3, medium).** Hover-on-FEN ŌåÆ legal-move count + ECO name + one-line `position describe`; commands for `engine perft` and `engine analyze`/`explain` on the selection. Depends on the daemon (per-keystroke JVM cold-start is unusable) and on `/catalog` for command discovery.

**Premature for K:** anything before F+E. A VSCode extension or Jupyter magics built against today's prose docs would scrape help text or hard-code commands ŌĆö the precise drift F kills. Building TS before there is a single Python user is speculative. A full notebook kernel (vs. a thin client + `_repr_svg_`) is over-engineering: CRTK is not a language runtime.

**One-line recommendation:** sequence is **F ŌåÆ E(MVP HTTP) ŌåÆ Python client ŌåÆ Jupyter rendering ŌåÆ E(stdio+jobs+streaming) ŌåÆ VSCode ŌåÆ TS**, each gated on its predecessor actually shipping and being regression-wired.

---

### 8F. Schemas & validation

**Priority:** P0 ┬Ę **Complexity:** medium ┬Ę **Verdict:** build-now ┬Ę **Dependencies:** none (this initiative is itself a dependency of A, C, E, I, K, and a soft dependency of D, J)

#### Goal

Turn CRTK's *implicit* contracts into *explicit, machine-readable, versioned* artifacts, and make malformed input fail loudly instead of silently. Concretely, three things that do not exist today:

1. A **machine-readable command catalog** ŌĆö `crtk schema print cli --json` that serializes the in-memory command tree ([CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java)) so an agent/SDK/editor never has to scrape the 83 KB prose help renderer ([HelpCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/HelpCommand.java)).
2. **Published JSON Schema files** for every stable on-disk and on-stdout shape (the `.record` object, training-JSONL rows, dataset `meta.json`, engine analysis rows, etc.).
3. A **`schemaVersion` field** on the records that need it plus a **`crtk <area> validate`/`crtk schema validate`** surface that streams a file and reports per-line errors with line numbers ŌĆö replacing today's behavior where [Record.fromJson](src/chess/struct/Record.java) and [Reader.java](src/chess/io/Reader.java) silently drop malformed objects.

This is the lowest-cost, highest-leverage P0 because it is the *precondition* for almost every other product theme: an SDK (E), editor tooling (K), an on-disk game DB (A), a review-to-study router (C), and trustworthy dataset provenance (I) all need a stable, declared contract to build on. Today they would have to hard-code command strings and field names against prose.

#### User story

- *As an agent author*, I run `crtk schema print cli --json` once at startup, get every area/action/flag/exit-code as data, and dispatch without grepping `crtk help`. (Today [wiki/ai-agents.md](wiki/ai-agents.md) hand-maintains a prose table that can drift from [Constants.java](src/application/cli/Constants.java).)
- *As an ML pipeline builder*, before training I run `crtk record validate -i puzzles.record --strict` and get `line 4193: missing field "position"` instead of a quietly-shorter dataset. (Today every exporter does `stats.invalid++` and drops the row ŌĆö see [RecordCommands.java](src/application/cli/command/RecordCommands.java) and [RecordTrainingJsonlCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/RecordTrainingJsonlCommand.java).)
- *As a downstream tool author*, I `git`-vendor `schemas/record.v2.schema.json` and validate `.record` files with any off-the-shelf JSON Schema validator, with no Java dependency on CRTK.
- *As a CRTK maintainer*, when I change a record field I bump `schemaVersion`, regenerate the schema, and a regression test fails if the published schema and the Java emitter disagree.

#### Non-goals

- **Not** a runtime schema-validation framework injected into hot paths. Movegen/eval/search stay schema-free; validation is opt-in at I/O boundaries only.
- **Not** a third-party JSON Schema library. Validation is implemented against `utility.Json` (preserve plain `javac --release 17`, no Maven/Gradle, no deps ŌĆö [AGENTS.md](AGENTS.md), [wiki/development-notes.md](wiki/development-notes.md)).
- **Not** a typed-option DSL rewrite of every handler in this initiative. The catalog initially serializes the metadata `CliCommand` already holds; richer typed options are a *future expansion* (see below), not the MVP.
- **Not** changing the FEN/UCI/SAN validators ŌĆö those are already strict ([Fen.java](src/chess/core/Fen.java), [Move.java](src/chess/core/Move.java), [SAN.java](src/chess/core/SAN.java)) and good. We *surface* them, we don't rewrite them.
- **Not** JSON Schema draft-2020-12 conformance perfection. We target a pragmatic, validator-compatible subset (`type`, `required`, `properties`, `items`, `enum`, `const`, `additionalProperties`, `$ref` to a local `$defs`) ŌĆö enough for real validators, no remote `$ref`.

#### MVP (smallest shippable)

The smallest thing that delivers value and unblocks downstream work:

1. **`crtk schema print cli --json`** ŌĆö serialize the command tree. Reuses every field already on [CliCommand.java](src/application/cli/CliCommand.java) (`name`, `summary`, `about`, `usageTail`, `aliases`, `examples`, `conventions`, `related`, `children`, `isRunnable()`). No new metadata required for v1; flags are emitted from the existing `examples`/`usageTail` strings, clearly marked `"flagsSource":"examples"` so consumers know they are not yet typed.
2. **One published schema + one validator**: `schemas/record.v2.schema.json` (hand-written, see versioning below) and `crtk record validate -i FILE [--strict]` that streams via [RecordIO.java](src/application/cli/RecordIO.java) and reports `{ok, total, valid, invalid, errors:[{index, line, field, message}]}` ŌĆö exit 0 clean, exit 3 if any invalid and `--strict`, exit 0-with-warnings count otherwise.
3. **`schemaVersion` added to `Record`** as an *optional* field (absent ŌćÆ assumed `1`, the current implicit shape), so old `.record` files keep loading. New writes stamp `2`.

That is shippable in isolation, has its own regression test, and immediately gives agents the catalog and ML users a fail-loud validator.

#### Full version

- `crtk schema list` / `crtk schema print <name>` covering **every** formalized schema (full list below).
- A **generated** catalog that includes typed option metadata once `CliCommand` carries a declared option list (see Architecture).
- `*-validate` on each area that owns a file format (`record validate`, `puzzle validate`, `book validate`, `db validate`, `dataset validate`).
- A regression test that proves **every published schema accepts the exact bytes the corresponding Java emitter produces** (golden-output Ōåö schema agreement).
- `crtk schema check` (CI gate) that fails if a registered schema name has no file, or a file has no Java round-trip test.

#### Proposed CLI surface

Noun-then-verb, consistent with the registry grammar. New `schema` area registered in [CliRegistry.buildRoot()](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) alongside `config`, `doctor`, `version`.

```
crtk schema list [--json]
    # enumerate every formalized schema: name, version, kind (object|jsonl|catalog), file path

crtk schema print <name> [--version N] [--output|-o PATH]
    # emit the JSON Schema for <name> to stdout (or file)
    # <name> in: cli | record | tag-line | puzzle | puzzle-elo | training-jsonl
    #            | classifier-meta | lc0-meta | npy-meta | engine-analysis-row
    #            | engine-bestmove-row | analysis-delta-row | review-row
    #            | study-task | repertoire-item | db-manifest | import-manifest
    #            | dataset-manifest | book-manifest | study-manifest

crtk schema print cli [--json]
    # the machine-readable command catalog (areas/actions/flags/exit-codes/aliases)

crtk schema validate --name <name> -i FILE [--strict] [--json] [--jsonl] [-o PATH]
    # validate FILE against a named schema; per-error rows with index+field+message
    # exit 0 ok | 0 with warnings (count printed) | 3 invalid-and-strict | 2 usage

crtk schema check
    # CI self-check: every registered name has a file AND a Java round-trip test marker
```

Per-area convenience validators (thin wrappers over `schema validate`, so the area that owns the format owns the verb):

```
crtk record validate   -i FILE [--strict] [--json|--jsonl] [-o PATH]
crtk puzzle validate    -i FILE [--strict] [--json|--jsonl]
crtk book validate      -i FILE.{json,toml} [--strict]      # supplements existing --check dry-run
crtk dataset validate   -i PREFIX.meta.json [--strict]      # checks meta + referenced .npy presence/shape
```

No engine budgets are relevant here ŌĆö schema/validation commands do no search. (The existing `--max-nodes`/`--max-duration`/`--threads` budget vocabulary is untouched; this initiative does not add or remove engine flags.)

#### Proposed Workbench surface

CLI is source of truth; the Workbench mirrors it with **no second implementation** (enforced by [WorkbenchCommandRegression.java](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java)).

- Add `schema list`, `schema print <name>`, `schema validate` as **command templates** in [CommandTemplates.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java) so they appear in the Build form and the "All CLI" template (which already walks `CliRegistry.root()`). Execution stays via the child-JVM path in [CommandRunner.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java) ŌĆö the Workbench runs the real CLI, not a reimplementation.
- The **Datasets** view ([DatasetPanel] mirroring [RecordIO.java](src/application/cli/RecordIO.java)) gains a "Validate" action that shells `crtk record validate --jsonl` and renders the error rows in a table. This reuses the existing streaming reader; it does not parse independently.
- The catalog from `crtk schema print cli --json` can *optionally* back the Build-form option list in a later pass, replacing the current hand-curated option groups in [CommandTemplates.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java). Mark this future; do not make it MVP (it would couple two moving parts at once).

ASSUMPTION: the Datasets panel class is named `DatasetPanel` per the digest; verify the exact class name in `src/application/gui/workbench/dataset/` before wiring.

#### Data model / schema implications (concrete fields)

**Add `schemaVersion` to [Record.java](src/chess/struct/Record.java).** Current fixed 7-field shape:
`created` (epoch-ms long), `engine` (string), `parent` (FEN|null), `position` (FEN|null), `description` (string), `tags` (string[]), `analysis` (info-line string[]). Proposed v2:

```
{ "schemaVersion": 2, "created": <long>, "engine": <string>,
  "parent": <FEN|null>, "position": <FEN|null>,
  "description": <string>, "tags": [<string>], "analysis": [<string>] }
```

Backward-compat rule: `fromJson` treats absent `schemaVersion` as `1` and parses exactly as today. This is the *only* breaking-ish change and it is additive (`additionalProperties` was already tolerated by the hand-rolled parser).

**Record schema does NOT add game-id/provenance here** ŌĆö those belong to initiative A (DB) and I (provenance). F only formalizes what exists today plus the version field, so F can ship without waiting on A/I.

**Schemas to formalize (every one, with where its bytes come from):**

| Schema name | Kind | Source of truth (Java) |
|---|---|---|
| `cli` (catalog) | object | [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) + [CliCommand.java](src/application/cli/CliCommand.java) |
| `record` | object (array container) | [Record.java](src/chess/struct/Record.java) `toJson` |
| `tag-line` | string grammar | [Sort.java](src/chess/tag/Sort.java) `FAMILY_ORDER` + [SCHEMA.md](tag/SCHEMA.md) |
| `puzzle` (mined row) | object | [Record.java](src/chess/struct/Record.java) + `META: puzzle_*` from [Difficulty.java](src/chess/puzzle/Difficulty.java) |
| `puzzle-elo` (row) | jsonl | [PuzzleEloExporter.java](src/chess/io/PuzzleEloExporter.java) |
| `training-jsonl` (row) | jsonl | [RecordTrainingJsonlCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/RecordTrainingJsonlCommand.java) |
| `classifier-meta` | object | [ClassifierDatasetExporter.java](src/chess/io/ClassifierDatasetExporter.java) |
| `lc0-meta` | object | [RecordLc0Exporter.java](src/chess/io/RecordLc0Exporter.java) |
| `npy-meta` | object | **does not exist yet** ŌĆö [RecordDatasetExporter.java](src/chess/io/RecordDatasetExporter.java) writes no meta (coordinate with I) |
| `engine-analyze-row` | jsonl | [EngineBatchCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/EngineBatchCommand.java) analyze rows |
| `engine-bestmove-row` | jsonl | [EngineBatchCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/EngineBatchCommand.java) bestmove rows |
| `analysis-delta-row` | jsonl | [RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java) |
| `review-row` | jsonl | **new (initiative C output)** ŌĆö formalize the contract now so C builds against it |
| `study-task` | object | `position describe --format training-jsonl` schema `crtk.position_description.training.v1` ([PositionDescribeCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/PositionDescribeCommand.java)) |
| `repertoire-item` | object | **new (initiative D)** ŌĆö formalize the contract so D has a target |
| `db-manifest` | object | **new (initiative A)** ŌĆö game-store manifest |
| `import-manifest` | object | **new (initiative B, read-only import)** |
| `dataset-manifest` | object | **new (initiative I)** ŌĆö ties multi-shard exports + provenance |
| `book-manifest` | object | [Book.java](src/chess/book/model/Book.java) (JSON/TOML keys) |
| `study-manifest` | object | [StudyBook.java](src/chess/book/study/StudyBook.java) |

The five rows marked **new** are *forward declarations*: F publishes the schema file and a stub validator so A/B/C/D/I implement *against a fixed contract* instead of inventing one. This is the mechanism by which F unblocks them.

#### Hand-written vs generated-from-Java schemas

Two distinct sources, deliberately split by stability and authorship:

- **`cli` catalog: generated** at runtime by walking `CliRegistry.root()`. There is no separate file to drift; `crtk schema print cli --json` *is* the artifact. A regression asserts it round-trips and covers every runnable leaf (mirrors what [WorkbenchCommandRegression.java](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java) already does structurally).
- **Data schemas (`record`, `training-jsonl`, etc.): hand-written `.schema.json` files**, checked into `schemas/`. Hand-written, *not* generated from Java, because (a) Java has no reflection-friendly typed shape ŌĆö the emitters are hand-built `StringBuilder` JSON (e.g. [EngineBatchCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/EngineBatchCommand.java)), so there is nothing to introspect; and (b) a hand-written schema that is *tested against* the emitter's golden bytes is a genuine independent check, whereas a generated schema would just restate the emitter and catch nothing. The schema is the spec; the test enforces emitterŌåöspec agreement.

#### Where schema files live & versioning

- Location: **`schemas/<name>.v<N>.schema.json`** at repo root (sibling to `config/`, `models/`, `wiki/`). Tracked in git (unlike `models/` which is gitignored). Bundled into release tarballs by [make_release_linux_cuda.sh](scripts/make_release_linux_cuda.sh) so consumers get them offline.
- Each file declares `"$id": "crtk/<name>/v<N>"` and a top-level `"const"` `schemaVersion` where the payload carries one.
- Versioning policy: **additive changes keep the version**; any field removal/rename/type-change bumps `N` and keeps the old file. `crtk schema list` reports the current `N` per name. This matches the existing `crtk.workbench.run-manifest.v1` convention in [RunManifest.java](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java) and `crtk.position_description.training.v1` ŌĆö F generalizes that one-off pattern into a policy.
- `crtk version --json` already emits a version; add a parallel `crtk schema list --json` rather than overloading `version`.

#### How schemas interact with deterministic golden-output tests

This is the crux that makes the schemas trustworthy rather than decorative. CRTK's testing philosophy is golden values embedded in source ([wiki/quality-and-testing.md](wiki/quality-and-testing.md)). The schemas plug into that directly:

- For each data schema, the regression suite already has (or will have) a golden emitter test ŌĆö e.g. [RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest.java](src/testing/RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest.java) asserts exact JSONL field substrings. F adds: **the same golden bytes must validate against `schemas/training-jsonl.vN.schema.json`**. One assertion line per existing golden, in the in-house harness.
- This means a schema can never silently diverge from reality: if someone edits the emitter, the golden test catches the byte change AND the schema-validation assertion catches a shape change. The schema becomes a *second, independent witness* to the same determinism the project already prizes.
- Crucially this **closes a known gap**: several dataset/ML tests ([RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest.java](src/testing/RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest.java), [RecordLC0ExporterRegressionTest.java](src/testing/RecordLC0ExporterRegressionTest.java)) compile but are **not wired into [run_regression_suite.sh](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh)** today, so the ML export contracts never gate a push. F's `schema check` target and the schema-agreement assertions give a reason to wire them into the `cli`/`core` suite.

#### Architecture implications

- **No new dependency.** Validation is implemented in a new `chess.schema` (or `application.cli.schema`) package using only `utility.Json` parse helpers ([Json.java](src/utility/Json.java): `streamTopLevelObjects`, `parseStringField`, `parseLongField`, `parseStringArrayField`). The validator walks a parsed schema (itself loaded with `utility.Json`) ŌĆö a small interpreter over the pragmatic subset, not a library.
- **Catalog serialization is in `application.cli`**, since it needs `CliRegistry`/`CliCommand` which already live there and must not be imported by `chess.*` (layer rule enforced by [SourceHeaderRegressionTest.java](src/testing/SourceHeaderRegressionTest.java): `chess.*` must not import `application.*`). So `cli`-catalog emission stays out of core; data-schema validation (`record`, etc.) can live in `chess.schema` and be called from CLI.
- **Schema files are resources, not classpath-embedded.** They load from `schemas/` relative to the app home (the launcher `cd`s to `APP_HOME` per [install.sh](install.sh)); fall back to a path resolved like [Config.java](src/application/Config.java) does for `config/`. ASSUMPTION: reuse the same CWD-relative resolution; document the footgun (running `java -jar` from elsewhere loses `schemas/` just as it loses `config/`).
- **Fail-loud is opt-in, not a global behavior change.** `Record.fromJson` keeps tolerant parsing for the read path (don't break mining/export that depend on skip-bad-rows); the *new* validate commands are the strict surface. This avoids destabilizing the many tolerant readers in [Reader.java](src/chess/io/Reader.java).

#### Existing components to reuse

- [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) / [CliCommand.java](src/application/cli/CliCommand.java) ŌĆö the catalog source; already in memory, `commandPath()`/`aliasPaths()`/`isRunnable()` exist.
- [utility.Json](src/utility/Json.java) ŌĆö emit (`esc`, `stringArray`) and parse (`parseStringField`, `streamTopLevelObjects`); the only JSON primitive, keeps no-deps.
- [RecordIO.java](src/application/cli/RecordIO.java) ŌĆö JSON-array vs JSONL auto-detect streaming with byte-progress; the validate commands stream through it.
- [Record.java](src/chess/struct/Record.java) ŌĆö add `schemaVersion`, publish its shape.
- [RunManifest.java](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java) ŌĆö the existing `SCHEMA = "crtk.workbench.run-manifest.v1"` + per-file SHA-256 pattern to generalize.
- [CommandSupport.java](src/application/cli/command/CommandSupport.java) ŌĆö `OutputMode`/`resolveOutputMode` (reject `--json`+`--jsonl`), `jsonString`; reuse for the validate command's output.
- [Validation.java](src/application/cli/Validation.java) / [ConfigOps.java](src/application/cli/ConfigOps.java) ŌĆö existing numeric/config validators and the warnings-vs-errors exit-code idiom (exit 1 warnings, 2 errors) to mirror.
- [WorkbenchCommandRegression.java](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java) ŌĆö the registry-walking test to extend so the catalog covers every leaf.

#### Files/packages likely affected

- New: `src/application/cli/command/SchemaCommand.java` (the `schema` area handlers + catalog serializer).
- New: `src/chess/schema/` package ŌĆö `JsonSchema.java` (load), `Validator.java` (interpret subset), `Schemas.java` (registry of nameŌåÆfile). (Layer-safe: no `application.*` import.)
- New: `schemas/*.v*.schema.json` (all formalized schemas).
- Edit: [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) (register `schema` area; add `record validate`, `puzzle validate`, `book validate`, `dataset validate` leaves).
- Edit: [Record.java](src/chess/struct/Record.java) (add `schemaVersion`, default-1 on read, write 2).
- Edit: [RecordCommands.java](src/application/cli/command/RecordCommands.java) (wire `record validate`).
- Edit: [CommandTemplates.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java) (mirror templates).
- Edit: [run_regression_suite.sh](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh) (add `schema` to a suite; wire the currently-dead ML export tests).
- Edit: [Constants.java](src/application/cli/Constants.java) (`CMD_SCHEMA`, `OPT_NAME`, etc.).

#### Testing plan (in-house harness style ŌĆö `main()` + `testing.TestSupport`)

- `SchemaCatalogRegressionTest.java`: walk `CliRegistry.root()`; assert `crtk schema print cli --json` (via `TestSupport.runMain`) emits one entry per runnable leaf, every entry has `name`+`summary`, and parsed JSON round-trips through `utility.Json`. Mirrors the coverage assertion in [WorkbenchCommandRegression.java](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java).
- `SchemaValidatorRegressionTest.java`: hand-built valid + invalid objects for the subset (`required` missing, wrong `type`, bad `enum`); assert error `field`/`message`/`index` exactly.
- `SchemaAgreementRegressionTest.java` (the important one): for each data schema, take the golden bytes a real emitter produces (call the emitter, capture stdout via `TestSupport.captureStdout`/`runMain`) and assert they **validate clean** against `schemas/<name>.vN.schema.json`. Wire alongside the existing [RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest.java](src/testing/RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest.java) and [RecordLC0ExporterRegressionTest.java](src/testing/RecordLC0ExporterRegressionTest.java) (which this PR finally adds to the runner).
- `RecordSchemaVersionRegressionTest.java`: a v1 (`schemaVersion` absent) file still loads; a v2 round-trips; `record validate --strict` on a corrupted row exits 3 with the right line number.
- CLI surface coverage added to [CLICommandRegressionTest.java](src/testing/CLICommandRegressionTest.java): `schema list`, `schema print <name>`, conflicting `--json`+`--jsonl` rejected with exit 2, `--strict` exit codes.

#### Docs plan

- New `wiki/schemas.md`: the schema catalog, versioning policy, where files live, the subset supported, and how to validate offline with a third-party validator.
- Update [wiki/ai-agents.md](wiki/ai-agents.md): replace the hand-maintained command table with "run `crtk schema print cli --json`"; document `record validate` for pre-flight checks. This directly addresses the empty `.agents` directory / no-machine-catalog gap the digest flags.
- Update [wiki/outputs-and-logs.md](wiki/outputs-and-logs.md): cross-link each documented output format to its schema name.
- Update [wiki/datasets.md](wiki/datasets.md): point the (currently overstated) determinism/provenance claims at the new validate command and the dataset schemas.
- Update [tag/SCHEMA.md](tag/SCHEMA.md): note it is now backed by `schemas/tag-line.vN.schema.json` (and, per the tag digest, register the dynamic MOVE_EFFECT/LINE/VARIATION/GAME families ŌĆö coordinate with the Tag Engine work).

#### Risks / tradeoffs

- **Subset validator scope creep.** A from-scratch JSON Schema interpreter can balloon toward full draft-2020-12. Mitigation: freeze the supported subset in `wiki/schemas.md` and reject unsupported keywords loudly in `schema check` so we never ship a schema we can't actually enforce.
- **Hand-written schema drift.** A schema can lie if the agreement test is missing. Mitigation: `schema check` fails CI if any registered name lacks a Java round-trip test marker ŌĆö no schema ships without a witness.
- **Tolerant-vs-strict split confusion.** Two behaviors (read=tolerant, validate=strict) for the same file could surprise users. Mitigation: document explicitly; `record validate` is the *only* strict path; readers keep skipping bad rows with a printed count.
- **CWD-relative `schemas/` footgun.** Same class of bug as the existing `config/`/`models/` relative-path issue ([wiki/configuration.md](wiki/configuration.md)). Mitigation: resolve via the same app-home logic and document it; `crtk doctor` should check `schemas/` presence (small add).
- **Forward-declared schemas (review/repertoire/db/import/dataset) may guess wrong** before A/C/D/I exist. Mitigation: ship them at v1 explicitly marked "provisional" in `schema list`; bumping to v2 when the owning initiative lands is expected and cheap.

#### Acceptance criteria (checkable)

- [ ] `crtk schema list --json` enumerates Ōēź 20 named schemas with `name`/`version`/`kind`.
- [ ] `crtk schema print cli --json` emits an entry for **every** runnable leaf in `CliRegistry.root()` (asserted by a registry-walking test).
- [ ] `schemas/record.v2.schema.json` exists and validates the exact bytes `Record.toJson` produces for a fixture (asserted in `SchemaAgreementRegressionTest`).
- [ ] `crtk record validate -i <good>` exits 0; `-i <corrupt> --strict` exits 3 and prints the offending index/line/field.
- [ ] A v1 `.record` (no `schemaVersion`) still loads byte-for-byte as before (no regression in mining/export goldens).
- [ ] Every formalized data schema has a corresponding agreement test, and `crtk schema check` passes.
- [ ] [RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest.java](src/testing/RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest.java) and [RecordLC0ExporterRegressionTest.java](src/testing/RecordLC0ExporterRegressionTest.java) are now invoked by [run_regression_suite.sh](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh).
- [ ] No new third-party dependency; `javac --release 17` clean build unchanged.
- [ ] Workbench "All CLI" template includes `schema list`/`print`/`validate` (asserted by [WorkbenchCommandRegression.java](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java)).

#### Future expansion

- **Typed option metadata on `CliCommand`** (declared flag list with names/types/enums/exclusive-groups), so the catalog stops emitting `"flagsSource":"examples"` and becomes fully precise. This also lets [CommandTemplates.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java) and [HelpCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/HelpCommand.java) be *generated* from one model, killing the three-source drift (registry / 83 KB embedded help / [wiki/command-reference.md](wiki/command-reference.md)).
- **Catalog feeds the SDK (E)**: generate Python/TS client stubs from `schema print cli --json`.
- **Catalog feeds editor tooling (K)**: VSCode completion and a Jupyter wrapper consume the catalog + output schemas.
- **Richer exit-code taxonomy** surfaced as schema metadata (today code 2 is overloaded across 84/88 failure sites ŌĆö the catalog could declare per-command exit codes so callers distinguish usage from engine-unavailable).

**Timeline:** MVP is short-term (catalog + record schema + record validate + schemaVersion). Full version is medium-term and naturally tracks A/C/I as their schemas firm up.

---

### 8G. Grounded explanation layer (and Section 14 detail)

**Initiative G ŌĆö verdict: build-later ┬Ę priority P1 ┬Ę complexity medium ┬Ę term medium-term ┬Ę depends on: C (game-review-to-study router), F (schemas/validation), light reuse of I (provenance).**

This is the project's single most-protected value ŌĆö "grounded (non-hallucinated) explanations" is in the core-preserve list ŌĆö and it is the one theme the fact-check rated `present` rather than `partial`/`absent`. So the work here is *deepening and hardening an existing, real capability*, not greenfield. The most important new artifact is not a model: it is a **verifier** that makes "grounded" enforceable rather than aspirational. Today, grounding is enforced only *by construction* in the classical generator ([ARCHITECTURE.md](src/chess/describe/ARCHITECTURE.md) self-scores truthfulness ~9.5/10), and the verification pass that would protect a future model is documented but **unimplemented** ([ARCHITECTURE.md](src/chess/describe/ARCHITECTURE.md) lines 157ŌĆō158: "Add a grounding/verification pass at inference ŌĆ” not yet coded").

#### Goal
