Turn CRTK's scattered, faithful-by-construction explanation surfaces (`position describe`, `fen text`, `puzzle text`, `fen relations`) into one coherent **`crtk explain`** area that:

1. emits a **machine-readable rationale** (a structured set of verified facts) *separately* from human prose, so downstream tools consume facts and humans read sentences;
2. **always** has a deterministic prose path that cannot hallucinate (the existing classical generator), and *optionally* layers model-assisted prose on top;
3. runs every piece of generated prose ŌĆö classical or model ŌĆö through a **verifier** that rejects ungrounded claims (illegal/unplayable moves, fabricated opening names, unproven "only move", impossible captures, wrong side-to-move, eval sign contradictions) and falls back to the deterministic text on any violation;
4. adapts to **audience** (beginner / club / advanced / coach / researcher / engine-debug / ml) without changing the underlying facts ŌĆö audience controls *which* facts and *what register*, never *whether* a claim is true;
5. explains not just a position but a **move**, a **game**, a **puzzle**, and a **review** unit (the output of initiative C).

#### User story

- *Club player:* "I lost this game; tell me where it went wrong and why, in language I understand." ŌåÆ `crtk explain game --pgn loss.pgn --audience club` ŌåÆ narrated turning points with grounded reasons, each traceable to an engine eval delta or a proven tactic.
- *Researcher / ML:* "Give me the structured rationale, not prose, for 50k positions, so I can train a captioner." ŌåÆ `crtk explain position --input fens.txt --format jsonl --facts-only` ŌåÆ one JSON object per line, every claim carrying a `grounded_by` provenance pointer.
- *Engine-debug:* "Why did the search pick this move and call the position +1.3?" ŌåÆ `crtk explain move --fen ... --uci e2e4 --audience engine-debug --engine builtin --max-nodes 2000000` ŌåÆ the eval, the PV, the SEE of the capture, the proven/unproven mate status, with no interpretive gloss.
- *Coach authoring a book:* model-assisted fluent prose that is *guaranteed* not to invent an opening name or a sacrifice.

#### Non-goals

- **Not** a chatbot / free-form Q&A. The input is always a position, move, game, or review unit; the output is bounded explanation.
- **Not** "understanding." [ARCHITECTURE.md](src/chess/describe/ARCHITECTURE.md) is explicit: the classical path "describes the position rather than understanding it." We deepen the *why* using tags + SEE + MateProver + PV, but we do not claim strategic reasoning the tags cannot support.
- **Not** shipping T5 weights. No trained position/description weights exist; [T5PositionDescriptionGenerator.java](src/chess/describe/T5PositionDescriptionGenerator.java) `available()` is hard-`false` and `generate()` throws. The model path stays optional and absent-by-default.
- **Not** an opening *theory* engine. ECO labeling is bounded to exact/transposition lookup from the bundled book; no line evaluation or "best move in the Najdorf."
- **Not** introducing any third-party dependency. Plain `javac --release 17`, no Maven/Gradle.

#### MVP (smallest shippable)

The MVP is the **verifier + the `explain position` / `explain move` verbs + facts/prose separation**, reusing the existing classical generator unchanged as the prose source. No model required.

1. **`chess.explain.Verifier`** (new package `chess.explain`): takes a `Position`, a structured rationale, and a prose string; returns `Verdict{grounded:boolean, violations:[Violation]}`. Checks:
   - every SAN/UCI mentioned is a legal move from the position (route through [MoveGenerator](src/chess/core/MoveGenerator.java) + [SAN.fromAlgebraic](src/chess/core/SAN.java));
   - any "captures X" claim names a piece actually on the destination square (or the en-passant pawn) per [Position](src/chess/core/Position.java);
   - any opening name appears only if [Encyclopedia.name(pos)](src/chess/eco/Encyclopedia.java) returns it (no fabricated names; empty for Chess960);
   - any "mate in N" claim is backed by a [MateProver](src/chess/engine/MateProver.java) `Proof` (proven, not estimated);
   - any "only move" claim is backed by structured evidence (see *Data model*), else downgraded;
   - declared side-to-move / eval-sign match the [PositionDescriptionInput.Evaluation](src/chess/describe/PositionDescriptionInput.java).
2. **`chess.explain.Rationale`**: the machine-readable fact list (schema below), built from [PositionDescriptionExtractor](src/chess/describe/PositionDescriptionExtractor.java) output + tags + optional engine eval.
3. **`crtk explain position`** and **`crtk explain move`**: classical prose + rationale, run through the verifier, `--facts-only` to suppress prose. These are thin re-homings of the existing [PositionDescribeCommand](src/application/cli/command/PositionDescribeCommand.java) logic plus the rationale/verifier.
4. **Audience** flag wired to the classical generator's existing `--detail` mechanism initially (beginnerŌēłbrief+glossed, researcherŌēłfacts-only); full register tuning is Full-version.

MVP deliberately leaves `explain game`/`explain puzzle`/`explain review` and any model path out ŌĆö those depend on C and on the verifier existing first.

#### Full version

- **`crtk explain game`** ŌĆö narrate a whole game by walking the mainline, calling `explain move` per ply, and selecting turning points from eval deltas. Reuses [GameAnalyzer](src/chess/tag/game/GameAnalyzer.java) / [LineAnalyzer](src/chess/tag/game/LineAnalyzer.java) and `fen tags --analyze-game` machinery in [TagsCommand](src/application/cli/command/TagsCommand.java).
- **`crtk explain review`** ŌĆö explain a *study unit* produced by initiative C (mistake ŌåÆ refutation), so the explanation and the routed puzzle share one rationale. Hard dependency on C.
- **`crtk explain puzzle`** ŌĆö supersede the current [PuzzleTextCommand](src/application/cli/command/PuzzleTextCommand.java) free-text path with a verified one (the existing one runs the T5 over PV lines with *no* grounding check).
- **Model-assisted prose**: when `--model` is supplied, run the working [chess.nn.t5.Runner](src/chess/nn/t5/Runner.java) (NOT the dead describe-package stub) with the [TagPrompt](src/chess/nn/t5/TagPrompt.java) "Do not invent moves" instruction, then verify; on any violation, **regenerate once, else fall back to classical**. This finally wires the *working* tag-to-text T5 into `explain`, resolving the dual-T5 confusion the digest flags (two unrelated "T5"s, one dead stub, one working runner).
- **Full audience register matrix** (7 audiences) with per-audience fact-selection + lexicon profiles.
- **"Why/plan" sentences**: turn the strategic tags already collected but never spoken (KingSafety, pawn Structure, passers, outposts) into grounded clauses ŌĆö the headline gap in [ARCHITECTURE.md](src/chess/describe/ARCHITECTURE.md) ("states verdicts but never causation").

#### Proposed CLI surface (noun-then-verb)

All under a new area `explain`. Position selection (`--fen` / `--input` / `--startpos` / `--stdin`), output mode (`--format text|json|jsonl|training-jsonl`), and engine budgets follow existing CLI conventions ([CommandSupport](src/application/cli/command/CommandSupport.java), [EngineOps](src/application/cli/EngineOps.java)).

```
crtk explain position
    --fen "<FEN>" | --input <file> | --startpos | --stdin
    --audience beginner|club|advanced|coach|researcher|engine-debug|ml   (default: club)
    --detail brief|normal|full                                          (default: normal)
    --eval static|engine                                                (default: static)
    --eval-depth N                  (engine eval; implies --eval engine; clamped 1..MAX_DEPTH)
    --max-nodes N                   (engine eval node cap; default 1_500_000 per EngineEvaluator)
    --facts-only                    (suppress prose; emit rationale only)
    --model <path.bin>              (optional model-assisted prose; verified, falls back)
    --max-new N                     (model token budget; default 128)
    --strict-grounding              (exit 3 instead of silent fallback when prose fails verify)
    --format text|json|jsonl|training-jsonl
    -o, --output <file>

crtk explain move
    --fen "<FEN>" (--uci <move> | --san <move>)
    --audience ...   --detail ...
    --engine builtin|external       (default: none -> static rationale)
    --evaluator classical|nnue|lc0|otis     (builtin)
    -P, --protocol-path <toml>      (external UCI)
    --max-nodes N  --max-duration <Ns>  --multipv N  --threads N  --hash N
    --facts-only  --model <path>  --strict-grounding  --format ...

crtk explain game
    --pgn <file> [--mainline | --sidelines]  [--game-id <id>]
    --audience ...  --turning-points-only
    --engine external -P <toml> --max-nodes N --max-duration <Ns> --multipv N --threads N
    --format text|json|jsonl  -o <file>

crtk explain puzzle
    --fen "<FEN>" | --input <records>
    --multipv N --pv-plies N --max-nodes N --max-duration <Ns>
    --audience ...  --model <path>  --strict-grounding  --format ...

crtk explain review
    --input <study-units.jsonl>     (output of initiative C)
    --audience ...  --format ...  -o <file>
```

Notes:
- **Engine budgets are always explicit** and never hidden: `--max-nodes`/`--max-duration`/`--depth`/`--threads`/`--multipv`/`--hash`, matching the in-house engine and external-UCI contracts. Static is the default for `explain position` (reproducible from FEN alone); engine eval is opt-in.
- The legacy `position describe` (alias `text`) is **kept as an alias** of `explain position` for one release, then deprecated in help ŌĆö avoids breaking existing scripts and the Workbench Describe tab while consolidating.

#### Proposed Workbench surface (mirrors CLI, no second implementation)

The Workbench already mirrors the CLI via [CommandRunner](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java) (spawns `application.Main` in a child JVM ŌĆö the *real* CLI) and [CommandTemplates](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java). The existing [PositionDescriptionPanel](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PositionDescriptionPanel.java) becomes the **Explain inspector**:

- Audience dropdown, detail, eval-toggle, model-path, strict-grounding checkbox ŌĆö each maps 1:1 to a CLI flag; the live command preview shows the exact `crtk explain ŌĆ”` invocation (no UI-only defaults the CLI can't reproduce ŌĆö enforced by [WorkbenchCommandRegression](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java)).
- A two-pane view: **Facts** (the rationale table, copyable) and **Prose** (the verified text), making facts-vs-prose separation visible.
- Verifier violations surface as a non-blocking banner ("model output rejected, showing deterministic text") so the GUI never silently shows what the CLI would reject.
- `fen relations` stays the visual grounding companion ([PositionRelationsCommand](src/application/cli/command/PositionRelationsCommand.java)); the Explain inspector links to it.

Add an Explain mode to the Review surface (initiative C) that calls `explain review` so a reviewed mistake's narration is the same code path as the CLI.

#### Data model / schema implications (concrete)

Two new contracts in `chess.explain`, both published as JSON Schema under initiative F.

**`Rationale`** (the machine-readable facts; `schema: "crtk.explain.rationale.v1"`):

```jsonc
{
  "schema": "crtk.explain.rationale.v1",
  "fen": "<normalized FEN>",
  "side_to_move": "white|black",
  "status": "normal|check|checkmate|stalemate|insufficient material",
  "phase": "opening|middlegame|endgame",          // honest label; see risk on phase
  "evaluation": { "source": "classical-static|engine-d10|external:<name>",
                  "cp_white": 0, "mate_in": 0, "wdl": null },
  "opening": { "eco": "B90", "name": "Sicilian, Najdorf" } | null,  // only if Encyclopedia returns it
  "facts": [
    { "id": "f1", "kind": "material|king_safety|tactic|threat|candidate|mate|opening|pawn_structure",
      "claim": "white is up an exchange",
      "grounded_by": { "source": "tag", "ref": "MATERIAL: balance=..." },   // tag | see | mateprover | eco | engine_eval | movegen
      "confidence": "proven|measured|heuristic" },
    { "id": "f2", "kind": "tactic", "claim": "Nxe5 wins material",
      "grounded_by": { "source": "see", "ref": "see=+320" }, "uci": "f3e5", "san": "Nxe5",
      "confidence": "measured" }
  ],
  "only_move": { "uci": "...", "evidence": "mateprover|multipv_gap", "second_best_cp": -450 } | null
}
```

**`Explanation`** (`schema: "crtk.explain.explanation.v1"`): wraps the rationale plus prose + the verifier verdict.

```jsonc
{
  "schema": "crtk.explain.explanation.v1",
  "audience": "club",
  "prose": "White is up the exchange; ...",
  "prose_source": "classical|model-verified|classical-fallback",
  "grounded": true,
  "violations": [],     // populated when model prose was rejected
  "rationale": { /* crtk.explain.rationale.v1 */ }
}
```

Reuse the existing [PositionDescriptionInput](src/chess/describe/PositionDescriptionInput.java) JSON verbatim as the `rationale.evaluation`/`material`/`moves`/`candidates` substrate ŌĆö it is already serializable and stable. The `training-jsonl` format extends today's `crtk.position_description.training.v1` (the digest confirms `target == classical_text` only) with a `rationale` field so a future captioner can learn factŌåÆprose, not just textŌåÆtext.

#### Architecture implications

- **New package `chess.explain`** in the dependency-free core layer: `Rationale`, `Explanation`, `Verifier`, `RationaleBuilder`, `Audience` enum, `ExplanationGenerator`. It may import `chess.core`, `chess.tag`, `chess.eval`, `chess.engine`, `chess.eco`, `chess.describe`, `chess.nn.t5` ŌĆö but **must not** import `application.*` or `testing.*` (enforced by [SourceHeaderRegressionTest](src/testing/SourceHeaderRegressionTest.java)).
- **Deterministic fallback is structural, not optional.** `ExplanationGenerator.generate()` always computes the classical prose first; the model path, if present, is a *replacement candidate* that must pass the verifier or it is discarded. This guarantees the no-hallucination value holds even with a buggy/garbage model.
- **The only optional dependency is the model file**, isolated exactly as today: the working runtime is the in-process, no-deps [chess.nn.t5.Runner](src/chess/nn/t5/Runner.java) (its own `.bin` loader, tokenizer, CPU greedy decode). No weights ship; absence is a first-class state (`available()==false` ŌåÆ classical path, no error).
- **Kill the dead stub confusion**: deprecate/remove [chess.describe.T5PositionDescriptionGenerator](src/chess/describe/T5PositionDescriptionGenerator.java) (permanently `available()==false`) and route `--model` to the working `chess.nn.t5` runner via the explain layer, so there is one model path, not two.
- **Determinism**: classical prose is a pure function of the structured input (no RNG/clock ŌĆö already true). Engine-eval enrichment uses the deterministic single-thread, fixed-depth, node-capped [EngineEvaluator](src/chess/describe/EngineEvaluator.java) (`DEFAULT_DEPTH=10`, `NODE_CAP=1_500_000`). Model-assisted prose is deterministic only under `--threads 1` greedy decode with a fixed model; this is documented, not asserted byte-equal across machines.

#### Existing components to reuse (real files)

- [ClassicalPositionDescriptionGenerator.java](src/chess/describe/ClassicalPositionDescriptionGenerator.java) ŌĆö the faithful prose engine; extend for "why" clauses and audience register.
- [PositionDescriptionExtractor.java](src/chess/describe/PositionDescriptionExtractor.java) / [PositionDescriptionInput.java](src/chess/describe/PositionDescriptionInput.java) ŌĆö structured signals (already collect the unused strategic tags).
- [DescriptionLexicon.java](src/chess/describe/DescriptionLexicon.java) ŌĆö deterministic word/number/list helpers; basis for per-audience lexicon profiles.
- [EngineEvaluator.java](src/chess/describe/EngineEvaluator.java) ŌĆö deterministic verdict correction + `mateIn`.
- [chess.nn.t5.Runner.java](src/chess/nn/t5/Runner.java) + [TagPrompt.java](src/chess/nn/t5/TagPrompt.java) ŌĆö the *working* tag-to-text path to wire in.
- [Generator.java](src/chess/tag/Generator.java) (`tags(Position[, Evaluator][, Analysis])`) ŌĆö grounded fact source.
- [See.java](src/chess/eval/See.java) ŌĆö `see()`/`seeGreaterEqual()` to ground "wins material" claims with a number.
- [MateProver.java](src/chess/engine/MateProver.java) ŌĆö proven mate evidence for "mate in N" and "only move".
- [Encyclopedia.java](src/chess/eco/Encyclopedia.java) ŌĆö `name(pos)`/`eco(pos)` as the *sole* source of opening names (verifier rejects any other).
- [SAN.java](src/chess/core/SAN.java) / [MoveGenerator.java](src/chess/core/MoveGenerator.java) ŌĆö legality + capture-target checks for the verifier.
- [PositionRelationsCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/PositionRelationsCommand.java) ŌĆö visual grounding companion.

#### Files / packages likely affected

- **New:** `src/chess/explain/{Rationale,Explanation,Verifier,RationaleBuilder,Audience,ExplanationGenerator}.java`, `src/chess/explain/package-info.java`.
- **New CLI:** `src/application/cli/command/ExplainCommand.java` (+ helpers); register `explain` area + 5 actions in [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java); add tokens to [Constants.java](src/application/cli/Constants.java).
- **Modified:** [PositionDescribeCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/PositionDescribeCommand.java) (alias-delegate to explain), [PuzzleTextCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/PuzzleTextCommand.java) / [TagTextCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/TagTextCommand.java) (route through verifier).
- **Workbench:** [PositionDescriptionPanel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PositionDescriptionPanel.java) ŌåÆ Explain inspector; [CommandTemplates.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java) add explain templates.
- **Schema/docs (initiative F):** `crtk.explain.rationale.v1` + `crtk.explain.explanation.v1` JSON Schema files; extend `crtk help --json` catalog.
- **Deprecate:** [T5PositionDescriptionGenerator.java](src/chess/describe/T5PositionDescriptionGenerator.java).

#### Testing plan (in-house harness; resistant to prose brittleness)

The hard rule from [quality-and-testing.md](wiki/quality-and-testing.md): tests pin *what CRTK does*. We do **not** assert exact sentences (that is brittle and the digest already flags golden-string fragility). Tests assert **the verifier and the facts**, not the prose wording.

New `src/testing/ExplainRegressionTest.java` (plain `main`, `testing.TestSupport.*`):

- `testVerifierRejectsIllegalMove` ŌĆö feed a rationale/prose naming an illegal SAN; assert `grounded==false` with an `ILLEGAL_MOVE` violation.
- `testVerifierRejectsFabricatedOpening` ŌĆö prose names "Najdorf" but `Encyclopedia.name` returns null; assert rejection.
- `testVerifierRejectsImpossibleCapture` ŌĆö "Nxe5" where e5 is empty and not EP; assert rejection.
- `testVerifierRejectsUnprovenOnlyMove` ŌĆö "only move" with no MateProver/multipv evidence; assert downgrade/violation.
- `testVerifierRejectsEvalSignContradiction` ŌĆö prose says "Black is winning", eval `cp_white=+600`; assert rejection.
- `testClassicalAlwaysPassesVerifier` ŌĆö over a fixture set of FENs (incl. mate-in-one, stalemate, insufficient material, Chess960, malformed-then-skipped), the classical prose **always** verifies `grounded==true`. This is the core invariant.
- `testModelAbsentFallsBackSilently` ŌĆö `--model` path with no/garbage model ŌåÆ `prose_source == "classical-fallback"`, exit 0 (unless `--strict-grounding`).
- `testFactsOnlyOmitsProse` and `testRationaleFieldsGroundedBy` ŌĆö every fact has a non-null `grounded_by.source` from the allowed enum.
- `testEngineEvalDeterministicRepeat` ŌĆö same FEN + `--eval engine --eval-depth 8` twice ŌåÆ identical rationale eval (reuses the determinism pattern already in `CLICommandRegressionTest.testPositionDescribeEngineEval`).
- `testChess960NoOpeningNoCrash` ŌĆö 960 FEN ŌåÆ `opening: null`, no exception.

Wire `ExplainRegressionTest` into the `core`/`cli` targets of [run_regression_suite.sh](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh) (and CI) ŌĆö explicitly avoiding the digest's "six unwired tests rot" failure mode. The verifier tests are the regression backbone; prose is sampled only for non-emptiness and audience-length bands, never exact strings.

#### Docs plan

- New `wiki/explain.md` ŌĆö the `crtk explain` area, the facts-vs-prose contract, the audience matrix, the grounding guarantee, and the "T5 absent ŌåÆ classical" behavior.
- Update [wiki/t5.md](wiki/t5.md) ŌĆö clarify the *one* working model path and that `explain` verifies model output (resolve the dual-T5 confusion).
- Update [src/chess/describe/ARCHITECTURE.md](src/chess/describe/ARCHITECTURE.md) ŌĆö mark the verification pass as *implemented* (it currently says "not yet coded").
- Update [wiki/ai-agents.md](wiki/ai-agents.md) and `wiki/outputs-and-logs.md` ŌĆö the two new JSON schemas + exit-code semantics (`--strict-grounding` ŌåÆ exit 3 on ungrounded prose).
- Update [wiki/workbench.md](wiki/workbench.md) ŌĆö Explain inspector.

#### Risks / tradeoffs

- **Phase label is honestly-wrong.** `phase` is a crude material-ratio bucket ([ARCHITECTURE.md](src/chess/describe/ARCHITECTURE.md): a developed middlegame can read "opening"). The verifier must **not** treat phase as a hard claim, or it will reject the classical generator's own faithful output. Mitigation: phase is `heuristic` confidence and excluded from hard verification.
- **"Only move" is the hardest claim to ground cheaply.** A true only-move proof needs either a MateProver `Proof` or a multipv gap from a real engine ŌĆö both require a budget. Default behavior: never assert "only move" without that evidence; downgrade to "the natural choice."
- **Verifier false-negatives on legitimate interpretive framing.** [ARCHITECTURE.md](src/chess/describe/ARCHITECTURE.md) notes "general chess truth" clauses ("an edge that rarely survives accurate play"). The verifier checks *position-specific* claims (moves, captures, openings, eval, mate, side), not general aphorisms; over-strict matching would reject good classical prose. Mitigation: verifier operates on extracted claim tokens, not whole sentences; classical prose is whitelisted at the claim level by construction.
- **Model determinism is environment-sensitive.** Greedy CPU decode is deterministic per-machine but the digest warns model outputs vary; we never assert byte-equality of model prose and we always have the deterministic fallback.
- **Scope creep into "understanding."** The "why/plan" sentences must stay tag-grounded; a plan clause is only emitted when a backing tag (KingSafety/Structure/passer/outpost) exists, never invented.
- **Engine-debug audience can leak non-reproducible numbers** if it surfaces external-engine node counts; mark such facts `source: external` and exclude from `training-jsonl`.

#### Acceptance criteria (checkable)

- [ ] `crtk explain position --fen <any-legal-FEN>` emits prose + a `crtk.explain.rationale.v1` object; every fact has a valid `grounded_by.source`.
- [ ] The verifier rejects each of: illegal move, fabricated opening, impossible capture, unproven only-move, eval-sign contradiction (5 passing regression tests).
- [ ] Classical prose verifies `grounded==true` on the full fixture set (incl. Chess960, mate, stalemate) ŌĆö invariant test green.
- [ ] With no model, `--model` falls back to classical with `prose_source=="classical-fallback"`, exit 0; with `--strict-grounding`, ungrounded model prose causes exit 3.
- [ ] `--facts-only --format jsonl` over a multi-FEN file emits one rationale per line, no prose.
- [ ] Workbench Explain inspector's command preview equals the runnable `crtk explain ŌĆ”` (WorkbenchCommandRegression passes).
- [ ] `position describe` still works as an alias for one release.
- [ ] `ExplainRegressionTest` is wired into `core`/`cli`/CI (not orphaned).
- [ ] Opening names appear in output **only** when `Encyclopedia.name` returns them.

#### Future expansion

- **`explain review`** as the bridge to initiative D (repertoire/SRS): a verified explanation becomes the front of an SRS card.
- A trained captioner (future, external [chess-nn-playground]) learning `rationale ŌåÆ prose` from the `training-jsonl` fact field, then run *only* behind the verifier ŌĆö the safe way to add fluency without risking grounding.
- Per-audience evaluation harness comparing classical vs verified-model prose on a held-out fixture (factual recall, not BLEU).
- Cross-link explanations into the book/PDF pipeline so published annotations carry the same grounding guarantee.

---

### 8H. Workbench productization (and Section 10 redesign detail)

**Theme:** H ŌĆö Workbench productization
**Verdict:** build-later (deepen, do not expand) ┬Ę **Priority:** P2 ┬Ę **Complexity:** large ┬Ę **Dependencies:** A (local PGN database), C (game-review-to-study router), F (machine-readable command catalog + schemas)

The single most important judgment in this section: the Workbench is already the most-developed and most-funded surface in the repo, and continuing to pour P0/P1 effort into UI polish is the wrong altitude while A/C/F (the actual study/research mission) are absent. This section therefore frames H as a **beneficiary** of A/C/F/G, not a competitor for the same budget. The work below is mostly *reorganization, persona framing, and CLI-mirror hardening* ŌĆö explicitly **not** a UI rewrite.

---

#### Goal

Make the Workbench a coherent "chess research instrument" (the design guide's stated North Star, [workbench-design-guide.md](wiki/workbench-design-guide.md):56) that (1) presents the existing capabilities through task-shaped persona modes instead of a feature menu, (2) gains a first-run flow that routes a new user to their job in one click, (3) absorbs the new CLI capabilities from A/C/F automatically through the existing CLI-mirroring machinery, and (4) closes the structural/coverage debt that the current regression net misses ŌĆö all without forking a second chess implementation or adding a third-party dependency.

#### User story

> As a returning student, I open the desktop app, see a calm dashboard with my current position and recent runs, pick "Beginner Review," drop in a PGN, and get a guided walk through my mistakes with grounded explanations ŌĆö never once typing a `crtk` command, but able to see the exact command that produced every result and copy it.

> As an ML researcher, I open the same app, switch to "Research / ML," point Datasets at an export, see label skew immediately, and build the exact `record dataset lc0 --weights ŌĆ”` command with explicit budgets visible in the preview before I run it.

#### Non-goals

- **No UI rewrite.** The 13ŌåÆ6 surface consolidation already shipped (`ViewRegistry` with 8 registered views: Dashboard, Board, Run, Datasets, Publish, Engine Lab, Console, Logs ŌĆö [WindowLifecycle.java](src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowLifecycle.java):1026-1056). We reorganize and label; we do not rebuild.
- **No second chess engine/core in the GUI.** Board/Play/Relations run in-process through the one shared `chess.core`; everything that *executes a command* shells out to the real CLI (`application.Main`) via [CommandRunner.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java):505-511. This invariant is load-bearing and is hardened, not relaxed.
- **No plugin/docking framework.** Explicitly a non-goal in the existing roadmap ([TODO.txt](TODO.txt):632) and a rejected theme (L). Persona modes are *presets over existing views*, not extension points.
- **No hidden GUI-only defaults.** The design guide bans this ([workbench-design-guide.md](wiki/workbench-design-guide.md):1190); the command preview must equal the runnable command.
- **No online/social/cloud surfaces.** Hard product boundary.

---

#### What already exists vs. what needs reorg

This matters because the digest shows H is `present`, and a naive plan would re-spec shipped work. Concrete inventory:

| Capability | Status | Real file |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Registry-driven 8-view shell | **Exists** | [WindowLifecycle.java](src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowLifecycle.java):1026-1056 (`ViewRegistry`, `RegisteredView`) |
| Board surface with Analyze/Play/Solve/Relations/Draw modes | **Exists** | [WindowBoardLayer.java](src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowBoardLayer.java):280-285 (`SwitchedWorkspace`/`WorkspaceMode`) |
| Board detail tabs Moves/Tags/ECO/Review/Study/Endgame/Raw/Editor | **Exists** | [WindowBoardLayer.java](src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowBoardLayer.java):1170-1177 |
| Command builder + ~25 templates + "All CLI" | **Exists** | [CommandTemplates.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java):95-120 |
| Child-JVM CLI execution (the mirror) | **Exists** | [CommandRunner.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java):505-511 |
| Run manifest with SHA-256 provenance (`crtk.workbench.run-manifest.v1`) | **Exists** | [RunManifest.java](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java):29 |
| In-memory PGN explorer (index/filter/dedupe) | **Exists, in-memory only** | [PgnExplorerModel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java):38-124 (all `static`, no persistence) |
| Game review panel | **Exists** | [GameReviewPanel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/GameReviewPanel.java) |
| ECO explorer, tablebase, study author, puzzle library | **Exists** | `game/EcoExplorerPanel.java`, `game/TablebasePanel.java`, `game/StudyAuthorPanel.java`, `game/PuzzleLibrary.java` |
| Dashboard with session/health/jobs/artifacts | **Exists** | [DashboardPanel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/dashboard/DashboardPanel.java) + [DashboardActions.java](src/application/gui/workbench/dashboard/DashboardActions.java) |

**What needs reorg (no new surfaces):**

1. **Persona framing** ŌĆö none exists. `grep -niE "persona|beginner|coach|onboarding|first-run"` across `WindowLifecycle.java` and [Defaults.java](src/application/gui/workbench/Defaults.java) returns zero persona hits (only one "first-run" *comment* in Defaults.java:8). The shell exposes raw surfaces; personas are a labeling/preset layer on top.
2. **First-run flow** ŌĆö none exists. The design guide *bans* a hero banner ([workbench-design-guide.md](wiki/workbench-design-guide.md):119), so onboarding must be a quiet, dismissible card grid on the Dashboard, not a splash.
3. **Dashboard cards ŌåÆ live deep-links** ŌĆö the TODO's own UX-redesign leftovers (live MCTS root-move grid, PublishŌåÆshared run-output bus, clickable Dashboard cards) are deferred; these are the productization finish, not new features.
4. **PgnExplorerModel promotion** ŌĆö its logic is workbench-only and in-memory. When A lands a `crtk pgn` store, the *same* logic must move to `chess.*` core so CLI and GUI share it (see "mirror guarantee" below). Until A lands, the GUI explorer stays as-is.
5. **Doc drift** ŌĆö [wiki/workbench.md](wiki/workbench.md) still documents 12 flat tabs vs the shipped 8 views. Stale, misleads first-run readers.

---

#### Persona modes (the core productization move)

Personas are **presets that pre-select a surface, a mode, an inspector layout, and a curated command-template subset** ŌĆö implemented as data over the existing `ViewRegistry`/`SwitchedWorkspace`, not new code paths. Each persona maps to surfaces that already exist; the value is removing the cognitive load of "which of 8 tabs and 5 board modes do I want?"

| Persona | Lands on | Board/Engine mode | Curated templates / inspector focus | Maps to existing |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Beginner Review** | Board ŌåÆ Review detail | Analyze | `engine analyze`, `position describe`; explanations foregrounded, budgets hidden behind "Advanced" | `GameReviewPanel`, `PositionDescriptionPanel`, classical describe |
| **Club Study** | Board ŌåÆ Study/ECO | Analyze + Solve | `fen tags`, `puzzle tags`, study author; opening tree visible | `StudyAuthorPanel`, `EcoExplorerPanel`, `PuzzlePanel` |
| **Coach** | Board ŌåÆ Review + Publish | Analyze | review ŌåÆ annotate ŌåÆ `book study`/`book pdf`; publish preview adjacent | `GameReviewPanel` + Publish surface |
| **Research / ML** | Datasets | ŌĆö | `record dataset {npy,lc0,classifier}`, `record export *-jsonl`, `engine bestmove-batch`; budgets always visible | Datasets surface, batch templates |
| **Engine Lab** | Engine Lab ŌåÆ Network/MCTS/Tree/Gauntlet | ŌĆö | `engine search`, `engine tree`, `engine trace`, `engine gauntlet --sprt`, `engine gpu` | Engine Lab modes |
| **Publishing** | Publish | ŌĆö | `book collection/render/cover/study/pdf` with `--check` dry-run | Publish surface |
| **Developer** | Run ŌåÆ Build | ŌĆö | "All CLI" template, batch run, console/logs, `doctor`, `config validate` | Run surface, Console, Logs |

Implementation: a `Persona` enum + a `PersonaPreset` record (`{landingView, boardMode, engineMode, List<String> templateNames, Set<String> visibleInspectorSections}`) consumed by `WindowLifecycle` at startup and by a Dashboard persona switcher chip row. **It changes which views/templates are emphasized, never which commands are runnable** ŌĆö every persona can still reach every surface (Apple "adaptability" rule, [workbench-design-guide.md](wiki/workbench-design-guide.md):173). Persona choice persists via the existing `WORKBENCH_PREFS` Preferences node ([WindowLifecycle.java](src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowLifecycle.java):84-85).

---

#### First-run flow

The first launch has no persisted persona. Flow:

1. Dashboard renders its normal calm grid (current position card defaults to startpos), **plus** a single dismissible "Pick your workflow" card containing the 7 persona chips. No hero banner, no modal (design guide :119).
2. Selecting a persona records it in `WORKBENCH_PREFS`, switches to the persona's landing surface, and removes the card.
3. A quiet status-strip hint ("Press ŌīśK for commands ┬Ę all results show their `crtk` command") replaces the card.
4. On subsequent launches the persona is restored; the chip row collapses into a small Dashboard control (re-pickable from the command palette: `Workbench: Switch persona`).

`crtk doctor`/`config validate` run silently on first launch (already wired through `DashboardActions`) and surface a single amber chip if the environment is unhealthy ŌĆö no blocking dialog.

#### Dashboard changes

Concrete, all on [DashboardPanel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/dashboard/DashboardPanel.java)/[DashboardActions.java](src/application/gui/workbench/dashboard/DashboardActions.java):

- Persona chip row (first-run card + persistent compact control).
- Cards become **clickable deep-links** to surface+mode (the deferred UX-redesign item). "Current position" ŌåÆ Board/Analyze; "Recent run" ŌåÆ Run with that manifest re-loaded; "Artifact" ŌåÆ reveal in OS file manager (`DesktopOpen`).
- "Runtime/model health" card shows backend availability mirroring `engine gpu` (loaded/available/deviceCount), reusing `HealthSnapshot`.
- No new full workflows on the Dashboard (it "should launch work, not duplicate full workflows," design guide :93).

---

#### The 5 example workflows (each must be doable GUI-first and CLI-visible)

1. **Beginner review.** Persona Beginner Review ŌåÆ Board/Review ŌåÆ drop PGN ŌåÆ step moves ŌåÆ each position shows grounded `position describe` text + `engine analyze` eval; mistakes flagged. *Depends on C* for automatic mistakeŌåÆstudy routing; until C lands, this is manual stepping with per-position analysis (already possible). Command preview shows `crtk engine analyze --fen ŌĆ” --max-nodes ŌĆ”`.
2. **Research / ML.** Persona Research/ML ŌåÆ Datasets loads an export via `RecordIO`, shows label distribution and bad-row count (existing Datasets analyzer) ŌåÆ build `record dataset lc0 -i ŌĆ” -o ŌĆ” --weights ŌĆ”` with budgets visible ŌåÆ run ŌåÆ manifest captures input/output SHA-256.
3. **Publishing.** Persona Publishing ŌåÆ Publish loads a `.book.toml` manifest ŌåÆ live preview ŌåÆ `--check` dry-run ŌåÆ `book render`/`book cover`; render shells to CLI, output goes to the shared Run/output bus (not a private terminal block, design guide :124).
4. **Study.** Persona Club Study ŌåÆ Board/Study + ECO opening tree ŌåÆ author a study from the current line ŌåÆ `book study` export. Reuses `StudyAuthorPanel`, `EcoExplorerPanel`.
5. **Database.** Persona Developer (or a future "Library" affordance) ŌåÆ load a PGN ŌåÆ `PgnExplorerModel` index/filter/dedupe. *Depends on A* to become a persistent, queryable store with a `crtk pgn` CLI peer; today it is a per-session viewer only.

---

#### Proposed CLI surface

H is fundamentally a GUI theme, so the only *new* CLI is what the GUI must mirror and what makes the mirror testable. Personas and first-run are GUI-local prefs and intentionally have **no** CLI command (they are presets, not capabilities ŌĆö adding a CLI flag would imply hidden behavior the CLI can't reproduce, violating the mirror contract).

Two small, justified additions, both gated on **F**:

```
crtk workbench [--fen FEN] [--flip|--black-down] [--persona <name>] [-h]
    # --persona only SELECTS the startup preset; it changes no command behavior.
    # Existing flags unchanged (LaunchCommand.java).

crtk help --json
    # (Owned by theme F.) Serializes CliRegistry to a machine-readable catalog
    # of areas/actions/flags/exit-codes. The Workbench's "All CLI" template and
    # command-preview validation should consume THIS instead of reflecting over
    # CliRegistry in-process, so a packaged jar with a different classpath cannot
    # drift. This is the structural fix for the mirror guarantee (see below).
```

No new engine commands are introduced here; all engine work in the GUI uses existing commands with explicit budgets surfaced in the preview: `engine analyze`/`bestmove`/`search`/`tree`/`gauntlet` with `--max-nodes`, `--max-duration`, `--multipv`, `--threads`, `--hash`, `--depth` ([CommandTemplates.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java):116-120 already wires `engineProtocol/nodesOption/durationOption/multipvOption/threadsOption`).

#### Proposed Workbench surface (mirroring CLI)

- Persona switcher: Dashboard chip row + palette action `Workbench: Switch persona`.
- Every existing surface unchanged in capability; persona only re-emphasizes.
- Command preview (`CommandRunner.displayCommandBlock`, [CommandRunner.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java):341) shown in *every* persona, including Beginner (collapsed under "Show command" but never absent).

---

#### Command-preview improvements

The preview is the mechanism that keeps the GUI honest. Improvements (all in `command/`):

- **Budget visibility.** When a template carries engine budget options, the preview must render them even at defaults (no silent `--max-nodes`); a default that the GUI applies but doesn't show is a hidden default and is banned.
- **Copy-exact + run-exact parity assertion.** The string from `displayCommand` must be the tokens passed to `javaInvocation`; add a test (below) that asserts the preview tokens equal the spawned args.
- **Catalog-backed validation.** Once `crtk help --json` (F) exists, validate flag names/enums against the catalog so a stale example flag in a template fails loudly instead of producing an invalid command.

#### Artifact / log visibility

- Run output streams to Console; bounded at 8 MiB head/tail with a truncation marker ([CommandRunner.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java):170 `MAX_OUTPUT_BYTES`). Keep, but ensure the manifest + log file capture the full run so the GUI cap is never the only record (`RunLog`, `RunManifest`).
- Persona Research/ML and Publishing must show artifact paths as clickable reveal-in-folder links (reuse `DesktopOpen`, `ArtifactIndex`).
- Logs surface stays first-class (it already is a top-level view); style as a Run/output companion per design guide :125.

---

#### How to GUARANTEE the Workbench mirrors the CLI and never forks a second chess impl

This is the most important engineering invariant in H. Layered defenses, strongest first:

1. **Execution path (already true).** Any command *runs* by spawning `java -cp <current classpath> application.Main <args>` ([CommandRunner.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java):505-511). The GUI does not reimplement `record export`, `engine analyze`, etc. ŌĆö it builds argv and runs the real CLI. Keep this; never add an in-process shortcut for a command that has a CLI form.
2. **Coverage regression (already true).** [WorkbenchCommandRegression.java](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java):450-468 (`testCommandControllerCoversCliRegistry`) walks `CliRegistry.root()` and asserts the "All CLI" template covers every runnable path and every choice resolves; :476 asserts the batch runner offers every CLI command. Extend, do not weaken.
3. **Catalog-backed mirror (new, via F).** Today the "All CLI" template reflects over `CliRegistry` *in the same JVM*. In a packaged/jlinked distribution the GUI classpath can differ from a user's `crtk` launcher, so "same registry" is an assumption. Switching the mirror to consume `crtk help --json` (F) makes the GUI mirror the *actual installed CLI*, and lets the coverage test compare the catalog to the templates as data.
4. **In-process chess is read-only/derivation-only.** Board/Play/Relations import `chess.core.*`, `chess.eval.*`, `chess.engine.*` directly for *interactive* board state and live eval ŌĆö this is allowed because it is the same shared core, not a fork. The rule to enforce: **anything that produces a persisted artifact must go through the CLI**, so provenance and determinism live in one place. Add a structure test that bans `chess.io.*` writers and `chess.struct.*` serialization from the GUI packages (the GUI may read core, but must not write artifacts itself).

---

#### Data model / schema implications

- **Persona preset (GUI-local, no on-disk schema needed):** `Persona` enum + `PersonaPreset(landingView:String, boardMode:int, engineMode:int, templateNames:List<String>, inspectorSections:Set<String>)`. Persisted only as a single Preferences string key `workflow.persona`.
- **Run manifest (extend existing):** [RunManifest.java](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java) already has `crtk.workbench.run-manifest.v1` with per-file SHA-256. Add an optional `persona` field and bump to `v2` only if/when consumers read it; until then, additive optional field is safe (tolerant parser).
- **PGN library (deferred to A):** when A defines the on-disk store + game-id/provenance fields and `crtk pgn` commands, the GUI explorer reads that store. The GUI introduces no competing on-disk format.

#### Architecture implications

- **Plain javac / no third-party deps preserved.** Personas, first-run, dashboard deep-links, and command-preview work are all pure Swing + existing `Ui`/`Theme` primitives. No new dependency.
- **Optional dep isolation:** none required for H. (If `crtk help --json` from F is consumed, it is parsed with the repo's own `utility.Json`, not a new library.)
- **Respect the layer chain** (`Window` ŌåÉ `WindowCommandLayer` ŌåÉ ŌĆ” ŌåÉ `WindowBase`). Persona logic belongs in `WindowLifecycle` (startup/registry) and `dashboard/`, not in `WindowBase`, to avoid growing the already-large base layers.

---

#### Existing components to reuse

- [WindowLifecycle.java](src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowLifecycle.java) ŌĆö `ViewRegistry` build site; add persona-driven landing/emphasis here.
- [WindowBoardLayer.java](src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowBoardLayer.java) ŌĆö board modes/detail tabs already present.
- [CommandRunner.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java), [CommandTemplates.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandTemplates.java) ŌĆö CLI mirror + templates.
- [DashboardPanel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/dashboard/DashboardPanel.java) / [DashboardActions.java](src/application/gui/workbench/dashboard/DashboardActions.java) ŌĆö persona chips, deep-links.
- [RunManifest.java](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java), `session/RunLog.java`, `session/ArtifactIndex.java`, `session/DesktopOpen.java`, `session/HealthSnapshot.java` ŌĆö provenance/artifacts/health.
- [PgnExplorerModel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/PgnExplorerModel.java), [GameReviewPanel.java](src/application/gui/workbench/game/GameReviewPanel.java), `game/StudyAuthorPanel.java`, `game/EcoExplorerPanel.java`, `game/PuzzleLibrary.java`, `game/PositionDescriptionPanel.java` ŌĆö persona content homes.
- [Defaults.java](src/application/gui/workbench/Defaults.java) ŌĆö conservative budget defaults; personas may override emphasis but not these values.
- `ui/Theme.java`, `ui/Ui.java`, `ui/SwitchedWorkspace.java`, `layout/ViewRegistry.java`, `layout/RegisteredView.java` ŌĆö shared primitives.

#### Files / packages likely affected

- `src/application/gui/workbench/window/WindowLifecycle.java` (persona landing, view emphasis)
- `src/application/gui/workbench/dashboard/DashboardPanel.java`, `DashboardActions.java` (chips, deep-links, first-run card)
- `src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java`, `CommandTemplates.java` (preview budget visibility, catalog-backed validation)
- New: `src/application/gui/workbench/<?>/Persona.java` + `PersonaPreset.java` (likely a new small package or under `window/`; respect the 2000-line cap and one-public-type-per-file rule)
- `src/application/cli/command/LaunchCommand.java` (parse `--persona`)
- `src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java` (optional `persona` field)
- `wiki/workbench.md` (de-drift to 8 views + personas), `wiki/workbench-design-guide.md` (persona section)

---

#### Testing plan (in-house harness style ŌĆö `main()` + `testing.TestSupport`, no JUnit)

Extend the existing headless, no-dependency harness ([WorkbenchStructureRegressionTest.java](src/testing/WorkbenchStructureRegressionTest.java), [WorkbenchCommandRegression.java](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java)).

1. **`testPersonaPresetsResolveToRegisteredViews`** ŌĆö every `PersonaPreset.landingView` exists in the `ViewRegistry`; every `templateName` resolves to a real `CommandTemplate`. (Mirrors the style of `testCommandControllerCoversCliRegistry`.)
2. **`testPersonaNeverHidesRunnableCommands`** ŌĆö assert that switching persona changes emphasis only: the set of runnable command paths reachable from the shell is invariant across all 7 personas (guards against personas silently removing capability ŌĆö the design guide non-goal).
3. **`testCommandPreviewEqualsSpawnedArgs`** ŌĆö for a sample of templates, assert `CommandRunner.displayCommand(args)` tokenizes to exactly the argv `javaInvocation` would pass to `application.Main` (no hidden flag, no dropped budget).
4. **`testGuiPackagesDoNotWriteArtifacts`** (new structure test) ŌĆö scan `application.gui.workbench.*` for imports of `chess.io.Writer`/`chess.io.Converter`/artifact serializers; fail if a GUI class writes a persisted artifact instead of routing through the CLI. This is the machine-enforced "no second impl that bypasses provenance" guard.
5. **Extend `WorkbenchStructureRegressionTest`:** add the missing real subpackages to `EXPECTED_FEATURE_PACKAGES` ŌĆö verified gap: the set at [WorkbenchStructureRegressionTest.java](src/testing/WorkbenchStructureRegressionTest.java):65-78 lists `audio, board, command, dashboard, game, launch, layout, mcts, network, publish, session, ui, window` but **omits the existing `draw`, `engine`, `play`, `relations` directories** (confirmed present in the package listing). Those packages currently escape package-info/layout coverage. Add them.
6. **First-run regression** (`WorkbenchUiRegression`-style, headless): instantiate the Dashboard with no persona pref and assert the persona card is present; set the pref and assert it is absent and the landing surface matches.
7. **Wire-in check:** ensure these new tests are added to `scripts/run_regression_suite.sh` (the digest flags six existing tests that compile but are never run ŌĆö do not repeat that mistake).

#### Docs plan

- [wiki/workbench.md](wiki/workbench.md) ŌĆö rewrite the tab list (12ŌåÆ8 views), document the 7 personas and first-run flow. This also closes the verified doc-drift onboarding footgun.
- [wiki/workbench-design-guide.md](wiki/workbench-design-guide.md) ŌĆö add a "Persona Presets" subsection under Target IA; reaffirm presets-not-capabilities.
- [wiki/use-cases.md](wiki/use-cases.md) ŌĆö cross-link each of the 5 example workflows to its persona.
- Regenerate the docs site via `./scripts/run_regression_suite.sh docs` (which also runs the doc gate).

---

#### Risks / tradeoffs

- **Opportunity cost (primary risk).** Every hour on Workbench polish is an hour not on A/C/F. Mitigation: H is P2/build-later; the *only* parts worth doing before A/C/F land are persona framing + first-run + the structure/coverage debt fixes (small), because they make the *existing* capability legible.
- **Persona scope creep into hidden behavior.** If personas ever change command behavior (not just emphasis) they break the mirror contract. Mitigation: test #2 above makes capability-invariance machine-checked.
- **Catalog dependency.** Catalog-backed mirror (defense #3) is blocked on F. Until F, keep the in-process registry reflection; do not invent a parallel catalog.
- **Large-file pressure.** The digest notes 9 workbench files already exceed 2000 raw lines (pass only because comments are stripped). Persona code must go in *new* small files, not bolt onto `WindowLifecycle`/`WindowBase`.
- **`BoardController` coupling.** The shipped redesign introduced one shared board controller; Play was deliberately single-instance. A persona that lands on Play must not couple Play's state to Analyze. Mitigation: persona switching uses `CardLayout`/`SwitchedWorkspace` (already the mechanism), preserving isolation.

#### Acceptance criteria (checkable)

- [ ] 7 personas selectable; choice persists across restarts (Preferences `workflow.persona`).
- [ ] First-run shows a dismissible persona card (no hero banner, no modal); subsequent runs restore the persona.
- [ ] `testPersonaPresetsResolveToRegisteredViews` and `testPersonaNeverHidesRunnableCommands` pass and are wired into the suite.
- [ ] `testCommandPreviewEqualsSpawnedArgs` passes; no budget flag is applied without appearing in the preview.
- [ ] `testGuiPackagesDoNotWriteArtifacts` passes (GUI writes artifacts only via the CLI).
- [ ] `EXPECTED_FEATURE_PACKAGES` includes `draw`, `engine`, `play`, `relations`; all have `package-info.java`.
- [ ] `wiki/workbench.md` documents 8 views + personas; `./scripts/run_regression_suite.sh docs` is green.
- [ ] All 5 example workflows are demonstrable GUI-first with the exact `crtk` command visible and copyable.
- [ ] `testCommandControllerCoversCliRegistry` still passes (mirror coverage not regressed).

#### Future expansion

- **Short-term (P2, small):** personas + first-run + structure/coverage debt fixes + doc de-drift. No dependency on A/C/F; makes existing power legible.
- **Medium-term (P2, medium, after F):** catalog-backed command mirror (`crtk help --json`), preview validation against the catalog, `--persona` launch flag.
- **Long-term (P2ŌåÆproductized, after A/C/G):** Library surface backed by A's `crtk pgn` store (promote `PgnExplorerModel` logic into core); Beginner Review becomes a true mistakeŌåÆstudy walkthrough fed by C; Coach persona gains one-click "review ŌåÆ annotated study ŌåÆ `book pdf`." A "Reviewer/Coach" SRS affordance only after D lands. Each of these is the Workbench *consuming* a CLI capability, never forking one.

---

### 8I. Dataset provenance & ML exports (and Section 13 detail)

**Priority: P1 ┬Ę Complexity: medium ┬Ę Verdict: build-now ┬Ę Depends on: F (schemas & machine-readable catalog)**

#### Goal

Make CRTK's dataset exports *provably reproducible*. Today the export side is genuinely strong ŌĆö [`RecordDatasetExporter`](src/chess/io/RecordDatasetExporter.java), [`RecordLc0Exporter`](src/chess/io/RecordLc0Exporter.java), [`ClassifierDatasetExporter`](src/chess/io/ClassifierDatasetExporter.java), plus the `training-jsonl` / `puzzle-jsonl` / `puzzle-elo-jsonl` text exporters and the Filter DSL labeling in [`Filter.java`](src/chess/uci/Filter.java) ŌĆö but the *provenance* promise is overstated and that directly undermines "reproducible datasets," a core preserved value. [`wiki/datasets.md`](wiki/datasets.md) claims output is "deterministic down to the byte," yet:

- `record dataset npy` writes **no** `meta.json` at all (verified: [RecordDatasetExporter.java:121-122](src/chess/io/RecordDatasetExporter.java) writes only `.features.npy` and `.labels.npy`).
- The `lc0`/`classifier` `meta.json` files capture sources/filters/counts but **no** CRTK version, git commit, input checksums, weights hash, command line, or schema version (verified: [ClassifierDatasetExporter.java:525-585](src/chess/io/ClassifierDatasetExporter.java), [RecordLc0Exporter.java:325-361](src/chess/io/RecordLc0Exporter.java)).
- No dataset has a **train/val/test split** primitive, and there is **no dedupe** ŌĆö duplicate FENs/transpositions flow straight into tensors (the Workbench `DatasetPanel` even *displays* a uniqueness ratio but nothing removes the duplicates).
- `Classifier.loadDefault()` is **broken against the shipped tree**: [Model.java:17](src/chess/nn/classifier/Model.java) sets `DEFAULT_WEIGHTS = models/classifier_21planes-...bin` but the shipped file is `models/puzzle-classifier_21planes-...bin` (verified via `ls models/`).
- [`install.sh`](install.sh) fetches NN weights with **no** sha256 verification, while [`scripts/fetch_lc0_net.sh`](scripts/fetch_lc0_net.sh) already supports `--sha256`.

This initiative closes those gaps with a uniform, dependency-free provenance manifest, a deterministic split/dedupe layer, and an audit tool ŌĆö reusing the SHA-256 + JSON-builder pattern that already exists in [`RunManifest.java`](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java).

#### User story

> As an ML researcher building a puzzle-classifier or LC0 fine-tune dataset, I run one `record dataset classifier` command, get tensors plus a `*.manifest.json`, and six months later I can prove exactly which CRTK build, source `.record` files (by content hash), filter DSL, label policy, and engine budgets produced every row ŌĆö and re-run the command to get byte-identical output. I can split by game so the same game's positions never straddle train/test, dedupe transpositions, and hand the manifest to a reviewer who runs `crtk dataset audit` to confirm the tensors match.

#### Non-goals

- **No training in CRTK.** Training stays in the external `chess-nn-playground` repo. CRTK exports and audits; it does not add `crtk model train` (consistent with the digest's finding that the ML loop is "half-open" by design).
- **No new mandatory third-party dependency.** Parquet/PyTorch/HuggingFace integration ships as *documented recipes* and an optional Python helper, never as a Java dependency (preserves `javac --release 17`, no Maven/Gradle).
- **No silent data loss.** Provenance work must not change which rows are emitted by default; dedupe/split are opt-in flags.
- **Not a dataset registry/server.** Manifests are local files next to tensors; a queryable catalog is out of scope (and tensions with the product boundary).

#### MVP (smallest shippable)

1. **Provenance manifest for every exporter.** A single new dependency-free class `chess.io.DatasetManifest` (mirroring [`RunManifest`](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java)) that every exporter writes as `<stem>.manifest.json` ŌĆö including the npy exporter, which today writes nothing. Schema string `crtk.dataset.manifest.v1`.
2. **Fix the classifier default-weights path drift** ([Model.java:17](src/chess/nn/classifier/Model.java)) so `loadDefault()` works out of the box ŌĆö rename the constant to match the shipped `puzzle-classifier_*.bin` (or accept both, with the shipped name winning).
3. **Weight checksum verification in `install.sh`**: converge model fetch onto the sha256-verifying path from [`scripts/fetch_lc0_net.sh`](scripts/fetch_lc0_net.sh).
4. **Wire the two orphaned tests into CI**: [`RecordLC0ExporterRegressionTest`](src/testing/RecordLC0ExporterRegressionTest.java) and [`RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest`](src/testing/RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest.java) exist but are **not** referenced by [`scripts/run_regression_suite.sh`](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh) (verified: grep returns nothing). Add them to the `cli` target so the dataset contracts actually gate a push.

MVP ships provenance + correctness fixes with zero new commands and zero new deps.

#### Full version

5. **Deterministic dedupe**: `--dedupe none|fen|game|transposition` over a streaming pass, using `Position.signatureCore()` (the FNV digest in [Position.java:457](src/chess/core/Position.java)) as the position key. Document the FNV collision caveat in the manifest's `dedupe.key_algorithm` field.
6. **Deterministic, leakage-safe splits**: `--split train:val:test=80:10:10 --split-by game|fen --seed N`. Splitting **by game** (using the `game_id` provenance field) is the leakage-safe default; positions from one source game never straddle splits. Emits `<stem>.train.*`, `<stem>.val.*`, `<stem>.test.*` plus one manifest recording the split policy + seed.
7. **`crtk dataset audit`**: re-hash tensors/JSONL and compare against a manifest; report pass/fail per file and flag any source `.record` whose content hash changed since generation.
8. **`crtk dataset manifest`**: print/validate an existing manifest (and verify it against F's published JSON Schema).
9. **Parquet + HuggingFace recipes**: documented Python one-liners (pandas/pyarrow) that consume the `.npy` + `manifest.json`, plus a sample notebook. No Java Parquet writer.

#### Proposed CLI surface (noun-then-verb)

Extends the existing `record` area and adds a thin `dataset` query area. All existing commands keep working; new behavior is opt-in flags.

```
### Existing exporters gain provenance + dedupe + split (manifest always written):
crtk record dataset npy        --input <records> --output <stem>
                               [--dedupe none|fen|game|transposition]
                               [--split train:val:test=80:10:10 --split-by game|fen --seed N]
                               [--no-manifest]
crtk record dataset lc0        --input <records> --output <stem> --weights <lc0.bin>
                               [--dedupe ...] [--split ... --split-by ... --seed N]
crtk record dataset classifier --input <records...> --output <stem>
                               [--filter <DSL>] [--label-filter <DSL>]
                               [--max-positives N] [--max-negatives N]
                               [--dedupe ...] [--split ... --split-by ... --seed N] [--recursive]

crtk record export training-jsonl   --input <records...> --output <jsonl>
                               [--filter <DSL>] [--include-engine-metadata]
                               [--dedupe ...] [--split ... --split-by ... --seed N]
                               [--max-records N] [--recursive]
crtk record export puzzle-jsonl     --input <records> --output <jsonl> --weights <lc0.bin>
                               [--puzzles] [--nonpuzzles] [--filter <DSL>] [--dedupe ...]
crtk record export puzzle-elo-jsonl --input <records...> --output <jsonl>
                               [--ratings-csv <csv>] [--max-records N] [--threads N] [--recursive]

### New audit/inspect verbs (P1):
crtk dataset audit    --manifest <stem>.manifest.json        # re-hash + compare tensors/sources
                      [--input <stem>]                       # explicit tensor stem if moved
                      [--strict]                             # nonzero exit on any drift
crtk dataset manifest --input <stem>.manifest.json [--json]  # print/validate one manifest
```

Engine-budget note: only `puzzle-jsonl` and `puzzle-elo-jsonl` invoke search. `puzzle-jsonl` loads an LC0 `.bin` (no UCI budget ŌĆö it's a forward pass). `puzzle-elo-jsonl` runs the in-house tree search via [`PuzzleEloExporter`](src/chess/io/PuzzleEloExporter.java) bounded by `--threads N` and the built-in `MAX_TREE_SOLVER_DEPTH=24` / `MAX_TREE_NODES_PER_ROOT=100000` caps; the manifest records these (`engine.tree_solver_depth`, `engine.tree_nodes_per_root`, `engine.threads`) so the non-deterministic-under-`--threads` risk is at least *recorded*. The upstream mining budgets (`--max-nodes`, `--max-duration`, `--protocol-path`, engine binary/version) belong to the records' own provenance and are propagated into the dataset manifest's `source.upstream` block when present.

#### Proposed Workbench surface (mirror CLI, no second impl)

The Workbench `DatasetPanel` already mirrors these exports and *displays* a uniqueness/duplicate ratio. Extend it to:

- Add `--dedupe` and `--split` controls whose generated command preview is the **exact** `record dataset ...` invocation (enforced by [`WorkbenchCommandRegression`](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java) ŌĆö the all-CLI template walk).
- Show the written `manifest.json` and the per-split row counts after a run, reading the same `DatasetManifest` JSON the CLI wrote (no recomputation in the GUI).
- A "Verify dataset" action that shells `crtk dataset audit` via [`CommandRunner`](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java) (child JVM running `application.Main`), surfacing pass/fail ŌĆö never a parallel in-GUI hashing implementation.

This keeps CLI as source of truth; the GUI is a thin front-end over the same Java exporters and the same `dataset audit` command.

#### Data model / schema implications (concrete fields)

**1. Extend [`Record`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) (depends on F).** Today the record is exactly `{created, engine, parent, position, description, tags, analysis}` ŌĆö no version, no game linkage. `training-jsonl` *hardcodes* `game_id:null`, `position_index:null`, `source_group_id:null` (verified [RecordTrainingJsonlCommand.java:503-506](src/application/cli/command/RecordTrainingJsonlCommand.java)). Add (tolerant, optional, defaulted) fields:

- `schema_version` (int) ŌĆö so old records load and migrate.
- `game_id` (string|null), `position_index` (int|null) ŌĆö enable split-by-game and review linkage (initiative C).
- `source_platform` (string|null) ŌĆö e.g. `mining`, `pgn-import`, `lichess-export` (initiative B, when it lands).

These are additive; [`Record.fromJson`](src/chess/struct/Record.java) already tolerates a fixed shape, so absent fields default to null/0.

**2. `DatasetManifest` (`crtk.dataset.manifest.v1`), one `<stem>.manifest.json` per export.** Concrete fields:

```jsonc
{
  "schema": "crtk.dataset.manifest.v1",
  "crtk_version": "1.0.0",                 // from VersionCommand.VERSION (single-sourced, see J)
  "git_commit": "abc123ŌĆ”|unknown",         // best-effort; "unknown" if not a git build
  "generated_at": 1718000000000,           // epoch ms (the ONLY non-reproducible field; excluded from audit hashes)
  "command_line": "record dataset classifier --input ŌĆ” --output ŌĆ”",
  "exporter": "classifier|lc0|npy|training-jsonl|puzzle-jsonl|puzzle-elo-jsonl",
  "schema_out": "crtk.dataset.classifier.v1", // the published F schema this output conforms to

  "sources": [                              // every input .record / .jsonl
    { "path": "dump/run.json", "bytes": 12345, "sha256": "ŌĆ”", "records_seen": 900 }
  ],
  "rows": { "written": 812, "skipped": { "invalid": 3, "filtered": 80, "deduped": 5, "class_cap": 0 } },

  "dedupe":  { "mode": "transposition", "key_algorithm": "Position.signatureCore (FNV-1a, non-cryptographic)", "removed": 5 },
  "split":   { "policy": "train:val:test=80:10:10", "by": "game", "seed": 42,
               "counts": { "train": 650, "val": 81, "test": 81 } },

  "labels":  { "row_filter": "<DSL>", "row_filter_sha256": "ŌĆ”",
               "label_filter": "<DSL>", "label_policy": "puzzle=2,sister-parent=1,other=0",
               "recommended_pos_weight": 4.1 },

  "engine":  { "present": false },          // or, for puzzle-elo:
  // "engine": { "present": true, "kind": "in-house-tree",
  //             "tree_solver_depth": 24, "tree_nodes_per_root": 100000, "threads": 8,
  //             "model_id": "crtk-tree-v14-evidence-direct", "deterministic_under_threads": false }

  "weights": { "path": "models/leela_112planes-ŌĆ”.bin", "sha256": "ŌĆ”" }, // when --weights used
  "source": { "upstream": { "protocol_sha256": "ŌĆ”", "engine_name": "Stockfish 16",
                            "max_nodes": 50000000, "max_duration_ms": 1000000 } }, // when present in records
  "outputs": [ { "path": "<stem>.train.inputs.npy", "bytes": ŌĆ”, "sha256": "ŌĆ”" }, ŌĆ” ]
}
```

The **audit hash set deliberately excludes `generated_at`** so re-runs are byte-identical (the same trap [`RunManifest`](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java) avoids and the same one [`Result.equals` includes `elapsedMillis`](src/chess/engine/Result.java) gets *wrong* ŌĆö do not repeat that mistake).

**3. Published JSON Schemas (F dependency).** `crtk.dataset.manifest.v1` plus one schema per output shape (`crtk.dataset.classifier.v1`, `crtk.dataset.lc0.v1`, `crtk.dataset.training-jsonl.v1`, `crtk.dataset.puzzle-jsonl.v1`). `crtk dataset manifest --json` validates against these.

#### Architecture implications (plain javac / no-deps; isolate optional deps)

- **All Java code stays dependency-free.** Manifest writing reuses [`utility.Json`](src/utility/Json.java) for escaping and `java.security.MessageDigest` for SHA-256 ŌĆö exactly the toolkit [`RunManifest`](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java) already uses (verified: `MessageDigest.getInstance("SHA-256")` at [RunManifest.java:456-458](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java)). No new imports outside `java.*`.
- **One shared manifest writer.** `chess.io.DatasetManifest` is the single source; every exporter calls it. This kills the current per-exporter, hand-rolled `StringBuilder` meta.json divergence (three different shapes today).
- **Streaming preserved.** Dedupe is a streaming `HashSet<Long>` of `signatureCore()` keys (constant-ish memory for typical corpora; document the large-corpus memory cost ŌĆö same assumption `PuzzleEloExporter` already bakes in with its 1.2M-entry map). Splits require a two-pass approach for split-by-game (pass 1 collects gameŌåÆsplit assignment deterministically by seeded hash of `game_id`; pass 2 routes rows), so the npy/lc0 single-pass writers gain an optional pre-pass ŌĆö kept off by default.
- **Parquet is a documented recipe, not a Java writer.** Writing Parquet from Java would require `parquet-mr`/Arrow (heavy, transitive Hadoop deps) ŌĆö forbidden. Instead: `.npy` + manifest is the canonical artifact; `wiki/datasets.md` gets a copy-paste `pyarrow` recipe to convert `.npy`ŌåÆParquet, and the sample notebook does the same. HuggingFace consumption is via the existing JSONL exporters (`training-jsonl`/`puzzle-jsonl` are already line-delimited JSON ŌĆö directly loadable by `datasets.load_dataset("json", ŌĆ”)`); we only need to document the column contract (F schema) and ship a manifest alongside.
- **Optional Python helper isolated under `tools/` or `python/`** (not in `src/`), with zero coupling to the Java build; it reads `.npy` + `manifest.json` and is purely a convenience (Section 13).

#### Existing components to reuse (real files)

- [`RecordDatasetExporter.java`](src/chess/io/RecordDatasetExporter.java) ŌĆö add the missing manifest; gains dedupe/split pre-pass.
- [`ClassifierDatasetExporter.java`](src/chess/io/ClassifierDatasetExporter.java) / [`RecordLc0Exporter.java`](src/chess/io/RecordLc0Exporter.java) ŌĆö replace bespoke meta.json with `DatasetManifest` (keep the encoder/shape/recommended_pos_weight fields inside it).
- [`RunManifest.java`](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java) ŌĆö the SHA-256 + dependency-free JSON-builder pattern and `generated_at`-excluded-from-equality discipline to copy.
- [`Filter.java` / `FilterDSL`](src/chess/uci/Filter.java) ŌĆö `fromString`/`toDSL` round-trip for hashing the label/row filters into the manifest (`fromString(toDSL(x))` is a fixed point, so the DSL hash is stable).
- [`Position.signatureCore()`](src/chess/core/Position.java) ŌĆö dedupe key.
- [`RecordIO.java`](src/application/cli/RecordIO.java) ŌĆö streaming JSON-array/JSONL reader feeding dedupe/split.
- [`NpyFloat32Writer.java`](src/chess/io/NpyFloat32Writer.java) ŌĆö tensor writer (unchanged; split just routes to N stems).
- [`VersionCommand.VERSION`](src/application/cli/command/VersionCommand.java) ŌĆö `crtk_version` (single-source it per initiative J so it can't drift from `package.json`).
- [`utility.Json`](src/utility/Json.java) ŌĆö JSON emit/escape; [`utility.Toml`](src/utility/Toml.java) for protocol hashing input.

#### Files / packages likely affected (real paths)

- `src/chess/io/DatasetManifest.java` (new), `RecordDatasetExporter.java`, `ClassifierDatasetExporter.java`, `RecordLc0Exporter.java`, `PuzzleEloExporter.java`.
- `src/application/cli/command/RecordCommands.java`, `RecordTrainingJsonlCommand.java`, `RecordPuzzleJsonlCommand.java` (flag parsing for `--dedupe`/`--split`/`--seed`; manifest emission).
- `src/application/cli/command/DatasetCommand.java` (new ŌĆö `audit`/`manifest`), wired in [`CliRegistry.java`](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java) (new `dataset` group) and [`Constants.java`](src/application/cli/Constants.java) (`OPT_DEDUPE`, `OPT_SPLIT`, `OPT_SPLIT_BY`, `OPT_SEED`, `OPT_NO_MANIFEST`, `OPT_MANIFEST`).
- `src/chess/struct/Record.java` (additive `schema_version`/`game_id`/`position_index`/`source_platform`; depends on F).
- `src/chess/nn/classifier/Model.java` (fix `DEFAULT_WEIGHTS` path drift).
- [`install.sh`](install.sh) (sha256 verify), converging on [`scripts/fetch_lc0_net.sh`](scripts/fetch_lc0_net.sh).
- [`scripts/run_regression_suite.sh`](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh) (wire orphaned tests + new ones).
- `tools/` or `python/` (new optional Python helper + sample notebook).

#### Testing plan (in-house harness, `main()` + `TestSupport`)

Style matches [`PositionRegressionTest`](src/testing/PositionRegressionTest.java) ŌĆö no JUnit; `static void main`, `TestSupport.assert*`, prints `<Class>: all checks passed`.

- **`DatasetManifestRegressionTest`** (new): build a small `.record` fixture, run `record dataset classifier` twice, assert (a) a `manifest.json` is written, (b) all manifest fields present and well-formed, (c) `generated_at` differs between runs but **every other field and every tensor sha256 is byte-identical** (the determinism claim, finally tested ŌĆö the digest flags that *no* test verifies re-run byte-equality today), (d) source `sha256` matches an independently computed hash.
- **`DatasetSplitRegressionTest`** (new): with a fixture where multiple positions share a `game_id`, run `--split ŌĆ” --split-by game --seed 7` and assert **no `game_id` appears in more than one split** (leakage check) and that re-running with the same seed reproduces the split exactly.
- **`DatasetDedupeRegressionTest`** (new): inject transpositions; assert `--dedupe transposition` removes exactly the expected count and `manifest.dedupe.removed` matches; assert `--dedupe none` changes nothing.
- **`DatasetAuditRegressionTest`** (new): generate a dataset, run `crtk dataset audit --manifest ŌĆ”` ŌåÆ pass; then mutate one tensor byte and one source record ŌåÆ audit `--strict` returns nonzero and names the drifted file.
- **Wire existing orphans**: add [`RecordLC0ExporterRegressionTest`](src/testing/RecordLC0ExporterRegressionTest.java) and [`RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest`](src/testing/RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest.java) into the `cli` target of [`run_regression_suite.sh`](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh) so they actually gate CI (verified currently NOT wired).
- **`ClassifierLoadDefaultRegressionTest`** (new, small): assert `chess.nn.classifier.Model.loadDefault()` succeeds against the shipped `models/` tree (would have caught the current path drift) ŌĆö gated/skipped loudly if the model file is absent, per the "a test that quietly skips itself isn't a test" rule.
- **F dependency**: `crtk dataset manifest --json` output validates against the published `crtk.dataset.manifest.v1` JSON Schema (shared with F's schema test).

#### Docs plan

- [`wiki/datasets.md`](wiki/datasets.md): replace the unqualified "byte-exact" claim with the *now-tested* determinism guarantee + the `generated_at` caveat; document `--dedupe`/`--split`/`--seed`, the manifest schema, `dataset audit`, the Parquet `pyarrow` recipe, and the HuggingFace `load_dataset("json", ŌĆ”)` recipe with the column contract.
- [`wiki/filter-dsl.md`](wiki/filter-dsl.md): note the filter DSL is hashed into the manifest (label provenance).
- [`wiki/ai-agents.md`](wiki/ai-agents.md): add `dataset audit`/`dataset manifest` to the command-to-contract table.
- New `wiki/ml-pipelines.md` (or a Section in datasets.md): the end-to-end miningŌåÆexportŌåÆsplitŌåÆtrain(external)ŌåÆaudit loop, plus the sample notebook walkthrough.
- [`models/README.md`](models/README.md): document weight sha256 verification now in `install.sh`.

#### Risks / tradeoffs

- **FNV dedupe collisions.** `signatureCore()` is a non-cryptographic FNV digest (not Zobrist; [Position.java:457](src/chess/core/Position.java)). For million-position corpora, collision-driven over-dedupe is possible. Mitigation: document the algorithm in the manifest, and offer `--dedupe fen` (exact normalized-FEN string compare) as the collision-free, higher-memory alternative.
- **Split-by-game requires a real `game_id`.** Until initiatives A/C populate `game_id`, mined records have `game_id:null`, so split-by-game degrades to split-by-fen with a warning. This makes the Record schema extension (F) a genuine dependency, not cosmetic.
- **Two-pass splits change the streaming model** for npy/lc0. Kept off by default; documented memory cost for the game-assignment pass.
- **`puzzle-elo-jsonl` non-determinism under `--threads`.** The tree solver is multi-threaded; the manifest *records* `deterministic_under_threads:false` rather than pretending otherwise. Recommend `--threads 1` for reproducible dataset builds; surface this in docs.
- **Manifest scope creep.** Resist turning the manifest into a dataset registry ŌĆö it is a sidecar file, full stop (product-boundary discipline).

#### Acceptance criteria (checkable)

- [ ] Every `record dataset *` and `record export *-jsonl` command writes a `<stem>.manifest.json` conforming to `crtk.dataset.manifest.v1` (npy included).
- [ ] Two identical export runs produce byte-identical tensors/JSONL and manifests that differ **only** in `generated_at` ŌĆö asserted by `DatasetManifestRegressionTest`.
- [ ] `--split ŌĆ” --split-by game` never places one `game_id` in two splits; `--seed` makes splits reproducible ŌĆö asserted by `DatasetSplitRegressionTest`.
- [ ] `--dedupe {fen,transposition}` removes exactly the expected rows and records the count in the manifest.
- [ ] `crtk dataset audit --manifest ŌĆ” --strict` exits 0 on an untouched dataset and nonzero (naming the file) after any tensor/source mutation.
- [x] `chess.nn.classifier.Model.loadDefault()` succeeds against the shipped `models/` tree.
- [x] `install.sh` verifies sha256 for every fetched weight file.
- [x] [`RecordLC0ExporterRegressionTest`](src/testing/RecordLC0ExporterRegressionTest.java) and [`RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest`](src/testing/RecordTrainingJSONLRegressionTest.java) run in `scripts/run_regression_suite.sh ci`.
- [ ] No new non-`java.*` import anywhere in `src/`.

#### Section 13 detail ŌĆö Notebook / Python integration & sample pipelines

- **Optional Python helper** (`tools/crtk_dataset.py` or `python/`, isolated from the Java build): `load_dataset(stem)` reads `<stem>.{features,labels}.npy` (or `.lc0.*` / `.classifier.*`) + `<stem>.manifest.json`, returns numpy arrays + a parsed manifest dict, and exposes `verify(stem)` that re-hashes locally (a Python mirror of `crtk dataset audit` for notebook users who don't want to shell out). Depends only on `numpy` (stdlib `json`/`hashlib` otherwise) ŌĆö explicitly *not* a CRTK Java dependency.
- **Parquet recipe (documented, not built-in)**: `pyarrow`/`pandas` snippet converting `.npy`ŌåÆParquet, carrying the manifest hash as Parquet key-value metadata so provenance survives the format conversion.
- **HuggingFace recipe**: `training-jsonl`/`puzzle-jsonl` are already HF-loadable (`datasets.load_dataset("json", data_files=ŌĆ”)`); document the per-column contract from the F schema and how to attach the manifest as dataset card metadata.
- **Sample pipeline notebook** (`tools/notebooks/puzzle_classifier_pipeline.ipynb`): mine ŌåÆ `record dataset classifier --dedupe transposition --split ŌĆ”` ŌåÆ load in Python ŌåÆ (train in `chess-nn-playground`, referenced not embedded) ŌåÆ `crtk dataset audit`. Demonstrates the full local-first ML loop and doubles as living documentation for the manifest contract.
- **No notebook execution in CI** (the project has no Python test harness); the notebook is documentation. The Python helper, if shipped, gets a tiny `python -m` smoke check only if a Python toolchain is already required elsewhere ŌĆö otherwise it stays untested-by-CI and clearly labeled as a convenience.

#### Sequencing

- **Short-term (MVP, P1)**: `DatasetManifest` for all exporters incl. npy; classifier path fix; `install.sh` sha256; wire orphaned tests. No new commands, no Record schema change, no deps. Shippable independently of F (manifests are self-describing; F's *published JSON Schema* upgrades validation later).
- **Medium-term (P1, after F lands)**: Record schema fields (`schema_version`/`game_id`/ŌĆ”), `--dedupe`, `--split --split-by`, `crtk dataset audit`/`manifest`, published JSON Schemas, Workbench mirroring.
- **Long-term (P2)**: Python helper + sample notebook + Parquet/HF recipes; richer `source.upstream` provenance once initiatives A/B/C populate game ids and source platforms.

---

### 8J. Packaging & onboarding (and Section 15 detail)

**Theme verdict:** `partial` ŌåÆ build-later, **priority P2**, **complexity medium** overall (but with cheap P0 correctness bugs carved out). **Depends on:** I (dataset provenance / checksums ŌĆö shares the model-hash work), F (machine-readable catalog ŌĆö `doctor --json` / `config show --json` reuse it). Loosely informs JŌåÆH (a packaged Workbench app) and JŌåÆK (editor tasks need a stable entry point).

The honest framing: packaging is *solid but Linux-only and partly inaccurate*. The work splits into three tranches that must not be conflated:

1. **Cheap correctness bugs** that mislead a brand-new user on first run (P0/P1, hours of work).
2. **Onboarding ergonomics** ŌĆö a guided setup, engine detection, safe optional-weight downloads (P2, the bulk of this initiative).
3. **Cross-platform distribution** ŌĆö `.deb`/Homebrew/Scoop/winget/jpackage bundles (P2/P3, large, deferrable because the portable jar already runs everywhere Java 17 does).

Do tranche 1 immediately and folded into the M (roadmap reconciliation) / I (provenance) work; tranche 2 is the real initiative; tranche 3 is sequenced last and gated on "don't break the simple build."

---

#### Goal
