The honest situation today: **every primitive exists, but nothing chains them.** A
grep for `game review`/`reviewGame`/`study router` across
[src/application/cli/](src/application/cli/) returns nothing ŌĆö there is no `crtk game
review` verb. The miner ([MineCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/MineCommand.java))
turns a *FEN* into a puzzle but has no notion of "the human played X, the puzzle is the
refutation." So the pipeline below is **8 existing commands + 3 thin new ones**
(`pgn import`, `game review`, `study schedule`). New work is marked **[NEW]**.

A recurring determinism hazard runs through the whole pipeline and is called out per
stage: **CRTK's own code is deterministic; the external UCI engine is not guaranteed
bit-identical across versions/builds.** Stages that touch an external engine
(`engine analyze-batch`, `puzzle mine`, `record export puzzle-elo-jsonl`) reproduce
byte-for-byte *only* with the same engine binary, protocol TOML, and explicit budgets
pinned. CRTK enforces the budgets; it cannot pin the engine for you.

---

### Stage 1 ŌĆö Import games

Bring external PGN into a local, indexed store. **[NEW]** ŌĆö the closest shipped command,
[`fen pgn`](src/application/cli/command/PgnCommand.java), is a *stateless* PGNŌåÆFEN
converter with no game id, no store, no index (confirmed: `runPgnToFens` just writes a
FEN list). Theme 8A (`build-now`, P1) defines the `crtk pgn` store; Stage 1 is its
`import` verb.

- **Command:** `crtk pgn import --input games.pgn --store study.pgndb` **[NEW]**
- **Input artifact:** `games.pgn` (standard PGN, one or many games)
- **Output artifact:** `study.pgndb/index.jsonl` (one record per game) + the raw games
  appended to `study.pgndb/games.pgn`. Each index row carries a stable
  `game_id` (assume SHA-256 over normalized movetext + the seven-tag roster ŌĆö **ASSUMPTION**,
  the schema is 8A's to fix) and a `schema_version` (per 8F).
- **Deterministic:** PGN parse and the index row are pure functions of the input ŌĆö
  [Pgn.java](src/chess/struct/Pgn.java) is engine-free. `game_id` is deterministic *iff*
  the hash inputs are canonicalized (movetext via the shared SAN core, tags sorted).
- **Engine-dependent:** Nothing. No engine touched in this stage.

> Boundary note (8B): import is **read-only, from a local file or a user-supplied public
> export**. No account linking, no continuous sync ŌĆö that would cross the product
> boundary and is deferred (8B, P3).

---

### Stage 2 ŌĆö Normalize / dedupe

Collapse re-imports and transpositions so the same game is reviewed once.

- **Command:** `crtk pgn import` runs this inline; standalone re-run is
  `crtk pgn dedupe --store study.pgndb` **[NEW]**
- **Input artifact:** `study.pgndb/index.jsonl` (post-Stage-1)
- **Output artifact:** `study.pgndb/index.jsonl` rewritten (duplicate `game_id` rows
  dropped, a `dupe_of` back-reference retained for audit)
- **Deterministic:** Yes, fully. Dedupe key is `game_id` (Stage 1) and the per-position
  key is [`Position.signatureCore()`](src/chess/core/Position.java) ŌĆö a deterministic
  FNV-1a digest, lazily cached. Same input ŌåÆ same surviving set, every time.
- **Engine-dependent:** Nothing.
- **Caveat (grounded):** `signatureCore()` is FNV-1a, **not** a collision-resistant
  Zobrist key (verified: repeated `* 1099511628211L` in
  [Position.java](src/chess/core/Position.java)). For a personal study DB
  (thousands of games) collision risk is negligible; for million-position dedupe it is a
  documented risk 8A/8F must own. **Do not** present `signatureCore()` as a cryptographic
  identity.

---

### Stage 3 ŌĆö Identify positions

Expand each surviving game into the position stream to be analyzed, **preserving
parentŌåÆchild lineage** (the lineage is what Stage 5 diffs).

- **Command:** `crtk fen pgn --input study.pgndb/games.pgn --pairs --output positions.fenpairs`
  (verified flag: `--pairs` in [PgnCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/PgnCommand.java),
  registered at [CliRegistry.java:103](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java))
- **Input artifact:** `study.pgndb/games.pgn`
- **Output artifact:** `positions.fenpairs` ŌĆö line-oriented; with `--pairs` each line
  carries the parent FEN and the resulting FEN so the move played is recoverable via
  [MoveInference.uniqueMove](src/chess/core/MoveInference.java). (`--mainline` alone gives
  bare positions and loses the "what move was played" link ŌĆö **use `--pairs` for review**.)
- **Deterministic:** Yes. Move replay and FEN formatting route through the one shared
  core; no engine.
- **Engine-dependent:** Nothing.

---

### Stage 4 ŌĆö Engine-analyze with EXPLICIT budgets

Attach reference-grade analysis to every position. This is the **only** mandatory
external-engine stage and the one place reproducibility depends on something CRTK does
not control.

- **Command:**
  `crtk engine analyze-batch --input positions.fenpairs --protocol-path config/default.engine.toml --max-nodes 2000000 --max-duration 2s --multipv 2 --threads 1 --output analyzed.jsonl`
  (verified: `analyze-batch` defaults to JSONL,
  [EngineBatchCommand.java:194-202](src/application/cli/command/EngineBatchCommand.java))
- **Input artifact:** `positions.fenpairs`
- **Output artifact:** `analyzed.jsonl` ŌĆö one row per position:
  `{"ok":true,"index":N,"fen":...,"engine":...,"pv":[{multipv,uci,san,eval,depth,nodes,...}]}`
  (hand-built rows, [EngineBatchCommand.java:256](src/application/cli/command/EngineBatchCommand.java)).
- **Budgets are explicit and enforced by CRTK:** `--max-nodes` and `--max-duration` are
  required discipline; `--multipv 2` is the floor for Stage 5/7 (PV1-vs-PV2 gap is the
  mistake signal). The budget *flags* are honored deterministically by CRTK's UCI driver
  ([Engine.java](src/chess/uci/Engine.java)).
- **Deterministic:** The **request** is deterministic (CRTK sends identical
  `go nodes`/position lines for identical inputs). The **response** is deterministic only
  if the engine binary, protocol TOML, thread count, and hash are fixed. Use `--threads 1`
  for byte-stable analysis; multi-threaded Stockfish search is **not** reproducible.
- **Engine-dependent:** Everything in the `pv` payload (eval, depth, nodes, chosen move).
  This is the reproducibility seam ŌĆö pin the engine version in the provenance manifest
  (Stage 11, per 8I).
- **Grounded caveat:** [Engine.analyse()](src/chess/uci/Engine.java) issues `go nodes`
  and ignores the protocol's `searchDepth`/`searchTime` templates ŌĆö so `--depth` is
  **inert** for external analysis (a known gap). Budget by nodes/time, not depth.

---

### Stage 5 ŌĆö Compute deltas

Turn raw evals into the eval-motion signal that exposes where a game went wrong.

- **Command:** `crtk record analysis-delta --input analyzed.records.json --output deltas.jsonl`
  (verified: [RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java),
  registered [CliRegistry.java:295](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java))
- **Input artifact:** a `.record` array carrying stored `analysis` per position. Because
  `analysis-delta` reads from `Record.analysis`, Stage 4's `analyzed.jsonl` must first be
  materialized as records ŌĆö done by the miner path or by an adapter the router owns. The
  parent/child linkage uses the `--pairs` lineage from Stage 3.
- **Output artifact:** `deltas.jsonl` ŌĆö one row per record:
  `{index, created, engine, position, initial_eval, final_eval, delta_type(cp|mate|mixed|none),
  delta_value, time_to_final_ms, fluctuation_type, fluctuation_range/min/max,
  max_abs_delta_from_final}` (fields verified at
  [RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java:261-279](src/application/cli/command/RecordAnalysisDeltaCommand.java)).
- **Deterministic:** Yes, *given the analysis payload*. The delta arithmetic is pure CRTK
  code over already-stored evals.
- **Engine-dependent:** Transitively ŌĆö the evals it diffs came from Stage 4, so the
  numeric deltas inherit Stage 4's engine dependence. The *computation* adds no new
  non-determinism.

---

### Stage 6 ŌĆö Tag positions

Attach engine-free, grounded structural/tactical tags to each reviewed position and the
whole-game annotation layers.

- **Command (per-position):** `crtk fen tags --input positions.fen --output tags.jsonl`
- **Command (whole-game):** `crtk fen tags --pgn study.pgndb/games.pgn --analyze-game --output game-analysis.json`
  (verified: `--analyze-game` **requires** `--pgn`,
  [TagsCommand.java:158-159](src/application/cli/command/TagsCommand.java))
- **Input artifact:** `positions.fen` / `study.pgndb/games.pgn`
- **Output artifact:** `tags.jsonl` (canonical `FAMILY: key=value` tag strings) and
  `game-analysis.json` (nested `{gameTags, lines, variations, sharedTactics,
  moves:[{ply,san,effects}]}` from the MOVE_EFFECT/LINE/VARIATION/GAME layers in
  [chess.tag.game](src/chess/tag/game/)).
- **Deterministic:** Yes ŌĆö this is the project's core grounded value. Static tagging is a
  pure function of the FEN; re-running yields identical, sorted, deduped tags. No engine.
- **Engine-dependent:** Only the optional `--analyze` enrichment (CAND/PV/richer META)
  routes through an engine; the **default** static and `--analyze-game` paths are
  engine-free.
- **Debt to fix first (8M/8F):** the dynamic MOVE_EFFECT/LINE/VARIATION/GAME families are
  **not** registered in [Sort.FAMILY_ORDER](src/chess/tag/Sort.java) or
  [Literals.java](src/chess/tag/core/Literals.java) (verified absent). Until registered,
  these game-review tags bypass the canonical sort/dedupe/Delta/Filter pipeline ŌĆö the
  router's tag output is *structurally forked* from the static contract. Registering them
  is a prerequisite for Stage 7 classification to operate uniformly.

---

### Stage 7 ŌĆö Classify mistakes

Convert (delta, tags, multipv-gap) per position into a mistake label and a turning-point
flag. **[NEW]** classification logic, but it is thin glue over Stages 5-6 outputs.

- **Command:** `crtk game review --store study.pgndb --analysis analyzed.jsonl --deltas deltas.jsonl --tags tags.jsonl --output review.jsonl` **[NEW]**
- **Input artifacts:** `deltas.jsonl` (Stage 5), `tags.jsonl` + `game-analysis.json`
  (Stage 6), `analyzed.jsonl` (Stage 4, for the PV1/PV2 gap)
- **Output artifact:** `review.jsonl` ŌĆö one row per reviewed move:
  `{game_id, ply, fen, played_uci, best_uci, delta_cp, class, is_turning_point, theme_tags[], schema_version}`.
  `class Ōłł {blunder, mistake, inaccuracy, good, best, forced}` from
  banded `delta_cp` thresholds (assume Lichess-like Ōēź300/Ōēź100/Ōēź50 ŌĆö **ASSUMPTION**, the
  bands are the router's to fix and must be documented constants, not magic numbers).
- **Deterministic:** The **classification function** is deterministic ŌĆö fixed cp bands +
  tag membership, pure CRTK code, no RNG, no clock.
- **Engine-dependent:** The **inputs** (`delta_cp`, `best_uci`) are engine-derived
  (Stage 4). So a label is reproducible iff Stage 4 was. The label *mapping* adds no
  non-determinism.
- **Honest blocker (grounded):** the engine-graded `MOVE_EFFECT quality=` /
  `turning_point` verdicts the tag engine *designed* are still TODO (deferred in the tag
  digest). Until they land, `is_turning_point` must be derived from the eval-delta
  sequence in Stage 5 (largest sustained swing), **not** read from a tag. Build the
  delta-based heuristic now; swap to graded tags when they ship.

---

### Stage 8 ŌĆö Generate study tasks

Turn classified mistakes into study units (the abstract task objects that Stages 9-10
specialize).

- **Command:** `crtk game review ... --emit-tasks tasks.jsonl` **[NEW]** (same verb, task
  emission mode)
- **Input artifact:** `review.jsonl`
- **Output artifact:** `tasks.jsonl` ŌĆö one row per study unit:
  `{task_id, game_id, ply, kind(tactic|positional|endgame|opening), source_fen,
  solution_line_uci[], prompt, theme_tags[], difficulty_hint, schema_version}`. Each task
  references its origin position so the user can jump back to the game (lineage from
  Stage 1's `game_id`).
- **Deterministic:** Yes ŌĆö task synthesis is a pure rewrite of `review.jsonl` rows.
- **Engine-dependent:** Inherited only (the `solution_line_uci` came from Stage 4's PV).
- **Cross-ref 8G:** `prompt` is the natural-language ask; it should be generated by
  [`position describe`](src/application/cli/command/PositionDescribeCommand.java)
  (classical, faithful-by-construction) so the study prompt **cannot hallucinate** a move
  the position doesn't support. Do **not** route through the dead describe-T5 stub
  ([T5PositionDescriptionGenerator.available()](src/chess/describe/T5PositionDescriptionGenerator.java)
  is always `false`).

---

### Stage 9 ŌĆö Produce puzzles / repertoire gaps

Specialize tasks into the two concrete artifacts a student trains on: tactical puzzles
(from blunders that had a refutation) and repertoire gaps (opening deviations).

- **Command (puzzles):**
  `crtk puzzle mine --input refutation-seeds.fen --protocol-path config/default.engine.toml --max-nodes 2000000 --max-duration 2s --engine-instances 4 --output study.puzzles`
  then rate with
  `crtk record export puzzle-elo-jsonl --input study.puzzles.puzzles.json --output study.elo.jsonl`
- **Command (repertoire gaps):** `crtk pgn gaps --store study.pgndb --eco config/book.eco.toml --output gaps.jsonl` **[NEW]** (consumes the ECO book +
  Stage 7 opening-class moves; this is the seam 8D builds on)
- **Input artifact:** the blunder/turning-point rows from `review.jsonl` (their *parent*
  FEN becomes the puzzle seed ŌĆö "the position before the mistake, find the move the human
  missed")
- **Output artifacts:**
  - `study.puzzles.puzzles.json` + `study.puzzles.nonpuzzles.json` (verified naming for a
    file root, [MineCommand.java:878-879](src/application/cli/command/MineCommand.java))
  - `study.elo.jsonl` (puzzle rows with `META: puzzle_*` Elo tags,
    `puzzle_elo_model=crtk-tree-v14-evidence-direct`)
  - `gaps.jsonl` **[NEW]** (opening lines where the user left book, keyed to ECO codes)
- **Deterministic:**
  - The puzzle **difficulty/Elo scorer** is deterministic: signature-keyed splitmix64
    jitter, no RNG ([Scorer.java](src/chess/puzzle/Scorer.java)).
  - **Filename is NOT deterministic for a directory root** ŌĆö the miner embeds
    `System.currentTimeMillis()` (verified, [MineCommand.java:883-886](src/application/cli/command/MineCommand.java)).
    **Always pass a file-stem `--output`, never a bare directory,** if you want
    reproducible artifact names.
  - The ECO label (`gaps.jsonl`) is deterministic ŌĆö engine-free lookup over
    [Encyclopedia.java](src/chess/eco/Encyclopedia.java).
- **Engine-dependent:**
  - `puzzle mine` acceptance and `puzzle-elo-jsonl` ratings depend on the external engine
    (mining) and a **multi-threaded tree search** (verified:
    [PuzzleEloExporter.java:798](src/chess/io/PuzzleEloExporter.java) parallelizes when
    `threads>1` and `rootsŌēź2000`). For byte-stable ratings, pass `--threads 1`; the
    parallel path's reproducibility is not asserted.
  - **Foot-gun (grounded):** the default puzzle quality gate hard-requires
    `nodes>=50000000` ([Config.java](src/application/Config.java) `DEFAULT_PUZZLE_QUALITY`).
    A review mine budgeted at 2M nodes (Stage 4 scale) will silently accept **zero**
    puzzles. The router must lower the gate explicitly via `--puzzle-quality` or warn.

---

### Stage 10 ŌĆö Schedule time-budgeted study

Order the tasks/puzzles into a session that fits a stated time budget. **[NEW]** ŌĆö this is
the SRS seam (theme 8D, `build-later`, P2). For the router's first version, ship a simple
deterministic scheduler; the spaced-repetition state machine is 8D's job.

- **Command:** `crtk study schedule --tasks tasks.jsonl --puzzles study.elo.jsonl --budget 30m --output session.jsonl` **[NEW]**
- **Input artifacts:** `tasks.jsonl` (Stage 8), `study.elo.jsonl` (Stage 9)
- **Output artifact:** `session.jsonl` ŌĆö an ordered list:
  `{slot, task_id, est_minutes, reason}`, greedily packed to the budget, hardest-blunders
  first then thematic clusters.
- **Deterministic:** Yes ŌĆö greedy pack over a stable sort (by `class` severity, then
  `difficulty_hint`, then `task_id` as tiebreak). No RNG, no clock-derived ordering.
  **Time budget is an explicit input** (`--budget 30m`), mirroring the engine-budget
  discipline elsewhere.
- **Engine-dependent:** Nothing ŌĆö operates on already-produced artifacts.
- **8D forward note:** when 8D lands, replace the greedy pack with due-date scheduling and
  persist per-card review state keyed on `signatureCore()`; `session.jsonl`'s shape is the
  forward-compatible contract.

---

### Stage 11 ŌĆö Export reports

Emit the human-facing review (and a provenance manifest so the whole run is auditable and
reproducible).

- **Command (PDF study book):**
  `crtk book study --input session.book.toml --output review.pdf`
  (native PDF, [chess.book.study](src/chess/book/study/), no LaTeX)
- **Command (manifest):** the router writes `run-manifest.json` itself **[NEW]**
- **Input artifacts:** `session.jsonl`, `review.jsonl`, the puzzle/gap artifacts
- **Output artifacts:**
  - `review.pdf` (annotated study book ŌĆö diagrams + solution lines, every line validated
    through the shared core by [StudyBookValidator](src/chess/book/study/))
  - `run-manifest.json` **[NEW]** ŌĆö `{schema_version, crtk_version, git_commit,
    engine{path,version,protocol_sha256}, budgets{max_nodes,max_duration,multipv,threads},
    inputs:[{path,sha256}], outputs:[{path,sha256}], created_at}`
- **Deterministic:** The PDF interior is deterministic **diagram + SAN content**, but byte
  stability is **not currently guaranteed**: [Font.java](src/chess/pdf/document/Font.java)
  hardcodes a `/usr/share/texmf` Latin Modern path and falls back per-machine, and AWT font
  metrics drive line wrapping. Same machine ŌåÆ stable; cross-machine ŌåÆ not asserted (a real
  8I/J gap). The **manifest** is deterministic except for `created_at`.
- **Engine-dependent:** Report *content* inherits Stage 4's engine dependence; the
  manifest **records** the engine version/protocol hash so the dependence is auditable ŌĆö
  this is exactly the provenance 8I demands and that the existing exporters
  (`record dataset npy` writes **no** meta.json at all; verified
  [RecordDatasetExporter.java](src/chess/io/RecordDatasetExporter.java)) currently lack.
- **Cross-ref 8I:** reuse the
  [RunManifest](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java) pattern
  (`crtk.workbench.run-manifest.v1`, per-file SHA-256) ŌĆö do not invent a second provenance
  format. The pipeline manifest should be a sibling schema (`crtk.review.run-manifest.v1`).

---

```
                          run-manifest.json           created_at; PDF bytes machine-
                                                      dependent (font path, 8I/J gap)
```

**Reproducibility summary.** Stages 1-3, 5-8, 10 and the manifest are CRTK-deterministic.
Stages 4 and 9 (mine/elo) are the *only* genuinely engine-dependent stages and reproduce
byte-for-byte solely under pinned engine binary + protocol + `--threads 1` + explicit
node/time budgets ŌĆö which is why the Stage 11 manifest must record the engine version and
budgets (8I). Two non-engine determinism leaks to fix before shipping: directory-root
mine filenames embed `currentTimeMillis()` (use a file stem), and `book study` PDF bytes
depend on local fonts (cross-machine instability).

---

## 13. ML / research / data-generation plan

This section defines the *research workflow and reproducibility contract* for CRTK as a local-first dataset toolkit. It deliberately does **not** re-derive the per-exporter tensor mechanics covered in [┬¦8I](#) (npy/lc0/classifier fan-out, train==serve encoding, Filter-DSL labeling) nor the schema-artifact mechanics in [┬¦8F](#) (`crtk help --json`, `schemaVersion`, fail-loud parsing). It builds *on top of* both: ┬¦8F gives the schema spine, ┬¦8I gives the exporters, and ┬¦13 turns those into a reproducible pipeline a researcher can trust, audit, and cite.

The framing constraint is the project's own preserved value ŌĆö **reproducible datasets** ŌĆö which the codebase currently *overstates*. [wiki/datasets.md](wiki/datasets.md) claims exports are "deterministic down to the byte" and that each export ships a `meta.json`, but the audit below shows that promise is not kept for the largest exports. Closing that gap is the core of this section.

---

### 13.1 The reproducibility gap (grounded audit baseline)

Before planning new work, here was the verified baseline. Every claim was checked against source at audit time;
implementation status blocks below are the source of truth for completed fixes.

| Export | Sidecar metadata at audit time | Provenance fields | Determinism |
|---|---|---|---|
| `record dataset npy` | **none** ŌĆö only `<stem>.features.npy` + `<stem>.labels.npy` ([RecordDatasetExporter.java:121-122](src/chess/io/RecordDatasetExporter.java)) | none | byte-stable (pure static encode) |
| `record dataset lc0` | `<stem>.lc0.meta.json` ([RecordLc0Exporter.java:330-354](src/chess/io/RecordLc0Exporter.java)) | `rows_written`, `rows_skipped`, `encoding`, `weights_path` ŌĆö **no** version/git/sha | byte-stable |
| `record dataset classifier` | `<stem>.classifier.meta.json` ([ClassifierDatasetExporter.java:275,555-571](src/chess/io/ClassifierDatasetExporter.java)) | `encoder`, `shape`, filter DSLs, class counts, `recommended_pos_weight` ŌĆö **no** version/git/sha/input-hash | byte-stable |
| `record export training-jsonl` | **none** | per-row `source_file`, `source_record_index`, `stockfish_version` (= free-form `Record.engine` string), but `game_id`/`position_index`/`source_group_id` **hard-coded `null`** ([RecordTrainingJsonlCommand.java:501-534](src/application/cli/command/RecordTrainingJsonlCommand.java)) | byte-stable |
| `record export puzzle-jsonl` | **none** | requires an LC0 `.bin`; no run sidecar | depends on loaded net |
| `record export puzzle-elo-jsonl` | **none** | model id string `crtk-tree-v14-evidence-direct` embedded per row | **NOT guaranteed** ŌĆö tree scoring runs `Runtime.getRuntime().availableProcessors()` threads by default and parallelizes at `roots.size() >= 2000` ([PuzzleEloExporter.java:290,798](src/chess/io/PuzzleEloExporter.java)) |

Three concrete defects fell out of this audit:

1. **No `meta.json` cannot prove what produced it.** None of the sidecars record the `crtk` version, git commit, input file checksums, weights hash, or the command line. A `classifier.meta.json` from two different builds, two different input dumps, or two different filter strings can be byte-identical in its provenance section ŌĆö so it proves nothing.
2. **The largest text exports (`training-jsonl`, `puzzle-jsonl`, `puzzle-elo-jsonl`) have no sidecar at all.** These are the ML-grade label exports, and they are the *least* provenanced.
3. **`puzzle-elo-jsonl` is not reproducible by default.** Multi-threaded tree scoring with no documented ordering guarantee, defaulting to all cores, directly contradicts the byte-exact claim. ASSUMPTION: scoring is order-independent *per root* (each root tree is scored independently per [PuzzleEloExporter.java:836-840](src/chess/io/PuzzleEloExporter.java)), so the *values* should be stable even if row *order* is not ŌĆö but this is untested (the digest confirms no reproducibility regression exists) and must not be asserted until a golden test pins it.

A secondary defect that breaks the classifier pipeline out of the box: [Model.java:17](src/chess/nn/classifier/Model.java) sets `DEFAULT_WEIGHTS = models/classifier_21planes-...bin` but the shipped file is `models/puzzle-classifier_21planes-...bin`, so `loadDefault()` fails on a clean tree. This is a one-line fix and is listed under ┬¦8I; it is restated here because it silently breaks the classifier dataset/inference path that this section's pipelines depend on.

---

### 13.2 The provenance manifest (the central deliverable)

The single highest-leverage ML deliverable is a **uniform provenance manifest** emitted by *every* exporter, replacing the inconsistent per-exporter `meta.json` with one schema. This is cheap (the pattern already exists ŌĆö [RunManifest.java:29,427](src/application/gui/workbench/session/RunManifest.java) already computes per-file SHA-256 with schema string `crtk.workbench.run-manifest.v1`) and it is the precondition for every audit tool and notebook workflow below.

Proposed schema `crtk.dataset.manifest.v1` (one `<stem>.manifest.json` per export, alongside the tensors/JSONL):

```json
{
  "schema": "crtk.dataset.manifest.v1",
  "created": 1700000000000,
  "crtk_version": "1.0.0",
  "git_commit": "992e368...",
  "command": "record dataset classifier -i puzzles/ -o out/p --filter \"...\"",
  "exporter": "classifier",
  "inputs": [
    {"path": ".../puzzles.json", "bytes": 1048576, "sha256": "ab12..."}
  ],
  "outputs": [
    {"path": ".../p.classifier.inputs.npy", "bytes": 5376000, "sha256": "cd34..."},
    {"path": ".../p.classifier.labels.npy", "bytes": 4000,    "sha256": "ef56..."}
  ],
  "weights": {"path": "models/...bin", "sha256": "77aa..."},
  "engine_protocol": {"path": "config/default.engine.toml", "sha256": "99bb...", "engine_name": "Stockfish 16"},
  "label_policy": {
    "scheme": "classifier-binary-21plane",
    "row_filter": "leaf[gate=AND;break=1;nodes>=50000000]",
    "label_filter": "...",
    "positive_definition": "puzzle-DSL match",
    "recommended_pos_weight": 3.41
  },
  "row_count": 1000,
  "rows_skipped": {"invalid": 2, "missing_position": 0, "row_filter": 17, "class_cap": 0},
  "determinism": {"byte_stable": true, "thread_count": 1}
}
```

Design rules:

- **Reuse, don't reinvent.** `RunManifest.sha256(Path)` and its path-entry shape are the template; promote that logic into a `chess.io` helper (e.g. `DatasetManifest`) so the CLI exporters and the workbench `RunManifest` share one implementation. This keeps the one-shared-core discipline and avoids a third copy of SHA-256 plumbing.
- **`crtk_version` + `git_commit` are the single source of truth for "what build produced this."** This pairs with the ┬¦8J fix to single-source the version (today duplicated in [VersionCommand.java:20](src/application/cli/command/VersionCommand.java) and `package.json`). The manifest must read the *same* constant `crtk version --json` reports.
- **`row_hashes` (optional, opt-in via `--row-hashes`).** For datasets used as training corpora, emit a sibling `<stem>.rowhashes.txt` of one `sha256(raw-record-json-v1)` digest per logical output row. This is what makes cross-split leakage detection (┬¦13.3) and dedup (┬¦13.4) auditable rather than asserted, while leaving room for a later semantic FEN+label hash as a new algorithm.
- **`engine_protocol` sha + `weights` sha are mandatory whenever an engine or net touched the export.** `puzzle-jsonl` loads an LC0 net; `puzzle-elo-jsonl` runs a tree search; external-engine analysis stamps `Record.engine`. Today the only engine identity captured is the free-form `Record.engine` string (which [┬¦8 external-engine digest] notes can be a filesystem *path*). The manifest must hash the protocol TOML and capture the engine `id name` line from the handshake, not just a label.

This depends on **┬¦8F** for the `schemaVersion`/catalog spine and pairs with **┬¦8I** for the exporter-side changes; ┬¦13 owns the *manifest schema and the cross-export uniformity*, ┬¦8I owns the per-exporter wiring.

---

### 13.3 Deterministic splits without leakage

CRTK has **no train/val/test split anywhere** (the digest confirms the only `--split` in the repo is GPU perft, unrelated; `record files --max-records` only shards by count into `.part-NNNN`). For an ML toolkit this is a first-class missing feature, and doing it wrong is the most common silent ML bug.

Plan: add a `record split` action (noun-verb consistent) operating on `.record`/JSONL streams:

```
crtk record split -i corpus.jsonl -o out/ \
  --ratio 0.8:0.1:0.1 \
  --seed 42 \
  --group-by position-signature \
  --names train,val,test
```

Hard requirements, each tied to a leakage failure mode:

- **Group-aware splitting is the default, not an option.** Chess datasets leak through *transpositions* and *sister positions*. Two records that reach the same position (identical `Position.signatureCore()`, the FNV digest per [Position.java:457](src/chess/core/Position.java)) must land in the *same* split, or a model memorizes the eval in train and is graded on it in val. `--group-by position-signature` is the floor. For game-derived corpora (┬¦8C/┬¦8A), `--group-by game-id` must be available so all positions from one game stay together. NOTE: `signatureCore` is FNV-1a, not a collision-resistant hash; for split-grouping that is acceptable (a collision merely co-locates two unrelated positions into one split ŌĆö conservative, not leaky), but the manifest must document the grouping key so a downstream consumer knows the guarantee.
- **The split is a deterministic function of `(row_hash, seed)`, never of input order or wall clock.** Assign each group to a bucket by `hash(seed || group_key) mod 10000` then partition by ratio. This makes the split reproducible from the manifest alone and immune to the input being re-ordered or re-merged.
- **The split emits a manifest per output** (┬¦13.2) plus a top-level `split.manifest.json` recording the ratio, seed, grouping key, group count per split, and a SHA-256 of the *sorted union of row hashes* across all splits ŌĆö so a reviewer can prove the splits partition the corpus with no overlap and no dropped rows.
- **Leakage audit is a separate verb, not a comment.** `crtk record audit-split --splits train.jsonl,val.jsonl,test.jsonl` reports any `position-signature` (or `game-id`) appearing in more than one split, and exits non-zero if found. This is the test that catches the bug the `--group-by` default is meant to prevent ŌĆö defense in depth.

**Implementation status (2026-06-16):**

- [x] Added `crtk record split` with deterministic counter-insensitive FEN grouping, seed-stable buckets, JSONL outputs, and per-output manifests.
- [x] Added split manifest metadata for split strategy, split spec, and seed.
- [x] Added `crtk record audit-split --splits A,B,C` leakage detector with `--split-by`/`--group-by` support and `RecordAuditSplitRegressionTest`.
- [x] Added top-level aggregate `<prefix>.split.manifest.json` with per-split row counts and a sorted raw-record row-hash digest.
- [x] Added `crtk record split --row-hashes`, emitting `<prefix>.<split>.rowhashes.txt` with one raw-record SHA-256 per output row and manifest coverage for the sidecars.
- [x] Added exporter-level `--row-hashes` sidecars for tensor/text dataset exports (`record dataset npy|lc0|classifier` and `record export training-jsonl|puzzle-jsonl|puzzle-elo-jsonl`), using the shared raw-record row-hash primitive and manifest coverage for the sidecars.

---

### 13.4 Dedup

The digest confirms **no dataset-level dedup exists** ŌĆö records stream straight through to tensors and JSONL; dedup lives only in the mining frontier and `PuzzleEloExporter` tree-building. The workbench `DatasetPanel` even *displays* a uniqueness ratio, implying duplicates are expected but never removed.

Plan: `crtk record dedup -i corpus.jsonl -o unique.jsonl --key position-signature [--keep first|last|highest-depth]`.

- Default key is `position-signature` (canonical FEN via `signatureCore`); `--key fen-exact` for byte-exact FEN; `--key row-hash` for the full FEN+label tuple.
- `--keep highest-depth` resolves collisions by preferring the record whose `analysis` reached the greatest PV1 depth (so dedup *improves* label quality rather than picking arbitrarily). Falls back to `first` when no analysis present.
- Emits a manifest with `rows_in`, `rows_out`, `duplicates_removed`, and the dedup key ŌĆö so the dedup is auditable, not a black box.
- **Order of operations matters and must be documented:** dedup *before* split (so the split sees unique groups) but *after* label assignment (so `--keep highest-depth` can see labels). A pipeline that splits then dedups can re-introduce leakage.

**Implementation status (2026-06-16):**

- [x] Added canonical `crtk record dedupe` plus `dedup` alias.
- [x] Added deterministic keys: `position-signature`, `fen-exact`, and `row-hash`.
- [x] Added `--keep first|last`, JSONL output, manifest sidecar, help/catalog wiring, and `RecordDedupeRegressionTest`.
- [ ] `--keep highest-depth` is intentionally reserved until analysis-depth extraction is pinned to the canonical record analysis schema.

---

### 13.5 Label policies

Today label policy is scattered and stringly-typed: the `training-jsonl` coarse/fine scheme is hard-coded in [RecordTrainingJsonlCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/RecordTrainingJsonlCommand.java) (`verified_puzzle=1/2`, `verified_near_puzzle=1/1`, `known_non_puzzle=0/0`), the classifier positive class is a Filter-DSL string, and the puzzle Elo "label" is a heuristic rating from a 73KB hand-tuned `Scorer` ([┬¦8 puzzle digest]). There is no single place that names the label policy, and the `meta.json` captures only fragments.

The plan does **not** unify these into one scheme (they serve genuinely different tasks). Instead:

- **The manifest's `label_policy` block is the contract.** Every exporter records its scheme name, the exact DSLs, and the positive-class definition. A consumer reads `label_policy.scheme` and knows how to interpret the labels without reverse-engineering the exporter.
- **The puzzle-Elo rating must be labeled as corpus-internal, in the manifest, not just in package docs.** [Difficulty.java] already warns "the rating is Elo-like only inside the puzzle corpus ŌĆ” should not be presented as a player strength estimate." That caveat must travel *with the data* ŌĆö `label_policy.scheme: "crtk-tree-v14-evidence-direct"` plus `"calibrated_to_humans": false`. Otherwise a downstream researcher trains on it as if it were a Lichess rating.
- **Filter-DSL is the one place label logic is already reproducible** ŌĆö it round-trips losslessly via `FilterDSL.fromString`/`toString` ([Filter.java:81-103,353](src/chess/uci/Filter.java)) and is deterministic. Lean on it: the manifest stores the canonical (re-serialized) DSL, not the user's raw input string, so two semantically-identical filters produce identical manifests.

**Implementation status (2026-06-16):**

- [x] Added a shared manifest metadata hook so exporter-specific policy fields still flow through one provenance writer.
- [x] `record dataset classifier` manifests now stamp `label_policy`, label source/positive definition, row counts, skip counts, optional filters, and optional class caps.
- [x] `record export training-jsonl` manifests now stamp `label_policy`, the canonical puzzle filter, coarse/fine label definition, row counts, invalid count, class counts, puzzle-parent count, and `include_engine_metadata`.
- [x] `record export puzzle-jsonl` manifests now stamp `label_policy`, LC0 label definition, selector, optional filters, row counts, skip counts, and the supplied weights hash.
- [x] `record export puzzle-elo-jsonl` manifests now stamp `label_policy`, rating source, puzzle filter, row counts, tree caps/thread count for direct scoring, and `calibrated_to_humans=false` with `rating_scope=corpus-internal`.
- [ ] The manifest still uses flat metadata keys; promoting `label_policy` to a nested block remains a future schema bump.

---

### 13.6 Export formats: JSONL canonical, Parquet/HF as recipes

CRTK's value is *producing reproducible, framework-agnostic artifacts*, not bundling a data stack. The boundary: ship `.npy` + `.jsonl` + manifest natively (no third-party Java deps ŌĆö preserved value), and provide **conversion recipes** rather than native Parquet/Arrow writers.

- **JSONL is the canonical interchange format.** It is already the default for `analyze-batch`/`bestmove-batch`/`training-jsonl`/`puzzle-*-jsonl`, it streams, and it is the natural unit for row-hashing. Standardize that every JSONL exporter (a) writes one object per line, (b) uses `utility.Json` (not hand-built `StringBuilder` ŌĆö the digest flags `EngineBatchCommand` for hand-rolling JSON, a drift risk), and (c) emits a sidecar manifest.
- **`.npy` for tensors** ŌĆö already framework-agnostic; `numpy.load` reads it directly, and `torch.from_numpy` / `tf.convert_to_tensor` are one call away.
- **Parquet/HF as documented recipes**, shipped in [wiki/datasets.md](wiki/datasets.md) and as a `tools/` Python script (NOT a Java dependency). A recipe is: `crtk record export training-jsonl` ŌåÆ `python tools/jsonl_to_parquet.py` (pandas/pyarrow, user-installed) ŌåÆ `datasets.load_dataset("parquet", ...)`. The manifest's `git_commit`/`crtk_version`/input hashes become the HF dataset card's provenance fields verbatim. This keeps the heavy data-stack dependency on the user's side of the boundary while making the conversion mechanical and the provenance carry through.

ASSUMPTION: the project will not accept a Java Parquet writer (it would pull in `parquet-mr` + Hadoop transitive deps, violating the zero-third-party-dep build). The recipe approach is the only one consistent with `javac --release 17` + no Maven/Gradle.

---

### 13.7 Audit tools

Provenance is worthless if it cannot be checked. Three small CLI verbs make the manifest *enforceable*:

1. **`crtk dataset verify -i <export-dir>`** ŌĆö re-hashes every output file listed in the manifest and confirms it matches; re-hashes inputs if still present; confirms `crtk_version` matches the current binary. Exits non-zero on any mismatch. This is the "did this dataset get corrupted / silently regenerated by a different build?" check.
2. **`crtk record audit-split`** (┬¦13.3) ŌĆö leakage detector across splits.
3. **`crtk dataset diff -a <manifest-a> -b <manifest-b>`** ŌĆö explains *why* two exports differ: different input hashes? different filter DSL? different crtk version? different weights hash? This turns "my results changed and I don't know why" into a one-command answer, which is exactly the audit the determinism claim implies but cannot currently deliver.

All three are pure-Java, read JSON via `utility.Json`, and depend only on ┬¦8F's `schemaVersion` discipline so they can reject manifests of unknown schema rather than misparsing them.

---

### 13.8 Notebook / Python integration

The integration story is **read the artifacts, don't wrap the JVM per-cell** ŌĆö until ┬¦8E lands a localhost daemon, every CLI call pays JVM startup (the digest flags this latency), so a notebook should *generate datasets via the CLI/batch once* and then *analyze the artifacts in Python*.

- **`tools/crtk_dataset.py`** (a thin, dependency-light helper, not a heavyweight SDK): `load_export(dir)` returns `(inputs_ndarray, labels_ndarray, manifest_dict)` by reading the `.npy` files and the `.manifest.json`; `verify(dir)` shells out to `crtk dataset verify` and raises on mismatch. This is ~50 lines of numpy + json and carries no provider-specific dependency.
- **Provenance is first-class in the notebook.** The first cell prints `manifest["crtk_version"]`, `git_commit`, and input hashes, so a published notebook embeds its own reproducibility receipt.
- **Generation from a notebook uses `batch run`**, which reuses one JVM across many commands ([┬¦8 CLI digest]): write a `pipeline.crtk` script (one command per line), call `crtk batch run -i pipeline.crtk --keep-going`, then load the outputs. This amortizes JVM startup over the whole pipeline instead of per cell.
- This depends on **┬¦8F** (so `tools/crtk_dataset.py` can validate against published schemas) and is strengthened by **┬¦8E** (a daemon would let interactive cells call CRTK without re-spawning the JVM). It does not block on either ŌĆö the artifact-reading path works today against `.npy` + manifest.

---

### 13.9 Concrete sample pipelines

Each produces *named, manifested* artifacts and is reproducible from its manifest alone. These assume the ┬¦13.2 manifest, ┬¦13.3 split, and ┬¦13.4 dedup verbs exist; where a verb is new it is flagged `[new]`.

#### Pipeline A ŌĆö Puzzle-detection classifier dataset (mine ŌåÆ dedup ŌåÆ split ŌåÆ export)

```bash
### 1. Mine puzzles from a PGN of master games, bounded and reproducible.
crtk puzzle mine -i masters.pgn -o dump/mined \
    --protocol-path config/default.engine.toml \
    --max-nodes 5000000 --max-duration 30s \
    --engine-instances 4
### -> dump/mined.puzzles.json, dump/mined.nonpuzzles.json

### 2. Dedup by canonical position, keeping the deepest analysis.   [new ┬¦13.4]
crtk record dedup -i dump/mined.puzzles.json -o dump/unique.jsonl \
    --key position-signature --keep highest-depth
### -> dump/unique.jsonl + dump/unique.manifest.json

### 3. Group-aware split (transpositions cannot leak across splits). [new ┬¦13.3]
crtk record split -i dump/unique.jsonl -o dump/splits/ \
    --ratio 0.8:0.1:0.1 --seed 42 --group-by position-signature
### -> dump/splits/{train,val,test}.jsonl + split.manifest.json

### 4. Export the train split to 21-plane classifier tensors.
crtk record dataset classifier -i dump/splits/train.jsonl -o dump/ds/train \
    --filter "leaf[gate=AND;break=1;nodes>=5000000]" --row-hashes
### -> dump/ds/train.classifier.inputs.npy, .labels.npy,
###    .classifier.meta.json, train.rowhashes.txt, train.classifier.manifest.json

### 5. Audit: prove no position leaks across splits, verify hashes.
crtk record audit-split --splits dump/splits/train.jsonl,dump/splits/val.jsonl,dump/splits/test.jsonl
crtk dataset verify -i dump/ds/                                    # [new ┬¦13.7]
```

Reproducibility receipt: `train.manifest.json` pins the `crtk` version, git commit, the SHA-256 of `train.jsonl`, the Stockfish protocol hash + handshake `id name`, the filter DSL, and the seed (carried from the split manifest). Re-running steps 3ŌĆō4 on the same `unique.jsonl` with the same seed reproduces byte-identical tensors; `crtk dataset verify` proves it.

#### Pipeline B ŌĆö LC0 value/policy training tensors with weights provenance

```bash
### 1. Analyze a position corpus with an external reference engine (batch, JSONL).
crtk engine analyze-batch -i positions.fen -o dump/analyzed.jsonl \
    --protocol-path config/default.engine.toml \
    --max-nodes 1000000 --multipv 2

### 2. Convert analyzed records to a .record file (parent/position linkage).
###    (record files merges/normalizes the JSONL into the record container.)
crtk record files -i dump/analyzed.jsonl -o dump/corpus.record.json

### 3. Export LC0 112-plane inputs + policy + value, stamping the net's hash.
crtk record dataset lc0 -i dump/corpus.record.json -o dump/lc0/run1 \
    --weights models/leela_112planes-10blocksx128.bin
### -> dump/lc0/run1.lc0.{inputs,policy,value}.npy, .lc0.meta.json, run1.manifest.json
###    manifest.weights.sha256 = <hash of the .bin>  [┬¦13.2]
```

This pipeline's value is that `run1.manifest.json` records the *weights hash*, the *engine protocol hash*, and the *analysis budget* (`--max-nodes 1000000 --multipv 2`). Two LC0 datasets that differ only because someone swapped the net file are now distinguishable by `crtk dataset diff`, which today is impossible because `lc0.meta.json` stores only `weights_path` (a string), not a hash ([RecordLc0Exporter.java:342](src/chess/io/RecordLc0Exporter.java)).

#### Pipeline C ŌĆö Notebook-driven analysis of a manifested export

```python
### tools/crtk_dataset.py usage, in a Jupyter cell.
import subprocess, tools.crtk_dataset as cd

X, y, manifest = cd.load_export("dump/ds/train")     # numpy + manifest dict
assert manifest["schema"] == "crtk.dataset.manifest.v1"
print("crtk", manifest["crtk_version"], "@", manifest["git_commit"][:8])
print("input sha256:", manifest["inputs"][0]["sha256"][:12])

cd.verify("dump/ds/train")        # raises if any output hash drifted
### ... train a torch model on X, y; the cell output embeds the provenance receipt.
```

The notebook never starts a JVM; it reads the `.npy` + manifest produced by Pipeline A. The provenance fields printed in cell 1 are exactly what a published reproduction needs.

---

### 13.10 Sequencing and dependencies

- **Depends on ┬¦8F** (schema spine: `schemaVersion`, `crtk help --json`, fail-loud parsing) ŌĆö the manifest, the audit tools, and the Python helper all validate against ┬¦8F's published schemas. Build ┬¦8F first.
- **Pairs with ┬¦8I** (exporter wiring) ŌĆö ┬¦8I adds the missing `meta.json` to `npy` and the JSONL exports and fixes the classifier default-weights path; ┬¦13 defines the *uniform manifest schema* those exporters emit and owns the cross-export consistency.
- **Feeds ┬¦8A/┬¦8C** ŌĆö the `game-id` grouping key for splits only becomes meaningful once ┬¦8A's PGN store assigns stable game ids (today `training-jsonl` hard-codes `game_id: null`). Until then, `--group-by position-signature` is the available guarantee.
- **The reproducibility regression test is the acceptance gate.** `DatasetDeterminismRegressionTest` now runs the deterministic dataset/export paths twice and asserts byte-identical tensor/JSONL outputs, with documented path-bearing manifest fields stripped before structural comparison. A separate future check should still assert `puzzle-elo-jsonl` rating-value equality across thread counts (or the byte-exact claim should stay scoped to fixed thread/budget settings).

#### Effort / priority

| Item | Effort | Priority | Note |
|---|---|---|---|
| Uniform `crtk.dataset.manifest.v1` (reuse `RunManifest` sha logic) | medium | P1 | core deliverable; unblocks everything else |
| Fix classifier `DEFAULT_WEIGHTS` path | trivial | P0 | done; constant matches `models/puzzle-classifier_...bin` and is covered by `ClassifierModelRegressionTest` |
| `record split` (group-aware, seeded) | medium | P1 | most common silent ML bug if absent |
| `record dedup` | small | P1 | done for `first|last`; `highest-depth` reserved pending schema-pinned depth extraction |
| `crtk dataset verify` / `diff`, `record audit-split` | small | P1 | done for manifest verify/audit/diff and split leakage audit |
| Weights/protocol hashing in manifest | small | P1 | distinguishes net/engine swaps |
| Determinism + leakage regression tests | medium | P1 | the acceptance gate |
| `tools/crtk_dataset.py` + Parquet/HF recipes | small | P2 | downstream of manifest |
| `--row-hashes` opt-in | small | P2 | done for `record split` and dataset/export sidecars |

---

## 14. Grounded explanation plan

The full grounded-explanation deep-dive lives in **[Section 8G](#8g-grounded-explanation-layer-and-section-14-detail)** (theme G: P1, build-later, depends on C and F). This section surfaces the four load-bearing specifics ŌĆö the **verifier**, the **deterministic fallback**, the **audience model**, and the **test strategy** ŌĆö so the grounding guarantee reads as one contract; it does not repeat 8G's CLI surface, schema bodies, or file list (see 8G for those).

Grounded explanation is the project's single most-protected value, and it is the one theme that is `present` rather than `partial`/`absent`. So the work is *deepening and hardening an existing capability*, not greenfield ŌĆö and the most important new artifact is **not a model, it is a verifier** that makes "grounded" enforceable instead of aspirational.

### 14.1 The verifier (the central new artifact)

`chess.explain.Verifier` takes a `Position`, a structured `Rationale`, and a prose string and returns `Verdict{grounded, violations[]}`. It rejects, at the claim level:

- any SAN/UCI that is not a legal move from the position ([MoveGenerator](src/chess/core/MoveGenerator.java) + [SAN.fromAlgebraic](src/chess/core/SAN.java));
- any "captures X" claim whose destination square holds no such piece (or is not the en-passant pawn);
- any opening name not returned by [Encyclopedia.name(pos)](src/chess/eco/Encyclopedia.java) (empty for Chess960 ŌĆö no fabricated names);
- any "mate in N" not backed by a [MateProver](src/chess/engine/MateProver.java) `Proof` (proven, never estimated);
- any "only move" claim without structured evidence (MateProver proof or a multipv gap) ŌĆö otherwise downgraded to "the natural choice";
- a declared side-to-move / eval-sign that contradicts the [PositionDescriptionInput.Evaluation](src/chess/describe/PositionDescriptionInput.java).

The verifier operates on *extracted claim tokens*, not whole sentences, so it never rejects legitimate general-chess aphorisms; `phase` is a crude material-ratio bucket and is marked `heuristic` confidence and **excluded** from hard verification (verifying it would reject the classical generator's own faithful output). This implements the inference-time grounding pass that [ARCHITECTURE.md](src/chess/describe/ARCHITECTURE.md):157-158 documents but never coded.

### 14.2 The deterministic fallback (structural, not optional)

`ExplanationGenerator.generate()` **always** computes the classical, faithful-by-construction prose first ([ClassicalPositionDescriptionGenerator](src/chess/describe/ClassicalPositionDescriptionGenerator.java)). A model path, if a `--model` is supplied, is only a *replacement candidate* that must pass the verifier; on any violation it regenerates once, then falls back to the classical text. This guarantees the no-hallucination value holds even with a buggy or garbage model. The one model runtime is the *working* in-process [chess.nn.t5.Runner](src/chess/nn/t5/Runner.java) (no deps, CPU greedy decode) with the [TagPrompt](src/chess/nn/t5/TagPrompt.java) "do not invent moves" instruction ŌĆö **not** the permanently-dead describe-package stub ([T5PositionDescriptionGenerator](src/chess/describe/T5PositionDescriptionGenerator.java), `available()==false`), which is retired. No weights ship; absence is a first-class state that yields `prose_source: "classical-fallback"`, exit 0 (or exit 3 under `--strict-grounding`).

### 14.3 The audience model

A single `--audience` flag (`beginner | club | advanced | coach | researcher | engine-debug | ml`, default `club`) controls *which* facts and *what register* ŌĆö never *whether* a claim is true. Audience tuning rides the classical generator's existing `--detail` mechanism plus per-audience fact-selection and lexicon profiles over [DescriptionLexicon](src/chess/describe/DescriptionLexicon.java); the `ml`/`researcher` end emits `--facts-only` (the machine-readable `crtk.explain.rationale.v1` rationale, every fact carrying a `grounded_by` provenance pointer), while the human end emits verified prose. Engine-debug facts that surface external-engine node counts are marked `source: external` and excluded from `training-jsonl` to keep that export reproducible.

### 14.4 Test strategy (assert the verifier and the facts, never the wording)

Tests pin *what CRTK does*, not exact sentences (golden-string prose is brittle). `ExplainRegressionTest` asserts: the verifier rejects each of illegal move / fabricated opening / impossible capture / unproven only-move / eval-sign contradiction; the classical prose **always** verifies `grounded==true` over a fixture set (incl. Chess960, mate, stalemate, insufficient material) ŌĆö the core invariant; an absent/garbage model falls back silently; `--facts-only --format jsonl` emits one rationale per line with no prose; engine-eval is deterministic on repeat. The test is wired into the `core`/`cli`/CI targets of [run_regression_suite.sh](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh) ŌĆö explicitly avoiding the "unwired test rots" failure mode. See **[Section 8G](#8g-grounded-explanation-layer-and-section-14-detail)** for the full schema bodies, CLI surface, and acceptance criteria.

---

## 15. Packaging / onboarding plan

The full packaging & onboarding deep-dive lives in **[Section 8J](#8j-packaging--onboarding-and-section-15-detail)** (theme J: P2, build-later, with cheap P0/P1 correctness bugs carved out). This section surfaces the tranche structure and the onboarding/cross-platform specifics so the packaging story reads as one piece; it does not repeat 8J's CLI surface, file list, testing plan, or acceptance criteria.

The honest framing (from 8J): packaging is *solid but Linux-only and partly inaccurate*. The work splits into three tranches that **must not be conflated**, and the plain `javac --release 17` + `jar` build path stays sacrosanct throughout ŌĆö any packaging tooling (jpackage, fpm, scoop manifests) is optional, lives in `scripts/`/`packaging/`, and never touches the compile path.

### 15.1 Tranche 1 ŌĆö cheap correctness bugs that mislead a new user (P0/P1, hours)

These mislead a brand-new user on first run and fold into the M (roadmap reconciliation) and I (provenance) work:

- **Fix the false jar claim.** [getting-started.md](wiki/getting-started.md):48 says "a prebuilt `crtk.jar` ships in the repository root," but `crtk.jar` is gitignored ([.gitignore](.gitignore):31), so a clean clone's `java -jar crtk.jar version` fails. Lead onboarding with a build step.
- **Single-source the version.** `VERSION = "1.0.0"` in [VersionCommand.java](src/application/cli/command/VersionCommand.java):20 and [package.json](package.json):3 duplicate the literal with no enforcement; add a regression that asserts agreement.
- **Verify weight downloads.** [install.sh](install.sh) fetches NNUE/LC0/BT4 with no checksum; converge it onto the sha256-verifying path already in [fetch_lc0_net.sh](scripts/fetch_lc0_net.sh) (shared with theme I).
- **Fix the classifier default-weights path drift** ([Model.java](src/chess/nn/classifier/Model.java)) so `loadDefault()` works out of the box.

### 15.2 Tranche 2 ŌĆö onboarding ergonomics (P2, the real initiative)

A thin `crtk setup` orchestrates the existing [DoctorCommand](src/application/cli/command/DoctorCommand.java)/[ConfigOps](src/application/cli/ConfigOps.java) checks, seeds config, prints OS-specific Stockfish hints, optionally downloads the default net (showing size + SHA-256 and verifying after), and ends with three copy-pasteable commands. Companion verbs: `crtk engine detect`/`install-hints`, a hash-checked `crtk model list|download|verify` that supersedes the two divergent fetch paths via a single tracked `config/models.toml`, `crtk examples install`, and `crtk doctor --json`/`--fix-suggestions` + `crtk config show --json` (the JSON surfaces depend on F's schema work). `crtk setup` *advises* and downloads user-space artifacts only ŌĆö it never `sudo`s or installs system packages; `install.sh` stays the privileged path.

### 15.3 Tranche 3 ŌĆö cross-platform distribution (P2/P3, deferrable)

Java itself is portable; *only the packaging is Linux/apt-only*. The safe path that does not break the simple build: keep the portable jar as the universal baseline, ship a **CPU-only cross-platform tarball/zip** next (no native libs ŌćÆ no `java.library.path` complexity), then add `jpackage`/jlink self-contained bundles and community manifests (`.deb` via fpm, Homebrew, Scoop, winget) last ŌĆö each fetching the already-built jar rather than recompiling. The cross-platform launchers must replicate the Linux launcher's `cd $APP_HOME` behavior to dodge the CWD-relative `config/`/`models/` footgun. See **[Section 8J](#8j-packaging--onboarding-and-section-15-detail)** for the model-catalog schema, the `doctor --json` shape, the full CLI surface, and the per-tranche testing plan.

---

## 16. GitHub issue breakdown

This section turns the theme verdicts into single-PR-sized GitHub issues, grouped into milestones. Ordering reflects the dependency chain established in the theme map: **M0 (reconcile reality) ŌåÆ M1 (schemas/catalog, the precondition for everything machine-facing) ŌåÆ M2 (PGN DB) ŌåÆ M3 (reviewŌåÆstudy) ŌåÆ M4 (explanation) ŌåÆ M5 (serve+SDK) ŌåÆ M6 (workbench personas) ŌåÆ M7 (packaging) ŌåÆ M8 (dataset/ML)**.

Conventions used below:
- **Priority** P0ŌĆōP3 mirror the theme map; an issue's priority can exceed its milestone's headline priority when it is a correctness landmine.
- File links are repo-root-relative. "Runner target" means `./scripts/run_regression_suite.sh <target>` (targets confirmed in [run_regression_suite.sh](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh): `build lint scripts core cli engine uci book docs perft-smoke jar recommended ci release`).
- Every issue is scoped to be one PR. Where a theme is large (A, C), it is split into 3ŌĆō5 issues that each land independently.

A standing constraint applies to all issues: preserve the core values ŌĆö one shared chess core, deterministic outputs, plain `javac --release 17` (no Maven/Gradle, no third-party Java deps), CLI-is-source-of-truth with the Workbench mirroring it, stable JSON/JSONL contracts, grounded explanations. Any new CLI verb must follow noun-then-verb and be registered in [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java).

---

### Milestone M0 ŌĆö Finish existing TODO / reconcile roadmap

The current [TODO.txt](TODO.txt) tells contributors to rebuild finished code. These issues are tiny, mostly documentation/test wiring, and must land first so nobody redoes shipped work.

#### M0-1 ŌĆö Reconcile TODO.txt with HEAD; strike stale rebuild instructions

**Context:** [TODO.txt](TODO.txt) calls `src/chess/tag/Threats.java` an "11-byte stub" (it is a real 10,600-byte impl wired into [Generator.java](src/chess/tag/Generator.java) at `addStructuralThreats`), and frames the OTIS CUDA backend as greenfield "add a CUDA implementation" when `native/cuda/build/libotis_cuda.so` is already built (Jun 5) with a Java wrapper.

Mark interleaved `[DONE]` Tag Engine items as closed. Add the genuinely-absent product themes (PGN DB, reviewŌåÆstudy, schemas) as new sections so the roadmap reflects the real plan.
**Acceptance criteria:**
- [x] No instruction in TODO.txt asks to rebuild a file that already exists with a real implementation.
- [x] OTIS CUDA section describes optimization, not initial implementation.
- [x] A grep for "11-byte stub" in TODO.txt returns nothing.
**Tests to run:** none (docs-only); `./scripts/run_regression_suite.sh lint` (whitespace/conflict-marker check).

#### M0-6 ŌĆö Single-source the version string
**Priority:** P2

**Implementation notes:** Without adding a build system, the cheapest enforcement is a tiny regression test that reads both literals and asserts equality, plus (optionally) `crtk version` parity with `git describe`. Keep `VersionCommand.VERSION` the canonical Java source.

**Labels:** `release`, `testing`, `P2`.

#### M0-7 ŌĆö Register dynamic tag families in Sort/Literals and document in SCHEMA.md
**Priority:** P1
**Context:** The game-analysis families `MOVE_EFFECT/LINE/VARIATION/GAME` are real impls ([MoveEffect.java](src/chess/tag/MoveEffect.java), [GameAnalyzer.java](src/chess/tag/game/GameAnalyzer.java)) but are absent from `Sort.FAMILY_ORDER` ([Sort.java](src/chess/tag/Sort.java), 20 static families only) and [Literals.java](src/chess/tag/core/Literals.java), using inline string literals. They bypass the canonical sort/dedupe/Delta/Filter pipeline ŌĆö a structural fork that blocks game-review-to-study (M3).
**Implementation notes:** Add the four family names to `Literals` constants and append them to `Sort.FAMILY_ORDER` (after `GAME`-appropriate position). Replace inline `"MOVE_EFFECT: san="` / `"GAME: "` literals with the new constants. Document the four families and the `--analyze-game` flag in [SCHEMA.md](tag/SCHEMA.md) (they are currently documented only in [GAME_ANALYSIS.md](tag/GAME_ANALYSIS.md)).
**Acceptance criteria:**
- [x] `Sort.sort()` orders and dedupes dynamic-family lines deterministically.
- [x] No inline dynamic-family prefix literals remain in `MoveEffect`/`GameAnalyzer`/`LineAnalyzer`/`VariationAnalyzer`.
- [x] SCHEMA.md documents all four dynamic families and `fen tags --analyze-game`.
**Tests to run:** `testing.TaggingRegressionTest`, `testing.TagFixtureRegressionTest` via `./scripts/run_regression_suite.sh core`.
**Docs to update:** [tag/SCHEMA.md](tag/SCHEMA.md), [tag-reference.md](wiki/tag-reference.md).
**Labels:** `tag-engine`, `schema`, `P1`.

#### M0-8 ŌĆö OTIS CPUŌåöCUDA policy parity (per-legal-move refinement)
**Priority:** P2
**Context:** [Backend.java](src/chess/nn/otis/cuda/Backend.java) (CUDA) returns raw policy-head logits and skips the per-legal-move refinement the pure-Java [Model.java](src/chess/nn/otis/Model.java) applies, so CUDA and CPU OTIS disagree at the policy level (WDL matches, policy does not).
**Implementation notes:** Apply the same per-legal-move refinement to the native-returned logits in `Backend` (the move generator lives Java-side), or document the divergence as intentional and make the parity test assert it explicitly. Prefer making them identical.
**Acceptance criteria:**
- [ ] `OtisBackendRegressionTest` asserts CPU and CUDA policy distributions match within tolerance when a device is present (skips cleanly otherwise).
**Tests to run:** `./scripts/run_regression_suite.sh engine` (`testing.OtisBackendRegressionTest`).
**Docs to update:** [gpu.md](wiki/gpu.md).
**Labels:** `nn-otis`, `gpu`, `correctness`, `P2`.

#### M0-9 ŌĆö Live-NN-visualization frame regression (Workbench)
**Priority:** P2
**Context:** TODO notes live search/NN visualization jumps from initial to final state (intermediate frames dropped) ŌĆö a regression, distinct from the deferred zoomable graph canvas.
**Implementation notes:** Add explicit render backpressure between the MCTS session and the Network/MCTS panels so incremental frames are emitted. Touch the MCTS/Network panel wiring under `src/application/gui/workbench/` (e.g. `MctsSearch`, Network observers).

**Docs to update:** [workbench.md](wiki/workbench.md).
**Labels:** `workbench`, `bug`, `P2`.
