| `crtk setup` + `engine detect` + `examples install` | extend `DoctorCommand`/`ConfigOps` + thin leaves | P2 | User-space onboarding orchestrator (never sudo); `--non-interactive` makes zero network calls; bounded `uci`+`quit` engine probe |
| TODO/URGENT-vs-HEAD drift checker + docs link/claim smoke | build-new dev-infra + extend docs target | P1 | Cross-references roadmap claims vs real file sizes (TODO calls a real ~278-line `Threats.java` an "11-byte stub"); fails on the false "prebuilt jar ships" claim and the stale "12 tabs" doc |
| `OtisBackendRegressionTest` policy-parity extension + stale-weights guard | extend `OtisBackendRegressionTest` + `Backend.java` | P2 | CUDA returns raw policy logits, skips the per-legal-move refinement the Java path applies ŌĆö assert CPUŌåöCUDA **policy** parity, not just WDL |
| Provenance-tagged gauntlet/SPRT match-record store + JSON `Result` serializer | extend `Gauntlet`/`EngineGauntletCommand` | P2 | Results are printed, never stored (a gap even vs Arena); persist reproducible, provenance-tagged match records |
| Workbench structure/mirror guards | extend `WorkbenchStructureRegressionTest` + `WorkbenchCommandRegression` | P1 | Ban `chess.io.*` writers from `application.gui.workbench.*`; make the mirror **catalog-backed** (consume `crtk help --json`, not in-process reflection); assert preview tokenizes to exactly the spawned argv |

### 22.3 Reuse, don't rebuild

The repo already ships most of the *rendering* and *harness* substrate; the new work is data/contract plumbing, not new frameworks.

| Already exists | What it is | Extend it for |
|---|---|---|
| `testing.TestSupport` + [run_regression_suite.sh](scripts/run_regression_suite.sh) | The only sanctioned harness (runMain/captureStdout/asserts) | Every new `*RegressionTest` ŌĆö public-static-`main`, wired into a named target, never JUnit |
| `WorkbenchCommandRegression` + `CommandTemplates` + `CommandRunner` | Already enforce GUIŌåÆCLI (child-JVM spawn, exact preview) | All new views ŌĆö extend, never embed a second impl; upgrade the regression to be catalog-backed |
| `RunManifest.sha256(Path)` (line 427), `crtk.workbench.run-manifest.v1` | The SHA-256 + provenance source of truth | Lift into shared `chess.io` ŌĆö do not write a second hasher |
| `GameReviewPanel`, `DatasetPanel`, `TreePanel`, `RelationsPanel`, `BoardPanel`, `InspectorPanel`, `AnalysisGraph`, `NnueTraceView` | The visualizers the review/dataset/explain inspectors need | Extend the panels; feed them CLI-produced artifacts |
| `DoctorCommand`, `VersionCommand`, `FenCommand --json`, `install.sh`, `fetch_lc0_net.sh` (`verify_sha256`) | Diagnostics + a working verified-download path | `doctor --json`; converge `install.sh`; single-source the version |
| `WorkbenchShots`/`WorkbenchRobotCapture`/`WorkbenchTestSupport` + `testdata/static.tsv` | Headless rendering + golden capture | Extend the corpus and reuse the renderers (note the pixel-diff gap in ┬¦22.5) |

### 22.4 Correctness landmines the tooling must catch

These are confirmed in-tree at `1ab42b9` ŌĆö the tools above exist partly to fence them off:

- `Sort.FAMILY_ORDER` (Sort.java:24) does **not** list MOVE_EFFECT/LINE/VARIATION/GAME ŌåÆ the four dynamic families bypass canonical sort/dedupe/Filter. Register + golden-fixture them **before** the review router consumes them.
- `install.sh` has **zero** sha256 checks while `fetch_lc0_net.sh` already verifies ŌĆö a supply-chain inconsistency.
- npy export writes **no** sidecar; `RecordLc0Exporter` and `ClassifierDatasetExporter` write **divergent** hand-rolled `meta.json` (lc0 stores a `weights_path` *string*, not a hash ŌĆö a swapped net is invisible). One shared `DatasetManifest` fixes all three.
- `OtisBackendRegressionTest` asserts WDL only; CPUŌåöCUDA disagree on **policy**.
- `Record.fromJson` returns `null` on malformed input (lines 456/462/475) ŌåÆ datasets silently shrink instead of failing loud.
- `Result.equals` includes `elapsedMillis`, and mining bakes `currentTimeMillis` into filenames ŌåÆ the byte-exact claim is untested until the determinism harness strips time fields and pins the excluded set.

### 22.5 Known tooling gaps (what the harness can't do today)

- **No golden-image diff.** `WorkbenchShots`/`WorkbenchRobotCapture` render PNGs but there is no pixel-baseline comparison; visual checks (live-NN frame-drop, persona/first-run) rely on component-tree dumps + bounded headless assertions, not image diffs.
- **No CI workflow files in `.github/`.** CI is a single sequential `ubuntu-latest` run with no per-step timeout; the import/review end-to-end and any Stockfish-gated tests must be bounded or moved to a non-blocking nightly, or they can hang the gate.
- **No aggregated log/progress store** beyond per-run `RunManifest` JSON; the daemon and batch-review progress will want observable progress (reuse `application.console.Bar`).
- **No distributed/container support.** All harnesses assume one machine; the 100k+-game store benchmark and the gauntlet match-record store will stress this.
- **Forward-declared schemas** (review/repertoire/db/import/dataset) ship as v1 *provisional* before A/C/D/I land ŌĆö accept a cheap v2 bump rather than guess the final shape.
- **`puzzle-elo-jsonl` parallelizes** (threads>1 at rootsŌēź2000) with reproducibility unproven on the parallel path ŌĆö either pin rating-value equality across thread counts or record `deterministic_under_threads:false` in the manifest.
- **Cross-machine PDF reproducibility** is bounded by the local Latin-Modern font path + AWT metrics; only same-machine byte-stability is achievable without bundling fonts.

---

## 23. CLI & GUI entrypoint design

Every capability in this plan enters through two doors: a **CLI verb** (the contract) and a **Workbench surface** (the mirror). This section specifies how both should look so new themes land consistently. It is grounded in the two house style guides ŌĆö [wiki/cli-command-guide.md](wiki/cli-command-guide.md) and [wiki/workbench-design-guide.md](wiki/workbench-design-guide.md) ŌĆö and treats their rules as binding, not aspirational.

### 23.1 The two contracts

Strategic principle #2 is load-bearing here: **the CLI is the contract; the GUI is a mirror.** New capability lands as a CLI verb first; no Workbench-only feature is allowed to be the only home of logic (the current PgnExplorer/GameReview in-memory state is exactly the anti-pattern this plan is closing).

The mirror is mechanical, not a guideline:

- The Workbench builds an exact `crtk ŌĆ”` command string and runs it by spawning the **real CLI in a child JVM** ([CommandRunner.java](src/application/gui/workbench/command/CommandRunner.java)`.javaInvocation`/`displayCommand`). The command preview a user sees *is* the runnable command.
- [WorkbenchCommandRegression.java](src/testing/WorkbenchCommandRegression.java) walks the registry and asserts every workbench template resolves to a real command.
- **Plan upgrade (M1/H):** make the mirror **catalog-backed** ŌĆö `WorkbenchCommandRegression` should consume `crtk help --json` (┬¦22) rather than in-process reflection, so it cannot drift when a jlinked runtime has a different classpath, and add `testCommandPreviewEqualsSpawnedArgs` (the preview tokenizes to exactly the spawned argv ŌĆö no hidden/dropped `--max-nodes`).

The result: there is exactly one chess core, one engine, one evaluator, one dataset path. A GUI surface is a *view onto a CLI verb plus its artifacts*, never a parallel implementation.

### 23.2 CLI entrypoint conventions (the shape every new verb takes)

Dispatch is process-per-invocation through [application.Main](src/application/Main.java) over the declarative tree in [CliRegistry.java](src/application/cli/CliRegistry.java). Every new verb obeys the existing contract:

| Rule | Requirement |
|---|---|
| Shape | `crtk <area> <action> [options] [args]`, noun-then-verb. Add a new **area** only for a durable domain; prefer an action on an existing noun |
| Names | Canonical reused tokens come from `application.cli.Constants`; never reintroduce legacy single-word forms (`moves`, `mine-puzzles`, ŌĆ”) |
| Flags | Named flags for structured values (`--fen`, `--input`, `--output`, `--format`, `--max-nodes`, `--max-duration`); positionals only for natural arguments (a move token, a short line) |
| Output | stdout stable and parseable; diagnostics on stderr; `--json`/`--jsonl` resolved through `CommandSupport.resolveOutputMode`; JSON only via `utility.Json` |
| Determinism | No wall-clock output, no hidden RNG defaults, no unstable ordering, no unbounded engine work |
| Core logic | Legality/FEN/SAN/UCI/Chess960/tagging/move application route through `chess.core` |
| Help | `crtk help <area> <action>` is ground truth; every flag appears there |
| Tests | Regression for success, failure, help, and machine-readable output |

**Contract additions this plan introduces** (all in ┬¦22):

- `crtk help --json` ŌĆö the whole area/action/flag/exit-code/example catalog (`crtk.cli.catalog.v1`), deterministic and generated.
- `crtk schema list|show|check` and `crtk record validate --strict` ŌĆö discoverable contracts + fail-loud ingestion.
- A documented **exit-code taxonomy** (`0` ok, `2` usage, `3` invalid input/FEN) used uniformly and asserted over the wire by the daemon.
- `schemaVersion` stamped into every on-disk artifact; `--max-nodes`/`--max-duration` budgets on every engine-touching verb.
- A second runtime entrypoint, `crtk serve` (┬¦22 G / Theme E), wraps the *same* `dispatch(args,stdin)` core under a lock ŌĆö a warm process, not a second implementation. Hard boundary: localhost only, no play/cloud endpoints.

New CLI areas this plan adds: `db` (or `pgn`), `import`, `review`, `study`, `repertoire`, `dataset`, `schema`, `model`, `setup`, `serve` ŌĆö each with the verb shapes detailed in ┬¦8 and mapped in ┬¦23.4.

### 23.3 GUI entrypoint conventions (the shape every surface takes)

**Launch entrypoints stay exactly three** (per [wiki/workbench.md](wiki/workbench.md)): `crtk workbench` / `crtk gui`, with `--fen <FEN>` and `--flip`/`--black-down`. No new launch flags; new capabilities are *surfaces inside* the shell, reached by navigation, not by new launch modes.

The shell is a VS Code-style editor frame driven by `ViewRegistry`/`SwitchedWorkspace`, organized into the design guide's **six target surfaces** ŌĆö `Dashboard`, `Board`, `Engine Lab`, `Run`, `Datasets`, `Publish` (plus the proposed 7th, `Library`, see ┬¦23.5). Every surface obeys the canonical contract:

| Convention | Rule (from the design guide) |
|---|---|
| Structure | Optional tab strip ŌåÆ `WorkspaceHeader` ŌåÆ optional toolbar band ŌåÆ body ŌåÆ optional 320ŌĆō380 px side rail ŌåÆ optional bottom panel |
| Layout | **Layout A** (editor + rail) for Board/Engine Lab/Run/Publish/Library; **Layout B** (scroll + grid) for Dashboard/Datasets/reports |
| Primitives | Color/font/spacing/radius/controls/scroll come only from `Theme`, `Ui`, `SurfacePanel`, `Card` ŌĆö no raw `JButton`/`JScrollPane`, no local color literals |
| Primary object | The header always answers: *what object am I looking at, what state is it in, what is the next action* |
| Toolbar | Apple-style leading (mode/nav) / center (view-shaping) / trailing (actions + search) grouping at VS Code density |
| States | Resting/hover/focus/selected/disabled/loading/error/missing/stale all designed; verified at 1000 px + 1600 px in light **and** dark |
| Command mirror | Any surface that runs work shows the exact `crtk` command preview and executes it via `CommandRunner` |
| Banned | Card-in-card, full-page-as-card, decorative gradients/orbs, tutorial paragraphs in task screens, UI-only chess/notation logic |

A surface earns a new top-level tab only if its **primary object** is none of {position, engine/search state, command run, dataset, publication, session} ŌĆö otherwise it is a *mode* of an existing surface.

### 23.4 Where each new theme enters (the master map)

| Theme | CLI entrypoint (verbs) | GUI home (surface ┬Ę mode) | Layout | Mirror enforcement |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **A** PGN database | `crtk db import/find/show/stats/sources/dedupe/compact` | **Library** (new surface, ┬¦23.5) | A | `CommandTemplates` `db` leaves + `WorkbenchCommandRegression` |
| **B** import/sync | `crtk import folder/lichess/chesscom` (fetch-only) | **Library** ┬Ę *Import* action + Dashboard "Import games" quick-link | A | child-JVM spawn; token never enters the GUI |
| **C** reviewŌåÆstudy | `crtk review game <id>` | **Board** ┬Ę *Review* mode (verdict timeline) | A | panel reads `.review.jsonl`; never recomputes verdicts |
| **D** repertoire/SRS | `crtk repertoire import/review/grade/weight/export/stats` | **Board** ┬Ę *Repertoire/Drill* mode | A | grade buttons write a results JSONL fed back to `repertoire grade` |
| **E** serve daemon | `crtk serve --port ŌĆ”` | **Dashboard** ┬Ę *Daemon* status card (+ Run companion) | B | the surface controls a process; it *is* the CLI |
| **F** schema/catalog | `crtk help --json`, `crtk schema ŌĆ”`, `crtk record validate` | **Run** preview (catalog-driven) + **Datasets** ┬Ę *Validate* action | A/B | the command form is generated from the catalog |
| **G** explanation | `crtk position describe` / `crtk explain` | **Board** ┬Ę *Explain* mode (Facts/Prose) + *Relations* | A | two-pane inspector reads CLI output; verifier runs CLI-side |
| **H** productization | (the meta theme ŌĆö personas, first-run, deep-links) | cross-surface (`Dashboard` first-run + deep-links) | ŌĆö | personas are **data** over existing `ViewRegistry`, no new code paths |
| **I** dataset provenance | `crtk dataset verify/audit/diff`, `record split/dedupe` | **Datasets** (existing, extended) | B | controls preview = exact CLI; manifest read, not recomputed |
| **J** packaging/onboarding | `crtk setup`, `crtk doctor --json`, `crtk model ŌĆ”` | **Dashboard** ┬Ę *Setup/Health* card (+ Settings group) | B | health card consumes `doctor --json`; "fix" buttons deep-link |

### 23.5 The one IA decision: a 7th surface for the game corpus

A local PGN database (Theme A) is the keystone, and its **primary object ŌĆö a queryable game corpus ŌĆö is genuinely new**: it is not a single position (that is `Board`), not an ML artifact (`Datasets`), not session state (`Dashboard`). The design guide's six-surface model has no home for it, and forcing it into `Board` (which is built around *one* position/game) would violate the guide's own Primary Object Model.

**Recommendation: add a 7th top-level surface, `Library`** (Layout A): a query/filter toolbar leading, a dense results table in the body, a game-metadata + position-preview rail trailing; double-click routes the selected game to the shared `Board`. This is the VS Code "Explorer/Search" analogue for games. Adopting it required a matching update to [wiki/workbench-design-guide.md](wiki/workbench-design-guide.md), **applied in this pass** (the guide now documents `Library` as the seventh surface):

- Added a **`Library`** row to *Target Information Architecture* (primary object = "game corpus", center = results table, rail = game metadata).
- Added a **"Game corpus"** row to the *Primary Object Model* (header context = store path, game count, active filter; actions = Import, Find, Open in Board, Export).
- Added `Library` to the *Surface Home Rules* and *Surface And Mode Blueprints* tables, and routed `db`/`import`/`pgn` (plus the new `Review`/`Repertoire`/`Explain` Board modes) to their homes.

(The conservative alternative ŌĆö `Library` as a *mode of Board* ŌĆö keeps the six-surface count but overloads Board's "one position" identity; flagged and **not** recommended.) `Review`, `Repertoire`, and `Explain` do **not** need new surfaces ŌĆö they are Board modes alongside the existing `Analyze`/`Play`/`Solve`/`Relations`/`Draw`.

### 23.6 Surface blueprints (new/changed)

Following the design guide's *Surface And Mode Blueprints* format (header title ┬Ę context ┬Ę leading toolbar ┬Ę center/body ┬Ę side rail ┬Ę trailing actions). Each surface is opaque `SurfacePanel`, built from `Ui`/`Theme`, and mirrors a CLI verb.

| Surface / mode | Header title | Header context | Leading toolbar | Center / body | Side rail | Trailing actions |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Library** (new) | `Library` | Store path ┬Ę game count ┬Ę active filter | Source/collection selector | Results table (event, players, result, ECO, date) | Selected-game metadata + small board preview | Import, Find, Open in Board, Export |
| **Board ┬Ę Review** | `Review` | Game id ┬Ę ply ┬Ę current verdict | Move transport, review mode | Shared board + per-ply verdict timeline (cp/WDL loss, tag delta) | Mistake list, engine budget used, "Send to puzzle drill" | Run review, copy command, export study |
| **Board ┬Ę Explain** | `Analyze` (Explain mode) | FEN summary ┬Ę side to move ┬Ę audience | Audience + eval + strict-grounding controls | Shared board | Two panes: **Facts** (copyable rationale table) over **Prose** (verified text); non-blocking "showing deterministic text" banner when model output is rejected | Explain, copy, export |
| **Board ┬Ę Repertoire** | `Repertoire` | Deck ┬Ę due/new counts ┬Ę session budget | Deck selector, "Show answer" | Shared board (prompt position) | Card metadata, line context, four grade buttons | Start session, grade, export PGN |
| **Datasets** (extended) | `Datasets` | Loaded export ┬Ę rows ┬Ę shape | Dataset mode | KPI cards ŌåÆ label-distribution charts ŌåÆ dense sample/issue table | Load/options; manifest viewer (version, git, hashes, split counts) | Load, **Validate** (`record validate`), **Verify** (`dataset audit`), Export |
| **Dashboard ┬Ę Daemon** | `Dashboard` | (card) `127.0.0.1:PORT` ┬Ę running/idle ┬Ę requests served | ŌĆö | Status card in the summary grid | ŌĆö | Start, Stop, Copy base URL |
| **Dashboard ┬Ę Setup/Health** | `Dashboard` | (card) status ┬Ę Java ┬Ę engines ┬Ę nets | ŌĆö | Health card from `doctor --json` (per-check status + fix-suggestions) | ŌĆö | Run setup, Detect engines, Download net (verified), Open folder |

All seven respect the responsive rules (rails collapse below 1000 px), the state matrix (every panel defines empty/loading/error/missing), and the command-preview rule (the visible `crtk ŌĆ”` string equals what runs). None of them contain a second chess implementation; each is a window onto a CLI verb and the artifacts it wrote.
